PREFACE
   This code of the City of Kamiah, as supplemented, contains ordinances up to
and including ordinance 2020-06, passed 10-14-2020.  Ordinances of the City
adopted after said ordinance supersede the provisions of this code to the
extent that they are in conflict or inconsistent therewith. Consult the City
office in order to ascertain whether any particular provision of the code has
been amended, superseded or repealed.
Sterling Codifiers
Cincinnati, Ohio
ORDINANCES PENDING CODIFICATION
Ordinances listed have been passed, but have not been incorporated in the
actual code. Please contact the office of the clerk if there are any questions
concerning the ordinances listed.
TITLE 1
GENERAL PROVISIONS
CHAPTER 1.01
CODE ADOPTION 1
SECTION:
1.01.010: Adopted
1.01.020: Title; Citation; Reference
1.01.030: Codification Authority
1.01.040: Ordinances Passed Prior To Adoption Of The Code
1.01.050: Reference Applies To All Amendments
1.01.060: Title, Chapter And Section Headings
1.01.070: Reference To Specific Ordinances
1.01.080: Repeal Of Existing Ordinances
1.01.090: Effect Of Code On Past Actions And Obligations
1.01.100: Effective Date
1.01.110: Severability
 
Notes
1 1. IC § 50-903 et seq.
1.01.010: ADOPTED:
Pursuant to the provisions of sections 50-903 to 50-906 of the Idaho Code,
there is adopted the Kamiah municipal code as published by Book Publishing
Company, Seattle, Washington. (Ord. 7-79 §1, 1979)
1.01.020: TITLE; CITATION; REFERENCE:
This code shall be known as the KAMIAH MUNICIPAL CODE and it shall be
sufficient to refer to the code as the Kamiah municipal code in any prosecution
for the violation of any provision thereof or in any proceeding at law or
equity. It shall be sufficient to designate any ordinance adding to, amending,
correcting or repealing all or any part or portion thereof as an addition to,
amendment to, correction or repeal of the Kamiah municipal code. Further
reference may be had to the titles, chapters, sections and subsections of the
Kamiah municipal code and such reference shall apply to that numbered title,
chapter, section or subsection as it appears in the code. (Ord. 7-79 §2, 1979)
1.01.030: CODIFICATION AUTHORITY:
This code consists of all the regulatory and penal ordinances and certain of
the administrative ordinances of the city of Kamiah, Idaho, codified pursuant
to the provisions of sections 50-903 through 50-906 of the Idaho Code. (Ord. 7-
79 §3, 1979)
1.01.040: ORDINANCES PASSED PRIOR TO ADOPTION OF THE CODE:
The last ordinance included in this code was ordinance 18-78, passed June 20,
1978. The following ordinances, passed subsequent to ordinance 18-78, but prior
to adoption of this code are adopted and made a part of this code: ordinances
19-78, 1-79, 2-79, 3-79 and 4-79. (Ord. 7-79 §4, 1979)
1.01.050: REFERENCE APPLIES TO ALL AMENDMENTS:
Whenever a reference is made to this code as the Kamiah municipal code or to
any portion thereof, or to any ordinances of the city of Kamiah, Idaho, the
reference shall apply to all amendments, corrections and additions heretofore,
now or hereafter made. (Ord. 7-79 §5, 1979)
1.01.060: TITLE, CHAPTER AND SECTION HEADINGS:
Title, chapter and section headings contained in this code shall not be deemed
to govern, limit, modify or in any manner affect the scope, meaning or intent
of the provisions of any title, chapter or section hereof. (Ord. 7-79 §6, 1979)
1.01.070: REFERENCE TO SPECIFIC ORDINANCES:
The provisions of this code shall not in any manner affect matters of record
which refer to, or are otherwise connected with ordinances which are therein
specifically designated by number or otherwise and which are included within
the code, but such reference shall be construed to apply to the corresponding
provisions contained within this code. (Ord. 7-79 §7, 1979)
1.01.080: REPEAL OF EXISTING ORDINANCES:
So far as the provisions of this code are the same in effect as those of
previously existing ordinances, they shall be construed as continuations
thereof, but is subject to the above limitation and the provisions of the next
section of this chapter; all ordinances and resolutions of the city of Kamiah,
Idaho, heretofore in force (except such as are of a private, local or temporary
nature, including franchises, grants, dedications and special levies for local
assessments), are hereby repealed. (Ord. 7-79 §8, 1980)
1.01.090: EFFECT OF CODE ON PAST ACTIONS AND OBLIGATIONS:
Neither the adoption of this code nor the repeal or amendment of any ordinance
or part or portion of any ordinance of the city shall in any manner affect the
prosecution for violations of ordinances, which violations were committed prior
to the effective date of this code, nor be construed as a waiver of any
license, fee, or penalty at the effective date due and unpaid under such
ordinances, nor be construed as affecting any of the provisions of such
ordinances, relating to the collection of any such license, fee, or penalty, or
the penal provisions applicable to any violation thereof, nor to affect the
validity of any bond or cash deposit, in lieu required to be posted, filed or
deposited pursuant to any ordinance and all rights and obligations thereunder
appertaining shall continue in full force and effect. (Ord. 7-79 §9, 1979)
1.01.100: EFFECTIVE DATE:
This code shall become effective on the date the ordinance adopting this code
as the "Kamiah municipal code" becomes effective. (Ord. 7-79 §10, 1979)
1.01.110: SEVERABILITY:
If any section, subsection, sentence, clause or phrase of this code is for any
reason held to be invalid or unconstitutional, such decision shall not affect
the validity of the remaining portions of this code. The council declared, that
it would have passed this code, and each section, subsection, sentence, clause
and phrase thereof, irrespective of the fact that any one or more sections,
subsections, sentences, clauses or phrases had been declared invalid or
unconstitutional, and if for any reason this code should be declared invalid or
unconstitutional, then the original ordinance or ordinances shall be in full
force and effect. (Ord. 7-79 §11, 1979)
CHAPTER 1.04
ADMINISTRATION OF CODE
SECTION:
1.04.010: Rules For Construction Of Ordinances And Amendments
1.04.020: Intent To Defraud
1.04.030: Liability Of Employers And Agents
1.04.040: Definitions
1.04.050: Grammatical Interpretation
1.04.060: Title Of Sections And Subsections
1.04.070: Constitutionality; Effect
1.04.010: RULES FOR CONSTRUCTION OF ORDINANCES AND AMENDMENTS:
In the construction of the revised ordinances and all ordinances amendatory
thereof or supplementary thereto, the rules set forth in this chapter shall be
observed unless such construction would be inconsistent with the manifest
intent of the legislative body or repugnant to the context of the ordinance.
(Prior code §1-103)
1.04.020: INTENT TO DEFRAUD:
Whenever, by any of the provisions of this code, an intent to defraud is
required in order to constitute an offense, it is sufficient if an intent
appears to defraud any person, association or body politic or any combination
of persons. (Prior code §1-103(a))
1.04.030: LIABILITY OF EMPLOYERS AND AGENTS:
When the provisions of an ordinance prohibit the commission or omission of an
act, not only the person actually doing the prohibited thing or omitting the
directed act, but also the employer and all other persons concerned or aiding
or abetting the person shall be guilty of the offense described and liable to
the penalty set forth in this code. (Prior code §1-103(b))
1.04.040: DEFINITIONS:
DAY: Any twenty four (24) hour period from twelve o'clock (12:00) midnight to
twelve o'clock (12:00) midnight.
GOVERNING BODY: The mayor and council or the board of trustees.
KNOWINGLY: Imports only a knowledge that the facts exist which bring the act or
omission within the provisions of this code. It does not require any knowledge
of the unlawfulness of such act or omission.
LAND, REAL ESTATE AND REAL PROPERTY: Includes lands, tenements, hereditaments,
water rights, possessory rights and claims.
MONTH: A calendar month unless otherwise expressed.
NEGLECT, NEGLIGENCE, AND NEGLIGENT AND NEGLIGENTLY: Imports a want of such
attention to the nature or probable consequences of the act or omission as a
prudent man ordinarily bestows in acting in his own concern.
OATH; SWEAR: "Oath" includes "affirmation", and "swear" includes the word
"affirm". Every mode of oral statement under oath or affirmation is embraced in
the term "testify" and every written one in the term "depose".
OFFICER: Includes officers and boards in charge of departments and the members
of such boards, and such references as use "municipality" mean this city.
"Clerk" or "treasurer" and others mean the city clerk or city treasurer as the
case may be applicable.
OWNER: Applied to a building or land includes any part owner, joint owner,
tenant in common, joint tenant or lessee of the whole or of a part of such
building or land.
PERSON: Includes bodies politic and corporate, partnerships, associations and
corporations.
PERSONAL PROPERTY: Includes every description of money, goods, chattels,
effects, evidence of rights in action, and all written instruments by which any
pecuniary obligation, right or title to property is created, acknowledged,
transferred, increased, defeated, discharged or diminished, and every right or
interest therein.
PROPERTY: Includes both real and personal property.
QUARTER: Any three (3) month period, ending with the last day of March, June,
September and December.
SIGNATURE: Includes any name, mark or sign written with the intent to
authenticate any instrument of writing.
STREETS: Includes alleys, lanes, courts, boulevards, public ways, public
squares, public places and sidewalks.
TENANT OR OCCUPANT: Applied to a building or land includes any person who
occupies the whole or any part of such building or land whether alone or with
others.
TIME: When any time is specified in these ordinances, it means standard time,
as distinguished from solar time, and "midnight" or "noon" shall be taken to be
midnight or noon standard time.
WILFULLY: When applied to the intent with which an act is done or omitted,
implies simply a purpose or willingness to commit the act or make the omission
referred to. It does not require any intent to violate law, or to injure
another, or to acquire an advantage.
WRITING: Includes printing, writing and typewriting.
YEAR: Any one calendar year.
Words prohibiting anything being done, except in accordance with a license or
permit or authority from a board or officers, shall be construed as giving such
board or officer power to license or permit or authorize such thing to be done.
(Prior code §1-103(e))
1.04.050: GRAMMATICAL INTERPRETATION:
   A.   The singular number includes the plural.
   B.   Words used in the present tense include the future.
   C.   Words used in the masculine gender comprehend as well the feminine and
neuter. (Prior code §1-103(e))
1.04.060: TITLE OF SECTIONS AND SUBSECTIONS:
The title of any section or subsection of the ordinances codified in this code
shall be deemed in no wise to restrict or qualify or to limit the effect of the
provisions set forth and contained in such section or subsection. (Prior code
§1-103(c))
1.04.070: CONSTITUTIONALITY; EFFECT:
Should any section, subsection or portion of the ordinances codified in this
code, or of any ordinance which may be hereafter passed, approved and published
as required by law, be declared by any court of competent jurisdiction to be
unconstitutional or void, such adjudication shall in no way affect the
remaining portion of such section, subsection, part or portion of the
ordinances codified in this code or of any such ordinance hereafter passed.
(Prior code §1-103(d))

SECTION:
1.12.010: Designated
 
Notes
1 1. IC §§ 50-213, 60-106.
1.12.010: DESIGNATED:
The Clearwater Progress, Ind., a weekly newspaper, printed and published in the

CHAPTER 1.14
ELECTIONS
SECTION:
1.14.010: Supervision Of Election Laws By County Clerk
1.14.020: County Clerk Shall Be Registrar
1.14.030: Election Expenses
1.14.040: Declaration Of Candidacy; City Clerk Duties
1.14.010: SUPERVISION OF ELECTION LAWS BY COUNTY CLERK:
The county clerk of Lewis County, Idaho, is the chief elections officer and
shall exercise general supervision of the administration of the election laws
in the city of Kamiah. (Ord. 2012-4, 2012)
1.14.020: COUNTY CLERK SHALL BE REGISTRAR:
The county clerk of Lewis County, Idaho, shall be the registrar for all city
elections and shall conduct voter registration for each city pursuant to the
provisions of the laws of the state of Idaho. (Ord. 2012-4, 2012)
1.14.030: ELECTION EXPENSES:
After an election has been ordered, all expenses associated with conducting
municipal general and special elections shall be paid from the county election
fund as provided by the laws of the state of Idaho. Expenses associated with
conducting runoff elections shall be paid by the city adopting runoff elections
pursuant to the provisions of Idaho Code. (Ord. 2012-4, 2012)
1.14.040: DECLARATION OF CANDIDACY; CITY CLERK DUTIES:
Candidates for elective city offices shall be nominated by declaration. The
declaration shall contain the name and address of the person and the office and
the term for which he is being nominated. There shall be no mention relating to
party or principal of the nominee. The completed declaration of candidacy shall
be accompanied by: a) a petition of candidacy signed by not less than five (5)
registered qualified electors; or b) a nonrefundable filing fee of forty
dollars ($40.00) which shall be deposited in the city treasury. It shall be the
duty of the city clerk to furnish upon application a reasonable number of
regular printed forms, as herein set forth, to any person or persons applying
therefor. The forms shall be of uniform size as determined by the clerk and
conform to Idaho Code. (Ord. 2012-4, 2012)
CHAPTER 1.16
PRECINCTS
SECTION:
1.16.010: Polling Place
1.16.010: POLLING PLACE:
The municipality of Kamiah, Lewis County, Idaho, consists of only one precinct
for the entire incorporated limits. The clerk of Lewis County, Idaho, shall
designate the polling place within that one precinct. (Ord. 2012-2, 2012)
CHAPTER 1.18
INITIATIVE AND REFERENDUM
SECTION:
1.18.010: Rights Established
1.18.020: Number Of Signatures Required
1.18.030: Petitions
1.18.040: Special Election
1.18.050: State Standards
1.18.010: RIGHTS ESTABLISHED:
The people of this city shall have the right to enact ordinances through the
initiative process, and to repeal ordinances through the referendum process,
according to the procedures set forth in this chapter. (Ord. 2012-3, 2012)
1.18.020: NUMBER OF SIGNATURES REQUIRED:
To enact an ordinance by initiative or to repeal an ordinance by referendum,
there shall be attached or appended to the petition the signatures of the legal
voters of the city equal to at least twenty percent (20%) of the total number
of voters registered to vote at the last general election of the city. (Ord.
2012-3, 2012)
1.18.030: PETITIONS:
Referendum petitions with the requisite number of signatures attached shall be
filed with the city clerk not less than sixty (60) days following the final
adoption of the ordinance to be subject to referendum. (Ord. 2012-3, 2012)
1.18.040: SPECIAL ELECTION:
There shall be no more than two (2) elections conducted in any calendar year,
except as provided in this section.
   A.   The dates on which elections may be conducted are:
      1.   The third Tuesday in May of each year; and
      2.   The Tuesday following the first Monday in November of each year.
      3.   In addition to the elections specified in subsections A1 and A2 of
this section, an emergency election may be called upon motion of the city
council. Initiative, referendum, bond, levy and any other ballot question
elections shall be held on the nearest date authorized in this subsection A
which falls more than forty five (45) days after the city clerk orders that
such election shall be held. (Ord. 2012-3, 2012)
1.18.050: STATE STANDARDS:
Referendum and initiative petitions shall conform with the requirements for
signature, verification of valid petitions, printing of petitions, and time
limits, except as expressly modified to meet the purposes of initiative and
referendum to be as nearly as practicable as provided in sections 34-1701
through 34-1705 of the Idaho Code. (Ord. 4-79 §5, 1979)
CHAPTER 1.20
GENERAL PENALTY 1
SECTION:
1.20.010: Designated
1.20.020: Separate Offense
 
Notes
1 1. IC § 50-302.
1.20.010: DESIGNATED:
Any person violating any of the provisions or failing to comply with any of the
mandatory requirements of any ordinance of the city is guilty of a misdemeanor.
Except in cases where a different punishment is prescribed by any ordinance of
the city or of any adopted code, any person convicted of a misdemeanor under
the ordinances thereof or hereof shall be punished by a fine of not to exceed
three hundred dollars ($300.00) or by imprisonment in the Lewis County jail for
a period of not to exceed six (6) months, or by both such fine and
imprisonment. (Ord. 9-78 §1, 1978)
1.20.020: SEPARATE OFFENSE:
Each person is guilty of a separate offense for each and every day during any
portion of which any violation under any provision of the ordinances of Kamiah
is committed, continued or permitted by such person, and he is punishable in
accordance therewith. (Ord. 9-78 §2, 1978)
TITLE 2
ADMINISTRATION AND PERSONNEL
CHAPTER 2.04
MAYOR 1
SECTION:
2.04.010: Duties Generally
2.04.020: Authorized To Sign Contracts
2.04.030: Power To Offer Reward
2.04.040: Veto Power
2.04.050: Power To Require Accounts And Reports Of Officers
2.04.060: Police Power
2.04.070: Authority To Require Aid In Law Enforcement
2.04.080: Additional Powers
 
Notes
1 1. IC ch. 50-6.
2.04.010: DUTIES GENERALLY:
The mayor, the superintending and administrative officer of the municipality,
shall devote so much of his time to the duties of his office as an efficient
and faithful discharge thereof may require. He shall preside at all meetings of
the council and shall have a vote when the council is equally divided, and call
special meetings of the council when necessary. He shall appoint all officers
and employees of the municipality, subject to the approval of the council, and
have such other powers as the council may prescribe. He shall from time to time
provide for the council such information and recommend such measures as he may
deem beneficial to the municipality, he shall examine the grounds of all
complaints against any of the officers of the municipality to determine the
existence of a violation or neglect of duty and report the evidence thereof, if
deemed sufficient for the removal of such officer, to the council. He shall
require that every officer, on the expiration of his term of office or
resignation or removal from the same, deliver to his successor all monies,
books, papers, maps, furniture, fixtures, apparatus, machinery, tools and
instruments and appurtenances belonging to such office. He shall perform all
other duties required and necessary for the efficient operation of the business
of the municipality. (Prior code §1-100)
2.04.020: AUTHORIZED TO SIGN CONTRACTS:
The mayor is authorized and empowered to sign his name officially for and in
behalf of the municipality on all contracts, including deeds, bonds, bills,
notes, obligations and other agreements, documents and papers, to which the
municipality is a party, and to require that the conditions in the instrument
are faithfully performed and to borrow money on the credit of the municipality
when so authorized by the council. (Prior code §1-1002)
2.04.030: POWER TO OFFER REWARD:
The mayor, whenever he deems it expedient, is empowered to offer a reward not
exceeding one hundred dollars ($100.00) for the arrest and conviction of any
person charged with violating the law. (Prior code §1-1003)
2.04.040: VETO POWER:
The mayor shall have power to veto or sign any ordinance passed by the council;
provided, that any ordinance vetoed by the mayor may be passed over his veto by
a vote of two-thirds (2/3) members of the council elected notwithstanding his
veto, and should the mayor neglect or refuse to sign any ordinance and return
the same with his objection, in writing, at the next regular meeting of the
council, the same shall become law without his signature. (Prior code §1-1005)
2.04.050: POWER TO REQUIRE ACCOUNTS AND REPORTS OF OFFICERS:
The mayor shall have the power, when he deems it necessary, to require any
officer of the municipality to exhibit his accounts or other papers, and to
make reports to the council in writing touching any subject or matter he may
require pertaining to his office. (Prior code §1-1006)
2.04.060: POLICE POWER:
The mayor shall have jurisdiction over all places within five (5) miles of the
corporate limits of the municipality for the enforcement of any health or
quarantine ordinance and regulation thereof, and shall have jurisdiction in all
matters, excepting taxation, within one-half (1/2) mile of the corporate limits
of the municipality. (Prior code §1-1007)
2.04.070: AUTHORITY TO REQUIRE AID IN LAW ENFORCEMENT:
The mayor is authorized to call on every male inhabitant of the municipality
over eighteen (18) years of age and under the age of fifty (50) years to aid in
enforcing the law. (Prior code §1-1008)
2.04.080: ADDITIONAL POWERS:
The mayor shall have all other powers provided by law or provided by ordinance
or resolution of the council. (Prior code §1-1009)
CHAPTER 2.08
COUNCIL 1
SECTION:
2.08.010: Duties
2.08.020: Ward Representation
2.08.030: Vacancy; Filling
2.08.040: Meetings; Time And Place
2.08.050: Meetings; How Conducted
2.08.060: President Of Council
2.08.070: Authority To Secure Bonding
 
Notes
1 1. IC ch. 50-7.
2.08.010: DUTIES:
The members of the council, the legislative and policy making branch of the
government of the municipality, shall devote so much of their time to the
duties of their office as an efficient and faithful discharge thereof may
require. They shall attend all meetings of the council unless lawfully excused
therefrom by the mayor or by a majority of the remaining members, and perform
all duties which by the nature of their office they should reasonably perform,
such as the passing of ordinances, resolutions, and the investigation and study
of work done for the municipality according to the character of the committee
upon which they may severally be appointed by the mayor. (Prior code §1-1101)
2.08.020: WARD REPRESENTATION:
There shall be two (2) councilmen to represent each ward of the municipality.
At each municipal election hereafter, one councilman shall be elected from each
municipal ward, for a term of four (4) years or until his successor is elected
and qualified. (Prior code §1-1102)
2.08.030: VACANCY; FILLING:
In the event an office or councilman becomes vacant, through death, moving out
of the ward, or for any other cause, the mayor shall appoint, with the approval
of the council, a resident of the ward to fill the unexpired portion of the
term to serve until the next general election at which time the unexpired term
shall be filled by regular election. (Prior code §1-1103)
2.08.040: MEETINGS; TIME AND PLACE:
The council shall hold regular sessions in city hall on the second and fourth
Wednesday of each month at six o'clock (6:00) P.M. (Ord. 2005-1 §1, 2005: Ord.
93-3 §1, 1993: Ord. 86-5 §1, 1986: Ord. 3-1973, 1973: prior code §1-1104)
2.08.050: MEETINGS; HOW CONDUCTED:
There is adopted by the municipality, for the purpose of establishing rules and
regulations for the conduct of council meetings, the clerk's duties and the
mayor's duties in relation to council meetings, that book entitled "How To
Conduct A Municipal Meeting" prepared by the Idaho municipal league, now on
file in the office of the clerk and the same is adopted and incorporated as
fully as if set out at length in this section. (Prior code §1-1105)
2.08.060: PRESIDENT OF COUNCIL:
At the time of taking office, the council shall elect one of its members
president of the council, who shall preside at all meetings of the council and
perform all other duties of the mayor in the absence of the mayor; and, in the
absence of the president, the council shall elect one of their members to
occupy his place temporarily who shall be styled acting president of the
council, and the president and acting president, when occupying the place of
mayor shall have the same privileges as other members of the council, and all
acts of the president and acting president, while so acting, shall be binding
upon the council and upon the municipality as if done by the mayor. (Prior code
§1-1106)
2.08.070: AUTHORITY TO SECURE BONDING:
   A.   Upon the requirement of any other governmental agency for security
bonding by the city clerk or other such city official that might hereafter be
responsible for the handling of funds provided in whole or part by such agency
other than the city of Kamiah, the city council is authorized by appropriate
motion or resolution to secure such bonding as from time to time may be
required.
   B.   The cost of any particular bond premium as authorized under this
section may be added to the cost of any particular public works project or paid
from the general fund revenues. (Ord. 11-77 §1, 1977)
CHAPTER 2.10
CITY ADMINISTRATOR
SECTION:
2.10.010: Establishment, Appointment And Removal Of The Position Of City
Administrator
2.10.020: Duties, Powers And Responsibilities
2.10.030: Compensation
2.10.040: Combination Of Positions
2.10.010: ESTABLISHMENT, APPOINTMENT AND REMOVAL OF THE POSITION OF CITY
ADMINISTRATOR:
Pursuant to Idaho Code 50-204 the mayor for the city of Kamiah has the
authority to appoint a city clerk, a city treasurer, a city attorney and such
other officers as may be deemed necessary for the efficient operation of the
city. It is hereby established along with the city clerk, city treasurer and
city attorney that the office of city administrator be created, which shall be
filled by appointment of the mayor, subject to the confirmation by the majority
of the city council. The city administrator shall be subject to removal by the
mayor with consent of one-half (1/2) plus one of the full city council or by
unanimous vote of the council. The city administrator shall be the executive
and liaison officer for the city, under direction and authority of the mayor.
(Ord. 2014-1, 2014)
2.10.020: DUTIES, POWERS AND RESPONSIBILITIES:
The city administrator shall have the following specific duties, powers and
responsibilities. He/she shall:
   A.   Under the authority of the office of the mayor, supervise, administer
and coordinate the activities and functions of the various city departments and
offices in carrying out the requirements of city ordinances and the policies of
the city council.
   B.   Regularly report to the mayor and council concerning the status of all
assignments, duties, projects and functions of the various city departments and
offices.
   C.   Be the personnel officer and recommend to the mayor and council
concerning personnel appointments, removals and discipline in accordance with
the city's personnel policy.
   D.   Prepare and submit to the mayor and council the preliminary budget for
each fiscal year. Upon adoption of the annual budget by the city council, the
city administrator shall supervise all purchases and expenditures by the
various city offices, departments, commissions and boards, for the purpose of
keeping the same within the limitations of the annual budget of the city.
   E.   Serve as public information officer of the city government and
investigate all complaints concerning city facilities.
   F.   Attend all meetings of the city council and report any matters
concerning city affairs under his/her supervision.
   G.   Assist generally in conducting the city's business in all matters, and
perform such other duties and assume such other responsibilities as the council
through the mayor may direct or as by ordinances and resolutions of the city
council may require. (Ord. 2014-1, 2014)
2.10.030: COMPENSATION:
This shall be an unclassified position and the salary and benefits of the city
administrator shall be set by the city council upon recommendation by the
mayor. (Ord. 2014-1, 2014)
2.10.040: COMBINATION OF POSITIONS:
The office of city administrator may be combined with any other appointive
position in the city. (Ord. 2014-1, 2014)
CHAPTER 2.12
CITY CLERK 1
SECTION:
2.12.010: Appointment
2.12.020: Duties Generally
2.12.030: Council Meetings; Duties
2.12.040: Financial Transactions; Annual Report
2.12.050: Copies Of Municipal Records
2.12.060: Books And Records To Be Kept
2.12.070: License Issuance
2.12.080: Record Of Municipal Bonds
2.12.090: Deposit Of Funds To Treasurer
 
Notes
1 1. IC § 50-207.
2.12.010: APPOINTMENT:
The mayor shall, with approval of the council, appoint a clerk who shall hold
office for the duration of his appointment or until such time as he shall be
removed by the mayor and council. (Prior code §1-1301)
2.12.020: DUTIES GENERALLY:
   A.   The clerk shall be custodian of the seal and affix same to documents as
provided.
   B.   The clerk shall also be custodian of all public records, documents,
ordinances, resolutions and orders of the council, and such other papers and
documents as may be delivered into his custody. (Prior code §1-1302(a))
2.12.030: COUNCIL MEETINGS; DUTIES:
The clerk shall attend all sessions of the council, keep a correct journal and
shall keep in a separate book a record of ordinances passed by the council and
of the titles of such ordinances; and all ordinances not published in book form
shall be carefully indexed alphabetically. The clerk shall see that each
ordinance is published as required by law, and he shall keep on file the proof
of such publication. (Prior code §1-1302(b))
2.12.040: FINANCIAL TRANSACTIONS; ANNUAL REPORT:
The clerk shall prepare and present to the council at its regular meeting each
month a full and complete statement of the financial transaction of his office
during the month preceding, which statements shall set forth all receipts for
licenses issued; money received with applications for licenses which are to
come before the council; all other funds received by him as clerk, and the
report shall give a detailed explanation of disbursements redeemed including a
statement of the aggregate of warrants of each fund issued, of warrants
redeemed during the month and warrants outstanding against each fund at the
close of such month. He shall also at the close of each fiscal year present to
the council an annual report covering the operations of the entire year, which
report shall contain a description of the bonds issued and sold during the
year, and the term of sale; and shall itemize each and every expense thereof.
The clerk shall also make such additional report and furnish such other data
from the records and files of his office as may be requested by the mayor or
council or be required by law. (Prior code §1-1302(c))
2.12.050: COPIES OF MUNICIPAL RECORDS:
It shall be the duty of the clerk to furnish any municipal officer with a
certified copy of any record, paper or public document on file in his office or
in his custody, for the use of such officer in the discharge of his official
duties, and he shall also furnish a certified copy of any such record, paper or
document to any person not an officer of the municipality upon the payment in
advance of fifteen cents ($0.15) per folio. (Prior code §1-1302(d))
2.12.060: BOOKS AND RECORDS TO BE KEPT:
The clerk shall keep such books and permanent records of the transaction and
business of his office as may be necessary to disclose accurately all
transactions and business of his office. He shall also countersign all
warrants, and keep a "warrant register and abstract of expenditures", showing
the number and amount of warrants issued and the person to whom issued, the
date redeemed, the interest paid, and the several funds against which each of
such warrants is drawn. (Prior code §1-1302(e))
2.12.070: LICENSE ISSUANCE:
The clerk shall issue all licenses, a duplicate of which shall be kept on file,
but no license shall be issued to any person unless fees and charges fixed by
law shall have first been paid, for which payment the clerk shall issue a
receipt in duplicate. The clerk shall endorse upon the receipt and duplicate
receipt the number of the license issued, the number of the application for
license, and the duplicate of such receipt so issued shall be kept on file with
the duplicate license. (Prior code §1-1302(f))
2.12.080: RECORD OF MUNICIPAL BONDS:
The clerk shall keep records of outstanding bonds of the municipality, showing
the number and amount of each, for what and to whom the bonds were issued, and
when any of the bonds are purchased or paid or canceled, the record shall show
the fact; and in his report at the close of each fiscal year, he shall describe
particularly the bonds issued and sold during the year, the terms of sale, and
itemize each and every expense thereof. (Prior code §1-1302(g))
2.12.090: DEPOSIT OF FUNDS TO TREASURER:
Within ten (10) days after the filing of his monthly report as provided in
section
2.12.040 of this chapter, the clerk shall deposit with the treasurer all funds
collected by him during the preceding month, less refunds which have been
authorized by the council. (Prior code §1-1302(h))
CHAPTER 2.16
CITY TREASURER 1
SECTION:
2.16.010: Appointment
2.16.020: Duties Generally
2.16.030: Books And Records
2.16.040: Vouchers And Warrants
2.16.050: Receipt For Money Or Funds
2.16.060: Books And Papers To Successors
2.16.070: Statement Of Receipts And Expenditures
2.16.080: Collection Of Monies
2.16.090: Monthly Report
 
Notes
1 1. IC § 15-208.
2.16.010: APPOINTMENT:
The mayor shall appoint, with approval of the governing body, a treasurer who
shall hold office for the duration of his appointment or until such time as he
shall be removed by the governing body. (Prior code §1-1701)
2.16.020: DUTIES GENERALLY:
It shall be the duty of the treasurer to receive and safely keep in designated
depositories, as required by law, all monies or funds belonging to the
municipality which may come into his hands; to disburse the same upon an
appropriation by ordinance or resolution of the governing body after audit and
allowance by the governing body of claims therefor, and upon warrant of the
mayor, countersigned by the clerk, and not otherwise. Securities belonging to
the municipality, incapable of deposit in a checking account, shall be kept by
the treasurer in a safety deposit box in some banking institution designated by
the governing body. All bonds or securities delivered to the treasurer by any
designated depository of municipal funds as security for such funds shall be
deposited with the county auditor or other public official as may be provided
by law. (Prior code §1-1702(a))
2.16.030: BOOKS AND RECORDS:
The treasurer shall keep in a suitable book or books a full and accurate
account of municipal money and funds received by him, showing the date of
receipt thereof, the person from whom received, on what account, and to what
fund the same is credited with the date of disbursement, the person to whom
disbursed, on what account and against what fund. (Prior code §1-1702(b))
2.16.040: VOUCHERS AND WARRANTS:
All warrants or orders paid and redeemed and all vouchers shall be delivered to
the clerk immediately upon payment or redemption, and such redeemed warrants
shall have written or stamped on the face thereof the word "Paid". (Prior code
§1-1702(c))
2.16.050: RECEIPT FOR MONEY OR FUNDS:
The treasurer shall execute and deliver to every officer or other person paying
money or funds, including water rentals, into the treasury a receipt therefor,
specifying the date of payment, the amount thereof and upon what fund or
account the same is received. (Prior code §1-1702(d))
2.16.060: BOOKS AND PAPERS TO SUCCESSORS:
The treasurer shall deliver to his successor in office all books, money, papers
and other property pertaining to his office. (Prior code §1-1702(e))
2.16.070: STATEMENT OF RECEIPTS AND EXPENDITURES:
It shall be the duty of the treasurer to cause to be published for at least one
insertion in some newspaper in the municipality, between the first and third
Mondays of May, August, November and February of each and every year a full
statement of the receipts and expenditures of the municipality, giving the
source from whence received, to what purpose applied and to whom paid. (Prior
code §1-1702(f))
2.16.080: COLLECTION OF MONIES:
The treasurer shall receive and all officers or other persons shall forthwith
pay to the treasurer, except as otherwise provided by this code, all money due
the municipality on any account whatsoever. (Prior code §1-1702(g))
2.16.090: MONTHLY REPORT:
The treasurer shall at the end of each and every month, and at other times when
required by the governing body, render an account, including in and showing,
under oath, the condition of the treasury at the date of such account,
including in the statement the balance of money in the treasury with a detailed
statement of the specified amount in each designated depository and of the
amount and class of security held to guarantee each deposit.
Such account shall also contain a statement of receipts and disbursements and
of all warrants redeemed and paid by him, which warrants, with all vouchers
held by him, shall be filed with his accounts in the clerk's office. The
governing body shall have free access to any and all books or papers in the
office of the treasurer for the purpose of inspection or examination. (Prior
code §1-1702(h))
CHAPTER 2.20
CITY ATTORNEY
SECTION:
2.20.010: Appointment
2.20.020: Duties
2.20.010: APPOINTMENT:
The mayor shall appoint, with approval of the governing body, a city attorney
who shall hold office for the duration of his appointment or until such time as
he shall be removed by the governing body. (Prior code §1-1401)
2.20.020: DUTIES:
It shall be the duty of the attorney to prosecute and defend in all courts all
actions on behalf of the municipality on account of official acts; to take
appeals or sue out writs of error on behalf of the municipality or any office
aforesaid, with the consent and approval of the mayor, and make the necessary
bonds in the name of the municipality; to advise the governing body or its
committees or any officer on such legal questions as may arise in relation to
the business of the municipality, and to attend the meetings of the governing
body. Having personal knowledge of the violation of this code, or upon
receiving the reliable information of any such violation, he shall institute
proceedings to bring the offender to the proper court. (Prior code §1-1402)
CHAPTER 2.24
CITY SUPERVISOR
SECTION:
2.24.010: Duties; Responsibilities
2.24.010: DUTIES; RESPONSIBILITIES:
The city supervisor is directly responsible to the mayor and city council and
has the following duties and responsibilities:
   A.   Be, and perform the duties of city clerk as required in section 50-207,
Idaho Code;
   B.   Be, and perform the duties of city treasurer as required in section 50-
208, Idaho Code;
   C.   Be, and perform the duties of city personnel officer;
   D.   Be, and perform the duties of city purchasing agent;
   E.   Assist the mayor and council in the administration of the entire city
operation;
   F.   Prepare and submit to the mayor and council a tentative budget for the
following fiscal year in accordance with section 50-1002, Idaho Code;
   G.   Prepare and submit to the council such reports as might be required by
that body or as he may deem necessary; recommend to the council for adoption
such measures as he may deem necessary and expedient;
   H.   Perform such other duties as the mayor and council may direct;
   I.   Possess such powers of authority as may be delegated by the mayor and/
or council. (Ord. 5-77 §2, 1977)
CHAPTER 2.28
CITY MARSHAL 1
SECTION:
2.28.010: Appointment
2.28.020: Duties Generally
2.28.030: Ratification Of Previous Acts
 
Notes
1 1. IC § 50-209.
2.28.010: APPOINTMENT:
The mayor shall appoint with the approval of the city council, a city marshal
who shall hold office during the duration of his appointment or until such time
as he shall be removed by the mayor and the city council.
Initial appointment of a city marshal shall be subject to such probationary
terms and conditions and for such term as the city council shall from time to
time prescribe.
The mayor shall, in addition to the city marshal, appoint such deputy marshals
as the city council shall from time to time deem necessary. Appointments of
deputies shall likewise be subject to such initial probationary requirements as
the city council shall fix. (Ord. 86-2 §2, 1986)
2.28.020: DUTIES GENERALLY:
The city marshal, in addition to the power and authority vested by Idaho Code
section 50-209 as amended, shall have such additional duties as the mayor and
city council shall from time to time direct. The marshal shall generally
preserve the peace and good order of the municipality and carry out such other
duties as are assigned to him by the mayor with the consent of the city
council. Specific direction to the marshal and his deputies of assigned tasks
and duties shall be passed upon by the city council, and be reflected in
writing in the minutes of city council meetings held by the city clerk.
Where, throughout other sections of this code, references are made to specific
duties of the chief of police, those duties shall now be assumed by the city
marshal and his deputies unless the city council shall specifically, by
appropriate motion, vote to limit such authority to such officers. (Ord. 86-
2 §2, 1986)
2.28.030: RATIFICATION OF PREVIOUS ACTS:
As of the date of the passage of the ordinance codified herein, all previous
lawful acts of the law enforcement officers of the city, since their
appointment by the mayor and city council, whether they be designated marshals,
deputy marshals or chiefs of police. (Ord. 86-2 §2, 1986)
CHAPTER 2.32
POUNDMASTER
SECTION:
2.32.010: Appointment
2.32.020: Compensation
2.32.030: Duty
2.32.010: APPOINTMENT:
The mayor, with approval of the council, may appoint a poundmaster who shall
hold office during the term of, and under the conditions prescribed by and for
appointive officers. (Prior code §1-2201)
2.32.020: COMPENSATION:
The compensation of the poundmaster shall be paid either by the redeemer or
highest bidder at public auction, which fee shall be one dollar ($1.00) per
animal redeemed or sold. (Prior code §1-2202)
2.32.030: DUTY:
It shall be the duty of the poundmaster to impound all animals found running at
large, post notices, hold public auctions, except in the case of disposal of
dogs, and collect the fees for feeding such animals that are impounded, which
fees shall be turned over to the clerk. (Prior code §1-2203)
CHAPTER 2.36
APPOINTIVE OFFICERS 1
SECTION:
2.36.010: Appointment By Mayor
2.36.020: Term Of Office; Removal
2.36.030: Bond
 
Notes
1 1. IC §§ 50-204 - 50-206.
2.36.010: APPOINTMENT BY MAYOR:
The mayor, with the consent of the governing body, shall appoint a clerk,
attorney, engineer, chief of police, chief of fire department and assistants,
treasurer and other such officers as may be deemed advisable for the efficient
operation of the municipality. (Prior code §1-1201)
2.36.020: TERM OF OFFICE; REMOVAL:
All appointive officers shall hold office for the term for which they were
appointed and qualified; provided, that any appointive officer may at any time
be removed by action of the mayor with concurrence of a majority of the
governing body; provided, further, that all employees holding positions by
virtue of appointment only, without approval of the governing body, may be
removed and discharged at the pleasure of the appointing power. (Prior code §1-
1202)
2.36.030: BOND:
The following officers shall give bonds to the municipality with two (2) or
more sufficient sureties in the penal sum as follows; provided, surety bonds
may be furnished at the expense of the municipality in lieu of personal bonds:
   A.   Clerk: Five thousand dollars ($5,000.00);
   B.   Treasurer: Twenty five thousand dollars ($25,000.00). (Ord. 1 §1, 1957:
prior code §1-1203)
CHAPTER 2.40
PLANNING AND ZONING COMMISSION 1
SECTION:
2.40.010: Definitions
2.40.020: Creation
2.40.030: Rules; Organization; Meetings
2.40.040: Duties
2.40.050: Maps, Plats And Replats
2.40.060: Employees; Expenditures
 
Notes
1 1. IC ch. 67-65.
2.40.010: DEFINITIONS:
As used in this chapter:
APPOINTIVE MEMBERS: All members of the commission.
COMMISSION: The planning and zoning commission created by this chapter.
GOVERNING BOARD: The council of the city. (Ord. 2008-4 §1, 2008)
2.40.020: CREATION:
The commission shall consist of five (5) members. They shall be appointed by
the city mayor and confirmed by the city council. All members must have been
residents of the county in which they are serving for at least two (2) years,
and must reside within the county or county impact area while serving on the
commission. Members shall be selected without respect to political
affiliations, and shall serve without compensation. All members shall have a
term of office of six (6) years. All vacancies shall be filled in the same
manner as original appointments. Members may be removed after public hearing by
a majority of the governing body. (Ord. 2017-2, 2017)
2.40.030: RULES; ORGANIZATION; MEETINGS:
The commission shall elect its own chairman and create and fill such offices as
it may determine necessary for the proper conduct of the affairs and business
of the commission. Meetings of the commission shall be held when duly called by
the chairman by written or oral notice. At least one regular meeting shall be
held each month for not less than nine (9) months in a year. A majority of
voting members of the commission shall constitute a quorum. All meetings shall
be open to the public. Written rules consistent with this chapter and the laws
of the state for the transaction of business of the commission shall be
adopted. Written records of meetings, hearings, resolutions, findings, studies,
permits and actions shall be maintained and open to the public. A copy of the
rules of the commission and its aforesaid written records shall be maintained
in the city's files in city hall. (Ord. 2008-4 §1, 2008)
2.40.040: DUTIES:
It shall be the duty of the commission to:
   A.   Conduct a planning process to prepare, implement, review and update a
comprehensive plan that includes all lands within the governing board's
jurisdiction;
   B.   Hold public hearings prior to recommendations on the comprehensive
plan, recommend changes to the plan and prior to recommending ordinances;
   C.   Provide ways and means to obtain citizen participation in the planning
process;
   D.   Prepare and recommend subdivision and zoning ordinances;
   E.   Recommend changes to a comprehensive plan and zoning ordinances prior
to annexation of an unincorporated area;
   F.   Recommend a map, a governing plan and ordinances for an area of city
impact that is within the unincorporated area;
   G.   Provide ways and means to obtain citizen participation in the
administration of ordinances;
   H.   Prepare a procedure for processing zoning permits, namely: special use
permits, rezone applications, planned unit development proposals, subdivision
applications and variance applications;
   I.   Hear all requests for amendment to the zoning and subdivision
ordinances, hold at least one public hearing and make its recommendation to the
governing board. (Ord. 2008-4 §1, 2008)
2.40.050: MAPS, PLATS AND REPLATS:
Any and all maps, plats and replats of land which require approval of the
governing board or an officer or an employee shall first be submitted to the
commission for its suggestions (within the time frame specified within the
subdivision and/or zoning ordinance). (Ord. 2008-4 §1, 2008)
2.40.060: EMPLOYEES; EXPENDITURES:
Any expenditures of the commission shall be within the amounts appropriated and
set aside by the governing board for the purposes of the commission as set
forth in this chapter. Within such limits, the commission is authorized to hire
such employees and technical advisors as it deems necessary for the
accomplishment of its authorized purposes and work. All contracts and purchases
for the commission shall be made by the city's purchasing agent. (Ord. 2008-
4 §1, 2008)
CHAPTER 2.44
FIRE DEPARTMENT 1
SECTION:
2.44.010: Established
2.44.020: Personnel
2.44.030: Fire Chief Duties
2.44.040: Volunteer Members Duties
 
Notes
1 1. IC § 50-309.
2.44.010: ESTABLISHED:
There is established within the municipality a department designated as the
municipal fire department. (Prior code §3-201)
2.44.020: PERSONNEL:
The municipal fire department shall consist of a chief of the fire department,
to be appointed by the governing body, and such other personnel as the
governing body may from time to time determine necessary. (Prior code §3-202)
2.44.030: FIRE CHIEF DUTIES:
The duties of the chief of the municipal fire department shall be to:
   A.   Direct the fighting of fires;
   B.   Have charge of, be responsible for, and keep in good repair all
equipment and apparatus connected with or belonging to the municipal fire
department;
   C.   Call and direct such fire drills and meetings as he deems necessary for
the training of men in efficient firefighting;
   D.   Have authority over the personnel of the municipal fire department
during their activities while firefighting and during drills and meetings;
   E.   Have police authority while on duty as fire chief;
   F.   Keep records of all fires and make reports of same to each regular
meeting of the governing body. (Prior code §3-202)
2.44.040: VOLUNTEER MEMBERS DUTIES:
It shall be the duty of the volunteer members of the municipal fire department
to respond to all fire calls unless prevented from so doing by unavoidable
circumstances. They shall attend fire department drills and meetings and obey
such rules and regulations as are established for the municipal fire
department. (Prior code §3-203)
CHAPTER 2.48
LIBRARY BOARD 1
SECTION:
2.48.010: Appointment; Term Of Office
2.48.020: Organization; Powers
 
Notes
1 1. IC ch. 33-26, § 50-210.
2.48.010: APPOINTMENT; TERM OF OFFICE:
The mayor, with the consent of the council, may appoint a library board
consisting of seven (7) members, one of whom shall be a member of the council.
Such directors shall hold their office for three (3) years from the date of
appointment, and until their successors are appointed, but upon their first
appointment they shall divide themselves at their first meeting by lot, into
three (3) classes: two (2) members shall form the first class and shall serve
for one year; two (2) members shall form the second class and shall serve for
two (2) years; and two (2) members shall form the third class and shall serve
for three (3) years. No compensation shall be paid or allowed to any member of
the library board in any manner whatsoever. (Prior code §2-301)
2.48.020: ORGANIZATION; POWERS:
The board shall, immediately after their appointment, meet and organize by the
election of one of their number president, and by the election of such other
officers as they may deem necessary. They shall make and adopt such rules and
regulations as may be expedient. They shall have exclusive control of the
expenditure of all library monies collected and the supervision, care and
custody of all library buildings, and may appoint a librarian and assistants
and prescribe rules for their conduct. (Prior code §2-302)

CHAPTER 2.56
BUILDING INSPECTOR
SECTION:
2.56.010: Appointment
2.56.020: Compensation
2.56.030: Duty
2.56.010: APPOINTMENT:
The mayor, with the approval of the council, may appoint a building inspector
who shall hold office during the term of and under the conditions prescribed
for appointive officers. (Prior code §1-2101)
2.56.020: COMPENSATION:
The compensation of the building inspector shall be paid by each applicant for
a building permit at the time of the issuance thereof. The fee shall be the sum
of one dollar ($1.00) for each one thousand dollars ($1,000.00) of cost to the
nearest thousand with a minimum fee of two dollars ($2.00). (Ord. 8 §1, 1958:
prior code §1-2102)
2.56.030: DUTY:
It shall be the duty of the building inspector to inspect and pass upon all
applications for building permits, in accordance with all regulations and laws
now in force, or that may hereafter be enacted by the municipality, governing
the erection of buildings, structures, or the improvements and alterations of
any building or structure now existing, or that may hereafter be erected. It
shall further be the duty of the building inspector to inspect any such
buildings three (3) times, two (2) of such inspections shall be made during the
progress of construction or alteration, and the final inspection to be made
upon completion of the work. (Ord. 8 §2, 1958: prior code §1-2103)

SECTION:

2.60.010: APPOINTMENT:
The mayor may appoint, with the approval of the council, a superintendent of

2.60.020: DUTIES:
The duties of the superintendent shall be as follows:
   A.   To supervise the operation of the sanitation department;
   B.   To enforce the provisions of this code and perform such other and
further duties as may be assigned to him by the governing body;
   C.   To make a complete and adequate report on the first day of each month
on matters pertaining to the department;
   D.   To propose rules and regulations necessary to carry out the provisions

CHAPTER 2.64
INDUSTRIAL DEVELOPMENT CORPORATION
SECTION:
2.64.010: Definitions
2.64.020: Created
2.64.030: Name
2.64.040: Powers And Limitations; Generally
2.64.050: Charter
2.64.060: Board Of Directors; Appointment; Quorum
2.64.070: Officers Of The Board
2.64.080: Conflict Of Interest
2.64.090: Powers And Limitations; Designated
2.64.100: Indemnification
2.64.110: Benefit Of Net Earnings
2.64.010: DEFINITIONS:
As used in this chapter, the following words shall have the following meanings:
ACT: Chapter 27, title 50, Idaho Code.
BOARD OF DIRECTORS: The board of directors of the public corporation.
CITY: The city of Kamiah, Idaho.
CORPORATION: The industrial development corporation of the city of Kamiah,
Idaho.
FACILITIES: Land, rights in land, buildings, structures, docks, wharves,
machinery, transmission equipment, landscaping, utilities, approaches, roadways
and parking, handling and storage areas, and similar ancillary facilities.
INDUSTRIAL DEVELOPMENT FACILITY OR INDUSTRIAL DEVELOPMENT FACILITIES:
Manufacturing, processing, production, assembly, warehousing, transportation,
pollution control, solid waste disposal, and energy facilities. (Ord. 1-83 §1,
1983)
2.64.020: CREATED:
The city hereby creates a public corporation to carry out the purposes of
chapter 27, title 50, Idaho Code (the "act"), as that law may from time to time
hereinafter be amended. (Ord. 1-83 §2, 1983)
2.64.030: NAME:
The name of the public corporation shall be "the industrial development
corporation of the city of Kamiah, Idaho" (the "corporation"). (Ord. 1-83 §3,
1983)
2.64.040: POWERS AND LIMITATIONS; GENERALLY:
The corporation shall have all the powers and be subject to all of the
limitations and provisions contained in the act, as that law may hereinafter
from time to time be amended. (Ord. 1-83 §4, 1983)
2.64.050: CHARTER:
A charter shall be issued to the corporation by the city council, which shall
grant to the corporation authority to act pursuant to the act. A copy of the
initial charter to be issued is attached as exhibit A to the ordinance codified
herein. Said charter may be amended from time to time by the city council and
shall contain the limitations set forth in the act. (Ord. 1-83 §5, 1983)
2.64.060: BOARD OF DIRECTORS; APPOINTMENT; QUORUM:
The board of directors of the corporation shall be designated and appointed by
the city council. A majority of the members of the board of directors shall
constitute a quorum. (Ord. 1-83 §6, 1983)
2.64.070: OFFICERS OF THE BOARD:
   A.   The affairs of the corporation shall be conducted and carried out by
the board of directors. The board shall elect among its own members, its
president, a vice president, a treasurer and a secretary, one of whom shall be
eligible to hold two (2) offices. The board of directors shall adopt bylaws
(rules and regulations) governing the conduct of the corporation.
   B.   Members of the board of directors shall serve with such compensation as
may be provided in the bylaws to be adopted by the board of directors. (Ord. 1-
83 §7, 1983)
2.64.080: CONFLICT OF INTEREST:
No director, officer, agent or employee of the corporation shall have directly
or indirectly any financial interest in any property to be included in or any
contract for property, service or materials to be furnished or used in
connection with any industrial development facilities financed through the
corporation. (Ord. 1-83 §8, 1983)
2.64.090: POWERS AND LIMITATIONS; DESIGNATED:
The corporation shall have all the powers granted by, as well as limited by,
the act and shall include the following:
   A.   To construct and maintain one or more industrial development
facilities;
   B.   To lease to a lessee all or any part of any industrial development
facility for such rentals and upon such terms and conditions, including options
to purchase, as its board of directors considers advisable and not in conflict
with the act;
   C.   To sell by installment contract or otherwise and convey all or any part
of any industrial development facility for such purchase price and upon such
terms and conditions as its board of directors considers advisable, which are
not in conflict with the act;
   D.   To make loans for the purpose of providing temporary or permanent
financing or refinancing of all or part of the project cost of any industrial
development facility, including the refunding of any outstanding obligations,
mortgages, or advances issued, made, or given by any person for the project
cost; and to charge and collect interest on the loans for the loan payments
upon such terms and conditions as its board of directors considers advisable
which are not in conflict with the act;
   E.   To issue revenue bonds for the purpose of financing all or part of the
project cost of any industrial development facility and to secure the payment
of the revenue bonds as provided in the act;
   F.   As security for the payment of the principal of and interest on any
revenue bonds issued and any agreements made in connection therewith, to
mortgage, pledge, or otherwise encumber any or all of its industrial
development facilities or any part or parts thereof, whether then owned or
thereafter acquired, and to assign any lease or mortgage and repledge any
security conveyed to the corporation, to secure any loan made by the
corporation and to pledge the revenues and receipts therefrom;
   G.   To sue and be sued, complain, and defend in its corporate name;
   H.   To make contracts and to execute all instruments necessary or
convenient for carrying out of its business;
   I.   To have a corporate seal and to use the same by causing it, or a
facsimile thereof, to be impressed or affixed or in any other manner
reproduced;
   J.   Subject to the limitations of 50-2706, Idaho Code, to borrow money,
accept grants from, or contract with any local, state, or federal governmental
agency or with any financial public, or private corporation;
   K.   To make and alter bylaws not inconsistent with its charter for the
administration and regulation of the affairs of the corporation;
   L.   To collect fees or charges from users or prospective users of
industrial development facilities to recover actual or anticipated
administrative costs;
   M.   To execute financing documents incidental to the powers enumerated in
this subsection;
   N.   The corporation created under this chapter may not operate any
industrial development facilities as a business other than as lessor, seller,
or lender. The purchase and holding of mortgages, deeds of trust, or other
security interests and contracting for any servicing thereof is not considered
the operation of an industrial development facility;
   O.   The corporation created by this chapter may not exercise any of the
powers authorized in this section or issue any revenue bonds with respect to
any industrial development facility unless the industrial development facility
is located wholly within the boundaries of the city;
   P.   The city may not give or lend any money or property nor exercise its
power of eminent domain in aid of the corporation. This provision shall not
preclude the city from dealing with the corporation on an arm's length basis;
   Q.   The corporation may not issue revenue obligations except upon approval
of the city of Kamiah, and upon approval of the city within whose planning
jurisdiction the proposed industrial development facility lies. (Ord. 1-83 §9,
1983)
2.64.100: INDEMNIFICATION:
Every person who was or is a party, or is threatened to be made a party to, or
is involved in any action, suit or proceeding, whether civil, criminal,
administrative or investigative, by reason of the fact that he or a person of
whom he is the legal representative is or was a director or officer of the
corporation, or is or was serving at the request of the corporation as a
director or officer of another corporation, or as its representative in a
partnership, joint venture, trust or other enterprise, shall be indemnified and
held harmless to the fullest extent legally permissible under the law of the
state of Idaho from time to time against all expenses, liability and loss
(including attorney fees, judgments, fines and amounts paid or to be paid or to
be paid in settlement), reasonably incurred or suffered by him in connection
therewith. Such rights of indemnification shall be a contract right which may
be enforced in any manner desired by such person. Such right of indemnification
shall not be exclusive of any other right which such directors, officers, or
representatives may have or hereafter acquire, and without limiting the
generality of such statement, they shall be entitled to their respective rights
of indemnification under any bylaw, agreement, vote of stockholders, provision
of law, or otherwise, as well as their rights under this section. The board of
directors may adopt bylaws from time to time with respect to indemnification to
provide at all times the fullest indemnification permitted by the laws of the
state of Idaho, and may cause the corporation to purchase and maintain
insurance on behalf of any person who is or was a director or officer of the
corporation as a director or officer of another corporation, or as its
representative in a partnership, joint venture, trust or other enterprise,
against any liability asserted against such person and incurred in any such
capacity or arising out of such status, whether or not the corporation would
have the power to indemnify such person. (Ord. 1-83 §10, 1983)
2.64.110: BENEFIT OF NET EARNINGS:
Any net earnings of the corporation, beyond those necessary for retirement of
indebtedness incurred by it, shall inure to the city of Kamiah, and not for the
benefit of any other person. Alteration of the charter of or dissolution of or
audits of the corporation shall be as provided by the act and by subsequent
resolutions of the city. Upon dissolution of the corporation, title to all
property owned by the corporation shall vest in the city. (Ord. 1-83 §11, 1983)
CHAPTER 2.68
PUBLIC HEARINGS
SECTION:
2.68.010: Rules Established
2.68.010: RULES ESTABLISHED:
The following rules are established to be observed in the conduct of any public
hearing before the city council of the city of Kamiah, Idaho, and the planning
and zoning commission of the city of Kamiah, hereinafter referred to as the
hearing body. The following rules shall be known as the "Kamiah rules of
procedure":
   A.   Number 1. At the beginning of each public hearing, the presiding
officer of the hearing body shall describe the order of events which will occur
at the hearing. Such officer shall ask the public for any objections to such
order, and if there are none, the meeting shall proceed as set forth. If
objections are received, the hearing body shall consider the objection, and
either adopt the order of events as originally set forth, or amend the order of
events based upon the objection, if it appears to that body that such objection
has merit.
   B.   Number 2. No person shall be permitted to testify or speak before the
hearing body at a public hearing unless such person has signed his name and
written his residential address thereafter upon sign up sheets to be provided
by the city. This rule shall not apply to staff or technical witnesses directed
by the presiding officer to give evidence or information to the hearing body.
   C.   Number 3. No person shall be permitted to speak before the hearing body
at a public hearing unless such person shall be recognized by the presiding
officer.
   D.   Number 4. All public hearing proceedings shall be recorded
electronically or stenographically, and all persons speaking at such public
hearings shall speak before a microphone in such a manner as will assure that
the recorded testimony or remarks will be accurate and trustworthy.
   E.   Number 5. After the sign up sheets have been collected at any hearing,
the hearing body shall establish by rules or regulations for the conduct of
that meeting a time limit to be observed by all speakers. The time limit shall
be established, depending on the number of speakers who sign up for each public
hearing, and shall apply only to the speakers' comments.
   F.   Number 6. The speaker shall not be interrupted by members of the
hearing body until his time limit has been expended, or until he has finished
his statement.
   G.   Number 7. At the conclusion of a speaker's comments, each member, when
recognized by the presiding officer, shall be allowed to question the speaker,
and the speaker shall be limited to answers to questions asked. The question
and answer period shall not be included in the speaker's time limit as
established.
   H.   Number 8. When the public hearing is quasi-judicial in nature, or one
after which the hearing body is required by law to make findings of fact, each
speaker must swear or affirm that his testimony will be true and correct.
   I.   Number 9. Any person not conforming to any of the above rules may be
prohibited from speaking during the public hearing and should any person refuse
to comply with prohibition, he may be removed from the room by order of the
presiding officer with the assistance of law enforcement if necessary.
   J.   Number 10. The presiding officer shall have the authority to interpret
and apply the foregoing rules, subject to an appeal to the hearing body whose
decision shall be determined by a majority vote of the members present. (Ord.
5-83 §1, 1983)
