TITLE 4
RESERVED
TITLE 5
BUSINESS LICENSES AND REGULATIONS
CHAPTER 5.04
ADVERTISING; BILLPOSTING
SECTION:
5.04.010: License Required
5.04.020: Application For License
5.04.030: Littering Streets And Alleys
5.04.040: Posting Advertising Matter
5.04.010: LICENSE REQUIRED:
No person shall engage in the distribution or attaching of any signs, bills,
pictures or advertising matter unless the person has first been licensed.
(Prior code §5-201)
5.04.020: APPLICATION FOR LICENSE:
Application for a license shall be made to the clerk, together with all
necessary information including, but not limited to, the names of all owners
and the business addresses of the same. Upon approval of the application by the
governing body, the clerk shall issue a license for which a fee of twenty five
dollars ($25.00) shall be paid per year. (Prior code §5-202)
5.04.030: LITTERING STREETS AND ALLEYS:
No person shall scatter or throw upon the public thoroughfares any handbills,
posters, advertisements or papers. Nothing in this section shall be construed
to authorize any person to obstruct the public thoroughfares or create any
nuisance therein. These provisions shall not interfere or prevent the posting
of notices required by law to be posted. (Prior code §5-203)
5.04.040: POSTING ADVERTISING MATTER:
No person shall post, paint, tack or otherwise attach any notice or other
advertising matter to any fence, wall or building or other property until first
obtaining the consent of the owner of such property. No person shall post,
paint, tack or otherwise attach any notices or advertising matter to any of the
telegraph, telephone, electric or other such poles. (Prior code §5-204)
CHAPTER 5.08
ALCOHOLIC BEVERAGES GENERALLY 1
SECTION:
5.08.010: Idaho Liquor And Beer Laws Adopted
5.08.020: Copies Of Laws On File
5.08.030: Exceptions From Code
5.08.040: Catering Permit
 
Notes
1 1. IC title 23, § 50-901.
5.08.010: IDAHO LIQUOR AND BEER LAWS ADOPTED:
There is adopted for the purposes of updating the current law for further
purposes of governing, licensing, sale and use of alcohol within the city of
Kamiah the laws of the state of Idaho and particularly title 23, Idaho Code, as
presently in effect as of June 20, 1978, of that certain volume; Idaho liquor
laws and beer laws, revised through the acts of the legislature 1976, published
by the authority of the department of law enforcement, liquor law division, by
the governing body of the city of Kamiah and the same is adopted and
incorporated as an ordinance of the city of Kamiah as though set forth at
length herein. (Ord. 11-78 §1, 1978)
5.08.020: COPIES OF LAWS ON FILE:
Three (3) copies of the Idaho liquor laws and beer laws, together with all
amendments thereto, certified by the city clerk, shall be kept on file in the
office of the city clerk for use and examination of them by the public. (Ord.
11-78 §2, 1978)
5.08.030: EXCEPTIONS FROM CODE:
All conduct and acts of persons referred to and related under Idaho Code
sections 23-601, 23-602, and 23-938 are specifically excepted from this code
and shall be punishable as provided by the Idaho state law in the Idaho Code.
(Ord. 11-78 §4, 1978)
5.08.040: CATERING PERMIT:
Prior to the issuance of any catering permit by any person, entity or
corporation holding a liquor license, by the drink, an application shall be
made to the city council more than fourteen (14) days prior to the expected
event where the catering permit is sought. Upon the filing of the application
with the city clerk, accompanied by a fee of twenty dollars ($20.00) per day,
the city council shall at its next regularly scheduled meeting, consider the
application. The council must consider the petition at least seven (7) days
prior to the proposed event for which the permit is sought and notify the
applicant whether the permit is granted or denied.
The city may deny a permit for any event which does not adequately provide for
potential crowd control, parking, restroom facilities, potential noise control
or cleanup. (Ord. 2016-9, 2016)
CHAPTER 5.16
BEER LICENSE 1
SECTION:
5.16.010: Definitions
5.16.020: License Required
5.16.030: Application For License
5.16.040: Qualifications For License
5.16.050: Revocation Of License
 
Notes
1 1. IC ch. 23-10.
5.16.010: DEFINITIONS:
BEER: Any beverage obtained by the alcoholic fermentation of an infusion or
decoction of barley, malt, and/or other ingredients in drinkable water of not
more than four percent (4%) of alcohol by weight.
RETAILER: Any person engaged in the sale or distribution of beer to the
consumer. (Prior code §5-901)
5.16.020: LICENSE REQUIRED:
It is unlawful for any person to dispose of beer without first obtaining a
proper license. (Prior code §5-902)
5.16.030: APPLICATION FOR LICENSE:
Application for a retail beer license shall be made under oath to the clerk and
the application shall show that the applicant possesses all of the
qualifications required by this code. Each application shall be forwarded,
after proper and adequate investigation by the chief of police, to the
governing body for approval or disapproval. (Prior code §5-903)
5.16.040: QUALIFICATIONS FOR LICENSE:
   A.   No retail license shall be issued to any applicant who:
      1.   Is not a bona fide owner of such business, or is not a citizen of
the United States, or has not been a bona fide resident of this state for a
period of thirty (30) days prior to the date of application; provided, that if
the applicant is a partnership, all partners shall be such citizens, and at
least one thereof, or the actual active manager therefor, shall have been such
resident; and if the applicant is a corporation, such corporation shall be
qualified to do business within the state, and the manager of such business
place shall be such citizen, and shall have been such resident;
      2.   Has or any partner or actual manager or officer or employee or
spouse of which has, been convicted of the violation of any laws of this state,
or of the United States, regulating, governing or prohibiting the sale of
alcoholic beverages or intoxicating liquor, or has within two (2) years
forfeited or suffered the forfeiture of a bond for his appearance to answer
charges of any such violation;
      3.   Has, or any partner or actual active manager or officer of which
has, been convicted of any felony within five (5) years or has paid any fine or
completed any sentence of confinement therefor within five (5) years.
   B.   A retailer licensee must continue, through the license period, to have
all of the foregoing qualifications and none of the foregoing
disqualifications, and for failure therein, upon proof thereof to an issuer of
a license, such issuer shall revoke the license issued, and in writing sent by
United States registered mail, shall notify each of the other issuers of a
retailer's license to such license (licensee), stating sufficient facts for
identification of the licensee and the grounds and date of revocation. (Ord. 9-
79 §1, 1979: prior code §5-904)
5.16.050: REVOCATION OF LICENSE:
The governing body of the municipality shall retain the right at all times to
revoke and cancel any license for just cause. When any license is revoked, the
licensee shall have the privilege of appearing before the governing body to
appeal such revocation. Any conduct or act on the part of the licensee which
may be sufficient cause for revocation of the license must be brought to the
attention of the governing body. (Prior code §5-908)
CHAPTER 5.20
LIQUOR LICENSE
SECTION:
5.20.010: Issuance Of License
5.20.020: Fee
5.20.030: Application For License
5.20.040: Number Of Licenses
5.20.050: Suspension Or Revocation Of License
5.20.010: ISSUANCE OF LICENSE:
The city clerk, upon the approval of the governing body, is authorized and
directed to issue licenses to qualified applicants to whom licenses to sell
retail liquor by the drink shall have been issued by the department of law
enforcement of the state of Idaho and Lewis County, Idaho, but that the number
of licenses so issued shall not exceed the maximum number provided in section
5.20.040 of this chapter. (Ord. 12-78 §1, 1978: Ord. 9 §2, 1959: prior code §5-
1003)
5.20.020: FEE:
Each licensee licensed under the provisions of this chapter shall pay an annual
license fee to the clerk in the sum of three hundred seventy five dollars
($375.00). The fee shall be for the entire year and shall not be prorated but
shall be paid in full at the beginning of each year. (Prior code §5-1004)
5.20.030: APPLICATION FOR LICENSE:
Upon application for license the licensee shall present for inspection a copy
of his state application to contain the information required under title 23,
chapter 9, of the Idaho Code, as amended, and the licensee shall also present a
copy of the state license and Lewis County license. If there are any false
statements that are contained within the state application for license, the
application for the municipal license shall be denied and no licensee shall be
entitled to have a license unless he has complied with all state laws and has
all of the qualifications required by state law. (Ord. 13-78 §1, 1978: prior
code §5-1005)
5.20.040: NUMBER OF LICENSES:
The governing body of the municipality shall be authorized to issue only the
number of licenses by type in accordance with the population of the city and
under the provisions of this chapter, as follows:
 
Population                 Number Of Retail Liquor
                           By The Drink Licenses
                          
   0 to 1,500             2 such licenses
   Each additional 1,5    1 additional license
 
(Ord. 31, 1962: prior code §5-1015)
5.20.050: SUSPENSION OR REVOCATION OF LICENSE:
The license of any licensee is subject to be suspended or revoked in the
judgment of the governing body for the violation of any of the provisions of
title 23, chapter 9, of the Idaho Code, as amended, or of any rule or
regulation contained in this chapter, and if upon examination and determination
of the facts just cause for revocation or suspension of the license has been
determined by the governing body, an order may be made suspending the same for
a period of at least six (6) months, and the governing body may refuse to grant
a renewal of the license. (Ord. 17-78 §1, 1978: prior code §5-1012)
CHAPTER 5.24
WINE LICENSE
SECTION:
5.24.010: Adoption Of State Law
5.24.020: Sale Of Wine Authorized
5.24.030: Fee
5.24.040: Regulations Of License
5.24.010: ADOPTION OF STATE LAW:
There is adopted for the purpose of governing the licensing and sale of table
wine within the city of Kamiah, in accordance with the provisions of chapter
23-13 of the Idaho Code, the provisions contained in said state law. (Ord.
1971-4 §1, 1974)
5.24.020: SALE OF WINE AUTHORIZED:
The city of Kamiah hereby authorizes the sale of wine containing not more than
fourteen percent (14%) alcohol by volume at retail within the boundaries of the
city of Kamiah, in accordance with the provisions of Idaho law. (Ord. 1971-
4 §2, 1974)
5.24.030: FEE:
There is established a charge of fifty dollars ($50.00) per year as a city
license fee for the sale of wine as authorized by state law. Proper application
forms and licenses will be provided through the office of the city clerk and
said licenses shall expire on January 1 at one o'clock (1:00) A.M. of each
year. (Ord. 1971-4 §3, 1974)
5.24.040: REGULATIONS OF LICENSE:
The qualifications for license shall be the same as set forth by Idaho law, and
the hours of sale, what persons can be sold wine, and all other regulations in
regard to the same shall be as prescribed by state law. (Ord. 1971-4 §4, 1971)
CHAPTER 5.26
LIQUOR SALES
SECTION:
5.26.010: Statutory Authority
5.26.020: Sunday Sales
5.26.030: Hours Of Sale Of Liquor By The Drink
5.26.040: Hours Of Sale Of Beer And Wine
5.26.050: Liquor Consumption After Authorized Hours Of Service
5.26.060: Liquor Consumption During Closed Hours
5.26.070: Improper Storage Of Unsealed Containers
5.26.010: STATUTORY AUTHORITY:
This chapter is adopted pursuant to the authority conferred by Idaho Code
sections 23-927, 23-1012 and 23-1332 as amended and current for the year 1987
and Lewis County ordinance 1987-2, adopted by the Lewis County commissioners on
December 14, 1987, which statutes and amended county ordinance provide that the
city and county may by ordinance allow the sale of liquor by the drink on
Sundays, Memorial Day and Thanksgiving and may also extend until two o'clock
(2:00) A.M. the hours of sale of liquor by the drink, beer and wine. (Ord. 88-
2 §1, 1987)
5.26.020: SUNDAY SALES:
Liquor by the drink may be sold, offered for sale or given away on any licensed
premises on Sunday under the same rules, limitations and conditions as apply to
all other days of the week. (Ord. 88-2 §2, 1987)
5.26.030: HOURS OF SALE OF LIQUOR BY THE DRINK:
No liquor by the drink shall be sold, offered for sale or given away upon any
licensed premises and all liquor not in sealed bottles must be locked in a
separate room or cabinet during the following hours:
   A.   On any day between the hours of two o'clock (2:00) A.M. and ten o'clock
(10:00) A.M. (Ord. 2012-5, 2012)
5.26.040: HOURS OF SALE OF BEER AND WINE:
Beer and wine as defined by the Idaho Code shall be sold only between the hours
of six o'clock (6:00) A.M. and two o'clock (2:00) A.M. of the following day.
These restrictions shall apply to beer and wine that is sold and dispensed for
consumption on the premises and likewise the packaged sale of beer and wine to
be consumed off the premises. (Ord. 88-2 §4, 1987)
5.26.050: LIQUOR CONSUMPTION AFTER AUTHORIZED HOURS OF SERVICE:
Any patron present on any licensed premises after the sale of liquor by the
drink, wine and beer has stopped as provided in sections
5.26.030 and
5.26.040 of this chapter shall have a reasonable time not to exceed thirty (30)
minutes to consume any beverages already served. (Ord. 88-2 §5, 1987)
5.26.060: LIQUOR CONSUMPTION DURING CLOSED HOURS:
Any person who consumes or intentionally permits the consumption of any
alcoholic beverage upon licensed premises during any closed periods provided in
this chapter shall be guilty of a misdemeanor as defined in Idaho Code sections
18-111 and 18-113. (Ord. 88-2 §6, 1987)
5.26.070: IMPROPER STORAGE OF UNSEALED CONTAINERS:
It shall be the duty of every person who is employed at or upon any licensed
premises or who owns or manages a licensed premises and who is present upon the
licensed premises during the hours and the times set forth in this chapter,
concerning liquor by the drink, to lock up and keep locked up in a locked room
or locked cabinet all unsealed containers of liquor, and any such person who
fails to perform the duty provided herein shall be guilty of a misdemeanor as
provided in Idaho Code sections 18-111 and 18-113. (Ord. 88-2 §6, 1987)
CHAPTER 5.28
HOTELS 1
SECTION:
5.28.010: Definition
5.28.020: Fire Extinguisher And Hose Requirement
5.28.030: Gong Requirement
5.28.040: Inspection
5.28.050: Guest Registration
 
Notes
1 1. IC ch. 39-18.
5.28.010: DEFINITION:
Every building or structure kept, used or maintained as, or advertised as, or
held out to the public to be an inn, hotel or public lodging house or place
where sleeping accommodations are furnished for hire to transient guests,
whether with or without meals, in which eight (8) or more rooms are used for
the accommodation of such guests, shall for the purposes of this chapter be
defined to be a "hotel", and whenever the word "hotel" occurs in this chapter,
it shall be construed to mean every such structure as is described in this
section. (Prior code §5-501)
5.28.020: FIRE EXTINGUISHER AND HOSE REQUIREMENT:
Each and every hotel shall be provided with at least one efficient chemical
fire extinguisher approved by the national board of fire underwriters, for each
two thousand five hundred (2,500) square feet or less of floor space or area,
which extinguisher or extinguishers shall be placed in a convenient location in
a public hallway outside of the sleeping rooms and in all public rooms, and
shall also always be in a condition for use; or, in lieu thereof, such hotel
shall be equipped with a standpipe at least one and one-fourth inches (11/4")
in diameter, with hose connection, and hose of sufficient length always
attached, in the hallway on each floor, which standpipe shall be equipped with
a sufficient pressure of water at all times. (Prior code §5-502)
5.28.030: GONG REQUIREMENT:
Each and every hotel shall be provided with a gong at least nine inches (9") in
diameter on each floor, which shall be placed in the hallway in such a position
that it will be of easy access and so that its ringing can be heard in every
room, and means for ringing such gong shall be provided, which may be operated
from the office or from the location of any such gong and shall be sufficient
to keep all of the gongs ringing continuously for at least three (3) minutes
after being started. (Prior code §5-503)
5.28.040: INSPECTION:
It shall be the duty of the municipal official designated by the governing body
to inspect hotels and determine that all building and health regulations in
addition to any other regulations that may be in force are adhered to. (Prior
code §5-504)
5.28.050: GUEST REGISTRATION:
Every operator of a hotel shall maintain a register in which each guest of such
hotel shall register his name, home address and date of registering. Such
register shall be available to any authorized person and shall be preserved for
one year. (Prior code §5-505)
CHAPTER 5.32
MOTELS
SECTION:
5.32.010: Service Station Restrictions
5.32.020: Unit Requirements
5.32.030: Fire And Building Code Conformance
5.32.040: Guest Registration
5.32.010: SERVICE STATION RESTRICTIONS:
Automobile service stations shall be located no closer than fifty feet (50') to
any motel. (Prior code §5-402)
5.32.020: UNIT REQUIREMENTS:
The minimum space for each unit shall be twelve feet by twenty feet (12' x 20')
and shall contain one full bath, toilet facilities, dressing compartment and
sleeping room. (Prior code §5-404)
5.32.030: FIRE AND BUILDING CODE CONFORMANCE:
The plumbing, heating and ventilation components shall meet all local fire and
building code requirements. (Prior code §5-405)
5.32.040: GUEST REGISTRATION:
Every operator of a motel shall maintain a register in which each guest of such
motel shall register his name, home address and license number of the vehicle
in which he is traveling. The date of his arrival and departure shall also be
recorded. Such register shall be available to any authorized person inspecting
the motel and shall be preserved for a period of not less than one year. (Prior
code §5-407)
CHAPTER 5.36
POOL HALLS AND CARD ROOMS 1
SECTION:
5.36.010: Definition
5.36.020: License Fee
5.36.030: Sale Or Transfer
 
Notes
1 1. IC § 18-1201.
5.36.010: DEFINITION:
Every person who keeps a hall or room containing a pool, billiard table or card
table, for the use of the public, is a pool hall, billiard hall or card room
keeper, and such hall or room is a pool, billiard hall or card room. (Prior
code §5-801)
5.36.020: LICENSE FEE:
Before a license shall be issued to any person to operate or open a billiard,
pool or card hall or room, such person shall pay to the clerk a license fee of
twenty five dollars ($25.00) per quarter for one card table, and five dollars
($5.00) per quarter for each additional card table; and five dollars ($5.00)
per quarter for each pool or billiard table. The license shall expire on the
last day of each quarter. (Prior code §5-803)
5.36.030: SALE OR TRANSFER:
The license granted in this chapter shall be a personal license to the person
making the application therefor, and if, during the term for which the license
is granted, the billiard, pool hall or card room is sold or transferred to any
other person, the license shall immediately terminate; provided, however, the
successor of the license may secure a license as hereinabove provided in the
same manner as the original licensee without being required to pay any
additional charge for the unexpired term of the original license. (Prior code
§5-804)
CHAPTER 5.40
SECONDHAND DEALERS AND PAWNBROKERS
SECTION:
5.40.010: Definitions
5.40.020: License Fee
5.40.030: Business Place Designated On License
5.40.040: Purchase Of Goods From Minors
5.40.050: Inspection
5.40.060: Records
5.40.010: DEFINITIONS:
PAWNBROKERS: Every person who makes a business of lending money on the security
of personal property deposited or pledged in his keeping is a pawnbroker.
SECONDHAND AND JUNK DEALERS: Every person who deals in secondhand furniture or
secondhand household goods or who engages in the purchase of any used, old or
discarded articles or things shall be termed a "secondhand dealer" and his
place of business shall be known as a "secondhand store" or "junk shop". (Prior
code §§5-1101, 5-1102)
5.40.020: LICENSE FEE:
Every person who shall engage in the business of running and operating a
secondhand store or junk shop or who is a pawnbroker shall pay a license fee of
one dollar ($1.00) per year. (Prior code §5-1103)
5.40.030: BUSINESS PLACE DESIGNATED ON LICENSE:
Every license granted to any secondhand dealer or pawnbroker shall designate
the house or place, together with the street and number, in which the person
receiving such license shall be authorized to carry on such business. In case
any licensee licensed as such desires to remove his store or place of business
from the place designated in his license to another location, he shall give
notice to the clerk who will endorse on the license held by the licensee the
designation of the new location in any other place than that designated in the
license unless the new location has been endorsed upon his license by the
clerk. (Prior code §5-1104)
5.40.040: PURCHASE OF GOODS FROM MINORS:
No secondhand dealer or pawnbroker shall purchase any goods or articles
whatsoever from any minor without first advising the chief of police and giving
him an opportunity to inspect the goods offered for sale before purchase.
(Prior code §5-1105)
5.40.050: INSPECTION:
Every secondhand dealer or pawnbroker shall, during reasonable hours, and upon
request of any police or peace officer, permit such officer to examine and
inspect any merchandise, article or thing in stock in his place of business.
(Prior code §5-1106)
5.40.060: RECORDS:
Every secondhand dealer and pawnbroker shall keep a book in which shall be
written, in the English language at the time of the purchase of any article or
thing, a description of the article or thing, and the name and address or the
name and description of the person from whom such purchase was made, and the
book, as well as every article or thing, shall at all reasonable hours be open
for police inspection. (Prior code §5-1107)
CHAPTER 5.44
TEMPORARY STREET VENDORS
SECTION:
5.44.010: Advertising
5.44.020: Permit Required; Application
5.44.030: Waiver Of Permit
5.44.040: Fee
5.44.050: Permit Denial; Hearing
5.44.060: Operating Without A Permit
5.44.070: Advertising Violation
5.44.010: ADVERTISING:
No person, corporation, association or business of any kind shall be permitted
to locate on the rights of way of the city, whether it be street right of way
or sidewalk right of way, merchandise, advertising or signs, advertising any
activity or any business or merchandise for sale under any circumstances.
However, the city shall have the right to waive by appropriate motion made by
the full city council the requirements set forth herein in the event any civic
organization desires to temporarily advertise any civic event within the Kamiah
community. In the event the provisions of this chapter are waived by the
council, the council shall within such waiver grant such permission to the
civic organization allowing advertising in a specific place where reasonable
safety to pedestrians or traffic is assured. (Ord. 98-13 §1, 1998: Ord. 90-
1 §1, 1990)
5.44.020: PERMIT REQUIRED; APPLICATION:
Any person or organization desiring to locate a temporary street vendor's stand
within the incorporated limits of the city shall be required to secure a permit
for the operation of such street stand from the city council prior to the
opening of such street stand within the city.
Application for such retail street stand shall be made on forms to be provided
by the city clerk and filed with the city clerk. Permits shall be issued in
writing by the city clerk after approval by a standing committee appointed by
the city council, i.e., city clerk and/or mayor. Should the committee conclude
that the street stand is of a potential controversial nature, the committee may
refer the matter to the full city council.
Furthermore, during organized and regular city celebrations, the city may
authorize the chamber of commerce to become the authorized standing committee
hereinabove mentioned for the issuance of permits with all powers that said
committee is hereunder granted. (Ord. 98-13 §2, 1998: Ord. 90-1 §2, 1990)
5.44.030: WAIVER OF PERMIT:
In the event that a locally organized nonprofit organization or group shall
desire to locate a temporary street stand for special events within the city,
the city council or committee may, by appropriate motion, waive the need for a
permit under such circumstance to any such local civic organization. (Ord. 98-
13 §3, 1998: Ord. 90-1 §3, 1990)
5.44.040: FEE:
Any person desiring a permit to locate a temporary retail street stand shall
pay a fee of ten dollars ($10.00) for every ten (10) days which shall accompany
the initial application to the city clerk, and which shall be retained by the
city for the purposes of investigation and review of the applicant and the
expected purpose for such street stand or business. (Ord. 98-13 §4, 1998: Ord.
90-1 §4, 1990)
5.44.050: PERMIT DENIAL; HEARING:
Any persons having a permit denied by the city council shall be entitled to a
hearing before the full city council, or such hearing examiners as are
appointed by the city council from time to time to hear such appeal. Grounds
for denial shall include, but not be limited to, previous criminal conduct of
the applicant, or his employees, inappropriate cleanliness concerning food
items, a history of fraud or fraudulent practices practiced by the applicant,
inappropriate previous conduct of the same character, or any other relevant
information. (Ord. 98-13 §5, 1998: Ord. 90-1 §5, 1990)
5.44.060: OPERATING WITHOUT A PERMIT:
Operating a temporary street stand within the city without a permit or without
a waiver granted by the city council or its standing committee, shall
constitute a general misdemeanor and be punishable as such. (Ord. 98-13 §6,
1998: Ord. 90-1 §6, 1990)
5.44.070: ADVERTISING VIOLATION:
Locating advertising or merchandise on the city's rights of way, in violation
of section
5.44.010 of this chapter, shall constitute a general misdemeanor and be
punishable by such. However, prior to prosecution under section
5.44.010 of this chapter and this section, any person so advertising shall be
entitled to one written warning in advance of such prosecution and proof of
such warning shall be a condition precedent to prosecution. (Ord. 98-13 §7,
1998: Ord. 90-1 §7, 1990)
TITLE 6
ANIMALS
CHAPTER 6.04
LIVESTOCK AND POULTRY AT LARGE
SECTION:
6.04.010: Livestock Running At Large Prohibited
6.04.020: Poultry Running At Large Prohibited
6.04.030: Notification Of Livestock At Large
6.04.040: Notice And Sale Of Livestock
6.04.050: Revenue From Sale
6.04.060: Freeing Impounded Livestock Prohibited
6.04.010: LIVESTOCK RUNNING AT LARGE PROHIBITED:
No livestock shall be permitted at large in the municipality at any time during
the year; and it is unlawful for anyone to herd or drive any livestock through
the streets without having the livestock under control by means of rope, strap
or other devices by which they may be led unless such livestock is being driven
in harness or hauled; provided, that this chapter shall not be construed as
prohibiting stockmen from driving herds through the municipality when necessary
to transfer them from one pasture to another or for the purpose of shipping,
but such stockmen so driving stock through the municipality shall be liable to
property owners for all damages done to their property by such stock while
being driven through the municipality, whether such damage is caused by the
negligence of the stockmen or their agents or not. Such stock shall be driven
through the municipality in as short a time as possible. (Ord. 2008-3 §1, 2008)
6.04.020: POULTRY RUNNING AT LARGE PROHIBITED:
It is unlawful for any person to keep fowl or poultry unless such fowl or
poultry are at all times kept upon his own premises and in enclosures. (Ord.
2008-3 §1, 2008)
6.04.030: NOTIFICATION OF LIVESTOCK AT LARGE:
If any livestock is found running at large contrary to the provisions of this
chapter, the sheriff or brand inspector shall be notified as provided by Idaho
Code section 25-2302 et seq. (Ord. 2008-3 §1, 2008)
6.04.040: NOTICE AND SALE OF LIVESTOCK:
The provisions of Idaho Code section 25-2303 et seq., shall be followed for the
notification and sale of livestock. (Ord. 2008-3 §1, 2008)
6.04.050: REVENUE FROM SALE:
The provisions of Idaho Code section 25-2303 et seq., shall be followed for the
disposition of revenue received for any sale of livestock. (Ord. 2008-3 §1,
2008)
6.04.060: FREEING IMPOUNDED LIVESTOCK PROHIBITED:
It is unlawful to break open or in any manner, directly or indirectly, aid or
assist in breaking open any pen or enclosure with intent of releasing any
livestock confined therein pursuant to the provisions of this chapter. (Ord.
2008-3 §1, 2008)
CHAPTER 6.08
DOGS
SECTION:
6.08.010: Definitions
6.08.020: License Required
6.08.030: Fees For License
6.08.040: Exemptions For License
6.08.050: Tag Issuance
6.08.060: Tag Regulations
6.08.070: Transfer Of Ownership
6.08.080: Revocation Of License
6.08.090: Dogs At Large
6.08.100: Offenses
6.08.110: Public Nuisances
6.08.120: Manner Of Keeping Animals
6.08.130: Impoundment, Citation Issued
6.08.140: Disposition Of Dangerous Dog
6.08.150: Quarantine Of Animals
6.08.160: Notice Of Impounding
6.08.170: Redemption Of Impounded Animals
6.08.180: Disposition Of Unclaimed Dogs
6.08.190: Release Of Unclaimed Animals
6.08.200: Vicious Animals
6.08.210: Animal Care Costs
6.08.220: Humane Treatment
6.08.230: Rabies Vaccination
6.08.240: Penalties For Violations
6.08.250: Kennels; Number Of Dogs Allowed
6.08.260: Liability Of Parents
6.08.270: Wolves Or Wolf Hybrids
6.08.010: DEFINITIONS:
As used in this chapter, unless the context otherwise indicates, the following
words and terms shall mean:
ALLOW (OR PERMIT): To permit an act by an animal by neglecting to provide
adequate restraint. A person does not have to intend the results of an animal's
actions in order to have allowed or permitted.
ANIMAL: Any nonhuman living creature, domestic or wild, male or female, natural
or sterilized.
ANIMAL CONTROL OFFICER: Any person designated by the city appointing authority
to carry out the provisions of this chapter under the laws of the state of
Idaho and the city of Kamiah.
ANIMAL SHELTER: Any premises designated by the city authority for the purpose
of impounding and caring for animals held under authority of this chapter.
AT LARGE: To be off the premises of the owner and not under the control of the
owner or another person.
DANGEROUS ANIMAL: Any animal of a species or type likely to cause injury to a
person, or any animal which has demonstrated a propensity to attack or cause
injury to a person.
DOG: Any member, male or female, of the family Canis familiaris.
HARBORING: The occupant of any premises on which an animal remains or to which
it customarily returns for food and care, is presumed to be harboring or
keeping the animal within the meaning of this chapter.
KENNEL: Includes any place other than a veterinary hospital where three (3) or
more dogs are kept or where one or more bitches are kept for breeding and the
offspring thereof are sold for profit or given away, or where such animals are
received for care and boarding.
LEASH: Shall include a cord, thong, leash or chain not more than six feet (6')
in length by which an animal is controlled by the person accompanying it for
exercise purposes.
NEUTERED ANIMAL: Includes both male and female dogs rendered incapable of
reproducing any offspring.
OWNER, CUSTODIAN OR KEEPER: Any person, firm, association, corporation or
partnership, or their agents or persons acting with their permission, owning,
keeping or harboring an animal.
POLICE OFFICER: Any employee of the city of Kamiah, the Kamiah marshal's
office, the Lewis County sheriff's office, or Idaho County sheriff's office who
is hired or charged with the duty of enforcing criminal and/or traffic laws
within the city of Kamiah.
PREMISES: All the real property under one's ownership or control inside the
inner line of a sidewalk, or, if there is no sidewalk, inside the curb, ditch
or shoulder marking edge of the used public right of way. Premises also means
the inside of a closed motor vehicle.
SPAYED FEMALE: Includes a female dog which has been sterilized by a licensed
veterinarian to avoid or prevent conception.
UNDER CONTROL: The owner or person in charge, by means of a leash, restrains
the dog to the owner's, or to the person in charge's immediate proximity,
preventing the dog from trespassing upon the property of others, or from
annoying or chasing other persons, animals or vehicles of any sort.
VETERINARY HOSPITAL: Any establishment maintained and operated by a licensed
veterinarian for the boarding of animals or the diagnoses, treatment and care
of diseased or injured animals.
VICIOUS ANIMAL: Includes an animal whose temperament or habits create danger or
likelihood of injury to persons or other animals or creates a reasonable
apprehension of injury to persons or other animals. (Ord. 98-14 §1, 1998)
6.08.020: LICENSE REQUIRED:
The keeping of dogs within the limits of the city is hereby forbidden unless
the owners, custodians or keepers, or those harboring thereof, shall procure a
license for each dog if over six (6) months of age, as herein provided for,
except this requirement will not apply to a nonresident keeping a dog within
the city for no longer than thirty (30) days. In any prosecution for a
violation of this section, the absence of a tag to be appended to a dog, as
provided for in section
6.08.050 of this chapter, shall be prima facie evidence that the dog has not
been legally licensed. Any person violating the provisions of this section
shall be guilty of an infraction punishable by a fine in the amount of twenty
dollars ($20.00). (Ord. 2016-3, 2016)
6.08.030: FEES FOR LICENSE:
The license fees for dogs for each year, or part thereof, shall be as
established by resolution of the city council.
The license for a dog shall be available during the month of January each year,
which shall be valid from January 1 of that year through December 31 of that
year. All licenses shall expire on December 31 of the year for which they are
issued. Proof of neutering or spaying must be provided at the time of
licensing.
There shall be no refund of a dog license fee, or any part thereof. (Ord. 2020-
01 §1, 2020; Ord. 2006-3 §1, 2006: Ord. 98-14 §1, 1998)
6.08.040: EXEMPTIONS FOR LICENSE:
No license fee shall be required of any city animal shelter, veterinary
hospital or humane society. (Ord. 98-14 §1, 1998)
6.08.050: TAG ISSUANCE:
On payment to the city clerk of the amount of any such license fee it shall be
the duty of the clerk to issue a license to the person applying therefor, which
license shall remain and be in force from its date through December 31 next
ensuing, and the city clerk shall furnish with such license a metal tag upon
which shall be stamped a number corresponding with the number entered on such
license and the year for which it is issued and the words "Kamiah", or "City of
Kamiah Dog License" and such tag shall be appended to a collar to be constantly
worn by the dog. In case a dog tag is lost or destroyed a duplicate will be
issued by the clerk upon receipt showing the payment of the license fee for the
current year and the payment of an amount established by resolution of the city
council for such duplicate. (Ord. 2020-01 §2, 2020; Ord. 2006-3, 2006: Ord. 98-
14 §1, 1998)
6.08.060: TAG REGULATIONS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to remove, steal, mutilate or destroy the
license identification tag of any dog. It shall be unlawful for anyone to
refuse to show or exhibit at any reasonable time to any license inspector,
animal control officer or police officer any dog in his possession or custody
and/or any license or identification tag issued therefor. (Ord. 98-14 §1, 1998)
6.08.070: TRANSFER OF OWNERSHIP:
It shall be unlawful for any owner to use any license tag for any dog other
than the one for which it has been issued. If there is a change of ownership of
a licensed dog the new owner must apply for and obtain a new license from the
city clerk. (Ord. 98-14 §1, 1998)
6.08.080: REVOCATION OF LICENSE:
   A.   The city clerk may revoke any license if the person holding the license
refuses or fails to comply with this chapter or any law governing the
protection and keeping of dogs, or if such person provides false or misleading
information in obtaining such license.
   B.   Any person whose license is revoked shall, within ten (10) days
thereafter, remove the dog(s) from the city limits, or humanely dispose of such
dog or dogs, kept or harbored by such person and no part of the license fee
shall be refunded.
   C.   If the applicant has withheld or falsified any information on the
application the city clerk shall refuse to issue a license.
   D.   Any person having been denied a license or having a license revoked may
not reapply for a period of thirty (30) days. (Ord. 98-14 §1, 1998)
6.08.090: DOGS AT LARGE:
It shall be unlawful for any person to cause, permit or allow a dog or dogs
owned, harbored, controlled or kept by him or her in the city to roam, run or
stray away from the premises, except, that while away from said premises, said
dog or dogs shall, at all times, be controlled by means of a leash not
exceeding six feet (6') in length by the owner or some duly authorized and
competent person; provided, however, that such leash is not required for any
dog when otherwise safely and securely confined or completely controlled while
in or upon any vehicle. This section shall not apply to dogs which are in
special areas of parks designated and posted by the park manager, when the
rules with respect to the use of such areas are complied with, and said dogs
are under custody and control of a trainer. Every female dog in heat shall be
confined in a building or secure enclosure. (Ord. 98-14 §1, 1998)
6.08.100: OFFENSES:
No dog shall be permitted to commit the following offenses on any premises or
property, public or private: bite or attempt to bite any person; destroy
private property; scatter refuse; chase vehicles; chase or harass livestock or
other animals; or commit any nuisances defined by this or any other chapter of
law; and no dog shall be permitted to deposit fecal matter on any property not
that of its owner. (Ord. 98-14 §1, 1998)
6.08.110: PUBLIC NUISANCES:
It shall be unlawful for any owner to fail to exercise proper care and control
of their animals to prevent them from becoming public nuisances. No person
owning any animal shall suffer or permit such animal to disturb the peace and
quiet of the neighborhood by barking or by making other loud or unusual noises.
A violation of this section is declared a public nuisance and adverse to the
public welfare. (Ord. 98-14 §1, 1998)
6.08.120: MANNER OF KEEPING ANIMALS:
No person who owns, harbors, controls or keeps any dog in the city shall cause,
permit or allow any such dog or dogs, or any pen, yard, enclosure or building
in which such animals are to be kept, in such a manner as to be nauseous, foul
or offensive. (Ord. 98-14 §1, 1998)
6.08.130: IMPOUNDMENT, CITATION ISSUED:
Any dog or dogs found without a license or running at large, or in violation in
any manner with the provisions of this chapter, shall, at the discretion of the
animal control officer or police officer, be:
   A.   Impounded and placed in the city animal shelter, or, if deemed
necessary, in a private animal shelter, and said officer, upon taking this
action, shall make a complete registry, entering the breed, color and sex of
such dog and any available license information. If the dog is licensed an entry
shall be made showing the name and address of the owner and the number of the
license tag; or
   B.   If the owner is known or may be determined, the animal control officer
or police officer may issue to the owner or person responsible a citation and
notice to appear before the district court. (Ord. 98-14 §1, 1998)
6.08.140: DISPOSITION OF DANGEROUS DOG:
Whenever it shall appear to a person attempting to impound a dog under the
provisions of this chapter that such a dog is dangerous to the public if
capture cannot be effected safely and promptly, said person is authorized to
destroy the dog. (Ord. 98-14 §1, 1998)
6.08.150: QUARANTINE OF ANIMALS:
Any animal that bites a person shall be quarantined for ten (10) days if
ordered by the animal control officer. At the discretion of the animal control
officer the quarantine may be on the premises of the owner. If the animal
control officer requires other confinement the owner shall, at his or her own
expense, surrender the animal for the quarantine period to the animal shelter
or shall place the animal in a veterinary hospital. Any animal that bites a
person or other animal, without provocation, shall be securely confined
thereafter in a fenced enclosure from which the animal cannot escape and which
is not accessible to the public, except that the animal may be taken off of the
owner's premises if securely controlled according to the provisions of this
chapter. The animal control officer shall maintain a record of every animal
that bites a person without provocation. (Ord. 98-14 §1, 1998)
6.08.160: NOTICE OF IMPOUNDING:
Not later than twenty four (24) hours after the impounding of any dog, the
owner, if known, shall be notified, either in person or in writing, by first
class mail addressed to the owner at his or her last known address, of said
impoundment, describing the animal and the place and time of taking and time
the animal may be redeemed. If the said owner or custodian is unknown, written
notice shall be posted for not less than three (3) calendar days in the front
window of city hall. (Ord. 98-14 §1, 1998)
6.08.170: REDEMPTION OF IMPOUNDED ANIMALS:
The owner or lawful custodian of any dog impounded under the provisions of this
chapter may reclaim such dog within three (3) days after receiving personal
notice or three (3) days after the mailing of notice or date of posting notices
at city hall, provided, said dog shall be released to the owner or custodian
only upon payment of the dog license fee, if unpaid, and all costs and charges
incurred by the city for impounding and maintenance of said animal and
maintaining its own facility. Charges as established by resolution of the city
council will be paid to the Kamiah city clerk for impounding any dog. (Ord.
2020-01 §3, 2020; Ord. 98-14 §1, 1998)
6.08.180: DISPOSITION OF UNCLAIMED DOGS:
It shall be the duty of the city to keep all dogs impounded if unclaimed for a
period of one hundred twenty (120) hours. If, at the expiration of the period
from the date of notice to the owner or the first date of posting of notice,
such animal shall not have been reclaimed, it may be placed in a suitable new
home by adoption procedures or humanely euthanized by the city or the agency
chosen by it. Except in the case of vicious animals, animals not having been
reclaimed after the expiration date may be released to persons upon obtaining a
license as provided for in this chapter and payment of the fees and charges
incurred by the city for impoundment and maintenance for said animal. (Ord.
2020-01 §4, 2020; Ord. 98-14 §1, 1998)
6.08.190: RELEASE OF UNCLAIMED ANIMALS:
In the event any dog is released to any person other than the owner or lawful
custodian pursuant to and in accordance with this chapter, such person to whom
such a dog is so released shall be deemed a purchaser of such dog from the
city. Such purchaser shall receive from the city clerk a certificate of
purchase and such certificate shall be sufficient evidence of the vesting of
complete title to such animal in the purchaser, and termination of interest and
rights of the former owner in and to such animal. (Ord. 98-14 §1, 1998)
6.08.200: VICIOUS ANIMALS:
   A.   Prohibited; Violation, Penalty: It shall be unlawful for any animal to
bite or attempt to bite any person, or to harass, worry, intimidate, chase,
bite or attempt to bite any animal. It shall further be unlawful for any person
to possess, harbor, feed, keep or otherwise maintain any such animal within the
city limits. Any person violating the provisions of this section shall be
guilty of a misdemeanor and upon conviction shall be punished by a fine not in
excess of three hundred dollars ($300.00), or six (6) months in jail, or both
said fine and imprisonment. Each day a person is in violation of this section
constitutes a separate offense.
   B.   Hearing: Any person charged with a violation of subsection A of this
section, may, within seven (7) days of being charged, submit a written request
for a hearing before the city council to show cause why the provisions of
subsection A of this section should not be enforced against him or her.
      1.   Further, that if the city council finds that such animal is a
vicious animal at said hearing, the city council may, in its discretion,
authorize said animal to be destroyed by the animal control officer and/or
place any other restrictions on said animal as the city council deems
necessary. The decision of the city council shall be final.
   C.   Disposition Of Animals: Any animal impounded under the provisions of
this chapter and remaining unclaimed after notice to the owner, or an animal
whose owner is unknown, or any animal who has bitten any person and is
thereafter unclaimed, or an animal who after examination by a veterinarian is
found to have rabies or other disease rendering said animal dangerous to
persons or other animals may be destroyed at the direction of the animal
control officer.
   D.   Exceptions: Acceptable reasons for not enforcing the provisions of
subsection A of this section are limited to the following:
      1.   The animal was provoked.
      2.   The animal was defending itself. (Ord. 98-14 §1, 1998)
6.08.210: ANIMAL CARE COSTS:
All costs of maintaining any animal at a veterinary hospital shall be paid by
the owner. (Ord. 98-14 §1, 1998)
6.08.220: HUMANE TREATMENT:
No owner shall fail to provide his or her animal with adequate food and water,
proper shelter and protection from the weather, veterinary care when needed to
prevent suffering because of illness, injury or advanced age, and with humane
care and treatment. No person shall beat, cruelly ill treat, torment, mutilate,
overload, overwork or otherwise abuse any animal. No person shall cause or
permit any dogfight, cockfight or bullfight, or other combat between animals or
between animals and human beings, or train or permit to be trained, animals for
such combat, provided this shall not prevent activities such as rodeos, etc.
(Ord. 98-14 §1, 1998)
6.08.230: RABIES VACCINATION:
It shall be unlawful for the owner of any dog to keep or maintain any dog
unless the dog shall have been vaccinated by a licensed veterinarian with
antirabies vaccine within one year preceding the date of which such dog is kept
or maintained. Proof of vaccination shall be provided by the said owner within
seven (7) days of request by the city clerk or police officer. (Ord. 98-14 §1,
1998)
6.08.240: PENALTIES FOR VIOLATIONS:
Any person violating any of the provisions of this chapter, unless otherwise
specifically set forth, shall be guilty of an infraction in the amount of fifty
dollars ($50.00) for a first violation within a two (2) year period, a fine of
seventy five dollars ($75.00) for a second violation within a two (2) year
period, and a fine of one hundred dollars ($100.00) for a third violation
within a two (2) year period. (Ord. 2016-2, 2016)
6.08.250: KENNELS; NUMBER OF DOGS ALLOWED:
It is hereby declared to be a misdemeanor for any person to maintain a "kennel"
in the city as defined in section
6.08.010 of this chapter and it is further declared to be a misdemeanor for any
household to have more than three (3) adult dogs. For purposes of this section
a "household" is defined as being a person or persons who dwell together under
the same roof whether married or unmarried, and whether they consider
themselves a family or not. (Ord. 98-14 §1, 1998)
6.08.260: LIABILITY OF PARENTS:
In the event that the owner of any animal is a minor, the parent or guardian of
such minor shall be liable for all injuries, property damage, fines and
impoundment fees caused or incurred by such animals. (Ord. 98-14 §1, 1998)
6.08.270: WOLVES OR WOLF HYBRIDS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to keep or harbor a wolf or wolf hybrid
animal within the city limits. (Ord. 98-14 §1, 1998)
CHAPTER 6.12
CRUELTY TO ANIMALS 1
SECTION:
6.12.010: Unlawful

6.12.010: UNLAWFUL:
It is unlawful for any person to torture or cruelly beat, starve or otherwise
ill treat any animal in his care or charge, whether belonging to himself or any
