10.48.080: Narrow Streets; No Parking
10.48.090: One-Way Streets; Standing Or Parking On
10.48.100: One-Way Roadways; Standing Or Parking On
10.48.110: Hazardous Or Congested Places
10.48.120: Prohibited On Certain Streets; Applicability
10.48.130: Time Limit Observed
10.48.140: Parking Signs Required
10.48.150: U.S. Highway 12
10.48.160: Mobile Home, Truck And Trailer Parking
10.48.165: State Statutes; Time Limit Parking
10.48.167: Residential Parking Areas; Parking Violations
10.48.170: Violation; Penalties
 
Notes
1 1. IC §§ 49-529(a)(1), 49-758.
10.48.010: PARKING REGULATIONS:
   A.   Except as to the following streets, all parking within the city shall
be parallel parking and subject to the restrictions hereinafter set forth. The
streets where angle parking shall be allowed are as follows:
      1.   Both sides of 4th Street, between Idaho Street and Hill Street;
      2.   Both sides of 6th Street, between Idaho Street and Hill Street;
      3.   Both sides of 5th Street, between Idaho Street and Main Street;
      4.   South side of 9th Street, between Hill and Pine, in front of school;
      5.   North side of 7th between Hill and Main, Presbyterian Church and
Legion Hall;
      6.   East side of Main, one hundred feet (100') north of 10th Street,
Baptist Church;
      7.   South side of 7th from Idaho to Oak, Catholic Church;
      8.   East side of Idaho from 6th Street, south seventy five feet (75'),
Lutheran Church;
      9.   South side of 6th Street from Idaho Street to alley, north side of
Lutheran Church;
      10.   East side of Fir Street from 2nd Street, south one hundred feet
(100'), Jehovah Witness Church;
      11.   North side of 15th Street from Ash, west to city line, Assembly of
God Church;
      12.   North side from Idaho Street to Spruce Street, south side of Wa-a-
Yas building.
   B.   In any area where parallel parking is required, the vehicle shall be
parked parallel with the edge of the roadway headed in the direction of lawful
traffic movement and with the right hand wheels of the vehicle within eighteen
inches (18") of the curb or edge of the roadway, and when angle parking is
required, the right front wheel of the vehicle shall be either touching the
curb or edge of the roadway or within six inches (6") thereof.
   C.   The city reserves the right to paint on the surface of the roadway
specific parking stalls. If any vehicle using an area so painted is of a size
that will fit within one stall, parking shall be accomplished in accordance
with the markings on the road. Furthermore, the city reserves the right to
paint a line parallel to the curb or edge of the roadway, in which general
parking shall occur and if said line is painted, all parking shall be within
the designated parking area.
   D.   There shall be no parking of any vehicles at any time on the sidewalks
of this city.
   E.   Double parking shall not be allowed at any place within the city,
except by regularly authorized delivery personnel or mail personnel and only
for such time as is consumed by an actual delivery during which time the
vehicle shall remain with its motor running and with emergency flashers in
operation.
   F.   Any person violating the provisions of any part of this section shall
be cited by the city marshal's office for said parking violation. If within ten
(10) days of the delivery of that citation to the person involved, the citation
can be satisfied by paying to the city clerk a fee of ten dollars ($10.00). If,
however, more than ten (10) days expire without payment being made, then the
city marshal is authorized to write a uniform traffic citation under the
provisions of the Idaho Code, and said penalty at that time shall be treated as
an infraction. The terms of the Idaho Code concerning infractions and their
penalties for nonmoving infractions are incorporated herein. (Ord. 88-5 §2,
1988)
10.48.020: PERMIT FOR LOADING OR UNLOADING:
   A.   The traffic engineer is authorized to issue special permits to permit
the backing of a vehicle to the curb for the purpose of loading or unloading
merchandise or materials subject to the terms and conditions of such permit.
Such permits may be issued either to the owner or lessee of real property or to
the owner of the vehicle and shall grant to such person the privilege as
therein stated and authorized herein.
   B.   It is unlawful for any permittee or other person to violate any of the
special terms or conditions of any such permit. (Prior code §10-212(2))
10.48.030: OBSTRUCTING TRAFFIC WHEN PARKING:
No person shall park any vehicle upon a street, other than an alley, in such a
manner or under such conditions as to leave available less than ten feet (10')
of the width of the roadway for free movement of vehicular traffic. (Prior code
§10-213(2))
10.48.040: ALLEYS; PARKING IN:
No person shall park a vehicle within an alley in such a manner or under such
conditions as to leave available less than ten feet (10') of the width of the
roadway for the free movement of vehicular traffic, and no person shall stop,
stand or park a vehicle within an alley, in such position as to block the
driveway entrance to any abutting property. (Prior code §10-213(3))
10.48.050: ALL NIGHT PARKING:
No person shall park a vehicle on any street for a period of time longer than
thirty (30) minutes between the hours of two o'clock (2:00) A.M. and five
o'clock (5:00) A.M. of any day, except physicians on emergency calls. (Prior
code §10-213(4))
10.48.060: PROHIBITED PARKING:
No person shall park a vehicle upon any roadway for the principal purpose of:
   A.   Displaying such vehicle for sale;
   B.   Washing, greasing, or repairing such vehicle except repairs
necessitated by an emergency. (Prior code §10-213(5))
10.48.070: SCHOOLS; NO PARKING AREAS:
   A.   The traffic engineer is authorized to erect signs indicating no parking
upon either or both sides of any street adjacent to any school property when
such parking would, in his opinion, interfere with traffic or create a
hazardous situation.
   B.   When official signs are erected indicating no parking upon either side
of a street adjacent to any school property as authorized in subsection A of
this section, no person shall park a vehicle in any such designated place.
(Prior code §10-213(6))
10.48.080: NARROW STREETS; NO PARKING:
   A.   The traffic engineer is authorized to erect signs indicating no parking
upon any street when the width of the roadway does not exceed twenty feet (20')
or upon one side of a street as indicated by such signs when the width of the
roadway does not exceed thirty feet (30').
   B.   When official signs prohibiting parking are erected upon narrow streets
as authorized in subsection A of this section, no person shall park a vehicle
upon any such street in violation of any such sign. (Prior code §10-213(7))
10.48.090: ONE-WAY STREETS; STANDING OR PARKING ON:
The traffic engineer is authorized to erect signs upon the left hand side of
any one-way street to prohibit the standing or parking of vehicles, and, when
such signs are in place, no person shall stand or park a vehicle upon such left
hand side in violation of any such sign. (Prior code §10-213(8))
10.48.100: ONE-WAY ROADWAYS; STANDING OR PARKING ON:
In the event a highway includes two (2) or more separate roadways and traffic
is restricted to one direction upon any such roadway, no person shall stand or
park a vehicle upon the left hand side of such one-way roadway unless signs are
erected to permit such standing or parking. The traffic engineer is authorized
to determine when standing or parking may be permitted upon the left hand side
of any such one-way roadway and to erect signs giving notice thereof. (Prior
code §10-213(9))
10.48.110: HAZARDOUS OR CONGESTED PLACES:
   A.   The traffic engineer is authorized to determine and designate, by
proper signs, places not exceeding one hundred feet (100') in length in which
the stopping, standing or parking of vehicles would create an especially
hazardous condition or would cause unusual delay to traffic.
   B.   When official signs are erected at hazardous or congested places as
authorized in subsection A of this section, no person shall stop, stand or park
a vehicle in any such designated place. (Prior code §10-213(10))
10.48.120: PROHIBITED ON CERTAIN STREETS; APPLICABILITY:
The provisions of this section through section
10.48.140 of this chapter, prohibiting the standing or parking of a vehicle,
shall apply at all times as may be hereafter adopted by the city council by
appropriate ordinance, as are then thereafter indicated on official signs,
except when it is necessary to stop a vehicle to avoid conflict with other
traffic or in compliance with the direction of a police officer or other
official traffic control device then lawfully in existence. (Ord. 3-78 §1,
1978: prior code §10-215(1))
10.48.130: TIME LIMIT OBSERVED:
The provisions of this section and sections
10.48.120 and 10.48.140 of this chapter, imposing a time limit on parking,
shall not relieve any person from the duty to observe other and more
restrictive provisions prohibiting or limiting the stopping, standing, or
parking of vehicles in specified places or at specified times. (Prior code §10-
215(2))
10.48.140: PARKING SIGNS REQUIRED:
Whenever by this chapter any parking time limit is imposed or parking
prohibited on designated streets, it shall be the duty of the traffic engineer
to erect appropriate signs giving notice thereof, and no such regulations shall
be effective unless the signs are erected and in place at the time of any
alleged offense. (Prior code §10-215(3))
10.48.150: U.S. HIGHWAY 12:
   A.   It is unlawful for any person to park or leave standing any motor
vehicle along U.S. Highway 12 as it passes through the incorporated limits of
the city of Kamiah between the following areas: East from the Maple Street
intersection with U.S. Highway 12 to a point two hundred feet (200') east of
the intersection of Idaho Street and U.S. Highway 12; and that area between the
west end of the Clearwater Bridge and the Camas Prairie Railroad right of way.
   B.   Prior to enforcing the terms of this section, the Kamiah city marshal
or his designee shall post signs along U.S. Highway 12 in the prohibited area
saying the following: "No Parking on Highway Right of Way". After the signs
hereunder contemplated are in place, any person violating the terms of this
section shall pay a parking assessment to the city of Kamiah in the amount of
ten dollars ($10.00) for each parking violation within ten (10) days of the
delivery of a citation to the person so parking on the highway right of way. If
the fee prescribed in this subsection is not paid within the ten (10) day
period of time, then the parking violation shall be considered an infraction
pursuant to the definitions in the Idaho Code and processed as an infraction
with the penalty being as prescribed by the Idaho legislature in the title 49,
Idaho Code.
   C.   In interpreting this section the prohibition is intended to eliminate
congested parking on the highway right of way belonging to the state of Idaho
on and along the actual roadbed of U.S. Highway 12 in the prohibited areas;
however, parking shall still be permitted on private property adjacent to the
highway right of way. (Ord. 88-9 §§2, 3, 1988)
10.48.160: MOBILE HOME, TRUCK AND TRAILER PARKING:
   A.   It is unlawful for any person to stop, stand, or park a nonmotorized
towed trailer, whether it be mobile home, camp trailer, storage trailer,
utility trailer or similar trailer on the city streets of the city of Kamiah
for more than seventy two (72) hours at any one location.
   B.   Any person so parking or so locating any such trailer on a continuous
basis for longer than seventy two (72) hours shall be entitled to one warning
about such parking from the marshal's office or any private citizen prior to
being deemed in violation hereof. If after such warning the vehicle is not
removed from the street within an additional twenty four (24) hours, the person
parking such trailer in that location who has received such previous warning
shall be guilty of a violation of this section.
   C.   Any person who violates this section shall be punished in accordance
with the general parking penalties adopted pursuant to this chapter.
   D.   All persons shall be entitled to apply to the marshal's office for a
temporary permit to allow on street parking of such trailers on a temporary
basis. Such permit shall be issued by the city marshal or his staff in written
form for not to exceed twenty one (21) days for each permit. Renewals shall be
granted only for good cause shown.
   E.   On street parking of semitrucks, semitrailers or logging trucks and/or
trailers for longer than forty eight (48) hours at any one time anywhere within
the city is specifically prohibited and shall be a further violation hereof.
(Ord. 88-3 §1, 1988)
10.48.165: STATE STATUTES; TIME LIMIT PARKING:
   A.   Incorporation Of State Statutes: All state statutes regarding motor
vehicle parking, standing or stopping regulations are incorporated herein.
   B.   Three Hour Parking Areas: The following streets of the city are
designated as three (3) hour parking areas, between the hours of nine o'clock
(9:00) A.M. and five o'clock (5:00) P.M. Monday through Saturday:
      1.   Main Street from Highway 12 to 6th Street on both sides of Main
Street.
      2.   4th Street from Idaho Street to Hill Street on both sides of 4th
Street, except that the provisions of this section shall not apply to the
parking space located as follows: The parking space located on the north side
of 4th Street immediately west of the alleyway running between 4th Street and
U.S. Highway 12.
      3.   5th Street from the alleyway between Idaho Street and Main Street to
the alleyway between Main Street and Hill Street, on both sides of 5th Street,
except that the provisions of this section shall not apply to the parking space
located as follows: The parking space located on the south side of 5th Street
and immediately east of the alleyway running between 5th Street and 6th Street.
(Ord. 98-10 §§1, 2, 1998: Ord. 97-9 §§1, 2, 4, 1997)
10.48.167: RESIDENTIAL PARKING AREAS; PARKING VIOLATIONS:
   A.   Findings: Certain residential areas of Kamiah are being bombarded with
a heavy concentration of vehicles which remain parked throughout the day and
that a substantial portion of these vehicles are not owned or operated by
residents of these areas; that the presence of these vehicles causes vehicular
congestion on residential streets, impedes movement of traffic and unduly
restricts the entry of residents to their homes; that such vehicular congestion
creates polluted air, excessive noise, trash and refuse and causes the
deterioration of residential areas.
   B.   Prohibited Acts: It shall be unlawful for any person to wilfully cause
or permit any vehicle to be parked upon the following streets, unless expressly
permitted herein:
      1.   Streets with parking restrictions shall include the following:
         a.   The north side of Ninth Street from the intersection at Main
Street and Ninth Street to Pine Street and Ninth Street;
         b.   Both sides of Maple Street from the intersection of Ninth Street
and Maple Street to the intersection of Eighth Street and Maple Street;
         c.   The east side of Hill Street where Ninth Street intersects with
Hill Street to the intersection of Hill Street and Twelfth Street.
Parking on the streets and areas designated in subsections B1a through B1c of
this section shall be for residents only from eight o'clock (8:00) A.M. until
four o'clock (4:00) P.M. Monday through Friday from August 15 through June 15
of each calendar year.
         d.   The west side of Hill Street where Ninth Street intersects with
Hill Street and Twelfth Street.
Parking on the streets and area named in subsection B1d of this section shall
be for a maximum time of forty five (45) minutes from eight o'clock (8:00) A.M.
until four o'clock (4:00) P.M. Monday through Friday.
   C.   Signage: The chief of police is hereby authorized to erect signs
indicating the area is a no parking area from seven thirty o'clock (7:30) A.M.
to four o'clock (4:00) P.M., is for residential parking only and a tow away
zone when such parking would, in his opinion, interfere with traffic or create
a hazardous situation.
   D.   Cost Of Removal Responsibility Of Owner: Any vehicle parked in
violation of traffic regulations or any vehicle parked so as to obstruct the
free movement of traffic or to cause a traffic hazard may be immediately cited
for parking in a restricted area/tow away zone. Should the owner of a vehicle
which is either parked in violation of traffic regulations or obstructing the
free movement of traffic or causing a traffic hazard, receive a citation for
parking in the restricted area/tow away zone and should said owner fail to pay
the citation and/or fail to remove said vehicle from the restricted area/tow
away zone said vehicle shall be removed upon order of the police department.
Any such vehicle removed by the police department shall be kept under the
control of the police department until the owner or authorized agent pays a
reasonable cost for removal and storage in addition to the penalty provided for
such improper parking. Any such vehicle shall be deemed to be improperly parked
after a period of three (3) minutes. If said vehicle is not redeemed within
seven (7) days following the posting of notice to the owner by mail, the costs
of redemption shall include the actual cost and expense of said removal,
storage and penalty(ies) and said costs and expenses shall be a lien in favor
of the city.
   E.   Notice Of Removal To Owner: Whenever the chief of police removes a
vehicle from a street as authorized and he knows or is able to ascertain from
the registration records of the department of motor vehicles the name and the
address of the owner thereof, the chief of police immediately shall notify in
writing such owner of the fact of such removal, the grounds thereof and the
place to which such vehicle has been removed. In the event such vehicle is
stored in a public garage, he shall deliver a copy of such notice to the
proprietor of the garage.
   F.   Enforcement: It shall be the duty of the officers of the police
department or such officers as are assigned by the chief of police to enforce
all street traffic laws of the state and city. When official signs are erected
indicating no parking as authorized herein, it shall be unlawful for any person
to park a vehicle in any such designated street in violation of any such sign.
   G.   Penalties: The owner and operator of any vehicle or other contrivance
over or upon any street, avenue or alleyway within the city, in violation of
any of the terms or conditions hereof, shall be guilty of an infraction. (Ord.
2007-2 §1, 2007)
10.48.170: VIOLATION; PENALTIES:
   A.   Any provision of this chapter that does not contain a specific parking
penalty shall be subject to the penalties expressed herein. Any person
violating any of the parking rules in this title and chapter shall be given a
citation on a form to be approved by motion of the city council, directing that
a fee of ten dollars ($10.00) be paid to the city clerk within ten (10) days of
the delivery of the citation to said person. In the event said fee is not paid
within the ten (10) days, then the city's enforcement officer shall be
authorized to issue a uniform traffic citation to the person, alleging a
parking violation which shall then be an infraction as that term is known and
understood pursuant to the Idaho Code and shall be treated in court as a
nonmoving infraction.
   B.   The terms of the Idaho Code concerning infraction trials, burdens of
proof, and penalties are incorporated herein as from time to time are adopted
by the Idaho state legislature. (Ord. 88-4 §1, 1988)
CHAPTER 10.52
LOADING ZONES
SECTION:
10.52.010: Designation
10.52.020: Permits
10.52.030: Passengers
10.52.040: Freight
10.52.050: Public Carrier Stops And Stands; Designation
10.52.060: Buses; Regulations
10.52.070: Bus Stand Restrictions
10.52.010: DESIGNATION:
The traffic engineer is authorized to determine the location of passengers and
freight curb loading zones and shall place and maintain appropriate signs
indicating the same and stating the hours during which the provisions of this
chapter are applicable. (Prior code §10-214(1))
10.52.020: PERMITS:
The traffic engineer shall not hereafter designate or sign any curb loading
zones upon special request of any person unless such person makes application
for a permit for such zone and for two (2) signs to indicate the ends of each
such zone. The traffic engineer upon granting a permit and issuing such signs
shall collect from the applicant and deposit in the treasury a service fee of
five dollars ($5.00) per year or fraction thereof and may by general
regulations impose conditions upon the use of such signs and for reimbursement
of the municipality for the value thereof in the event of their loss or damage
and their return in the event of misuse or upon the expiration of permit. Every
such permit shall expire at the end of one year. (Prior code §10-214(2))
10.52.030: PASSENGERS:
No person shall stop, stand, or park a vehicle for any purpose or period of
time other than for the expeditious loading or unloading of passengers in any
place marked as a passenger curb loading zone during hours when the regulations
applicable to such curb loading zone are effective, and then only for a period
not to exceed three (3) minutes. (Prior code §10-214(3))
10.52.040: FREIGHT:
No person shall stop, stand or park a vehicle for any purpose or length of time
other than for the expeditious unloading and delivery or pick up and loading of
materials in any place marked as a freight curb loading zone during hours when
the provisions applicable to such zones are in effect. In no case shall the
stop for loading and unloading of materials exceed thirty (30) minutes. (Prior
code §10-214(4))
10.52.050: PUBLIC CARRIER STOPS AND STANDS; DESIGNATION:
The traffic engineer is authorized and required to establish bus stops, bus
stands, taxicab stands and stands for other passenger common carrier motor
vehicles on such public streets in such places and in such numbers as he shall
determine to be of the greatest benefit and convenience to the public, and
every such bus stop, bus stand, taxicab stand, or other stand shall be
designated by appropriate signs. (Prior code §10-214(5))
10.52.060: BUSES; REGULATIONS:
   A.   The operator of a bus shall not stand or park such vehicle upon any
street at any place other than at a bus stand so designated.
   B.   The operator of a bus shall not stop such vehicle upon any street at
any place for the purpose of loading or unloading passengers or their baggage
other than at a bus stop, bus stand, or passenger loading zone so designated,
except in case of an emergency.
   C.   The operator of a bus shall enter a bus stop, bus stand or passenger
loading zone on a public street in such a manner that the bus when stopped to
load or unload passengers or baggage shall be in a position with the right
front wheel of such vehicle not farther than eighteen inches (18") from the
curb and the bus approximately parallel to the curb, so as not to unduly impede
the movement of other vehicular traffic. (Prior code §10-214(6))
10.52.070: BUS STAND RESTRICTIONS:
No person shall stop, stand, or park a vehicle other than a bus in a bus stop,
except that the driver of a passenger vehicle may temporarily stop therein for
the purpose of and while actually engaged in loading or unloading passengers
when such stopping does not interfere with any bus waiting to enter or about to
enter such zone. (Prior code §10-214(7))
CHAPTER 10.56
REMOVAL AND IMPOUNDMENT OF VEHICLES
SECTION:
10.56.010: Definitions
10.56.020: Removal Of Parked Cars By Police; Cost
10.56.030: Wrecked Or Abandoned Motor Vehicles
10.56.040: Personal Property Unredeemed
10.56.050: Proof Of Ownership
10.56.060: Sale Of Impounded Properties
10.56.010: DEFINITIONS:
ABANDONED MOTOR VEHICLE OR OTHER PERSONAL PROPERTY: An automobile or personal
property which remains upon the streets or other public property for a period
longer than forty eight (48) hours, the owner of which cannot be located or the
owner refuses to remove the same.
STOLEN MOTOR VEHICLE OR OTHER PERSONAL PROPERTY: That property which the police
department has reasonable grounds to believe to be stolen.
UNIDENTIFIED MOTOR VEHICLE OR OTHER PERSONAL PROPERTY: As used in this title,
is identified to be such motor vehicle or other personal property where
ownership thereof cannot be ascertained.
WRECKED MOTOR VEHICLE OR OTHER PERSONAL PROPERTY: One damaged by accident or
any cause, and left upon the streets or public place unattended. (Prior code
§220)
10.56.020: REMOVAL OF PARKED CARS BY POLICE; COST:
If at any time a vehicle is parked in a prohibited place or at a time when
parking is prohibited where parked, for a period of ten (10) minutes or more,
and such vehicle is obstructing the free movement of traffic or is causing a
traffic hazard, or is directly interfering with the maintenance or care, or
emergency use of the streets, and the person in charge cannot be immediately
located, or if located, fails, neglects, or refuses to move said vehicle at
once, or where a motor vehicle is parked in a parking meter area and is in
violation as set forth in this chapter, for a period of one hour, the police
department may in its discretion, in addition to the penalty provided therefor,
remove or cause to be removed the vehicle keeping it in its custody or under
its control at such place as may be designated by the police department until
the owner or his authorized agent applies for same and has paid a reasonable
cost for removing and storing the vehicle which costs shall be assessed and
collected by the police department, and the costs and expenses shall be a lien
in favor of the municipality on the car; provided, that when any such motor
vehicle is interfering with the maintenance or emergency use of the streets,
but not otherwise violating this title, then the police department may, in its
own discretion, remove the motor vehicle or other vehicle and care for the
same, and may in its own discretion deliver the same to the owner without any
cost or charge for such removal or storage. (Prior code §10-219)
10.56.030: WRECKED OR ABANDONED MOTOR VEHICLES:
   A.   The marshal's office is authorized in its discretion, in addition to
any penalty that may be provided therefor, to remove an unidentified, stolen,
wrecked or abandoned motor vehicle or other personal property, as defined in
section
10.56.010 of this chapter, found upon any public street or public property and
shall keep the same in its custody and control at such place as may be
designated by the marshal's office until redeemed by the owner thereof as
herein provided; and all such unidentified, stolen, wrecked or abandoned motor
vehicles or other personal property which is now in its possession shall be
subject to the actual cost of removal or tow in from the public place, and a
storage charge of twenty five dollars ($25.00) per day as long as the same is
in possession and custody of said office.
   B.   It is unlawful for any owner or any person in charge of a motor vehicle
or other personal property to leave or abandon the same upon the streets or
public places as provided in this chapter. (Ord. 2002-6 §2, 2002: prior code
§10-220)
10.56.040: PERSONAL PROPERTY UNREDEEMED:
All motor vehicles and other personal property impounded or heretofore
impounded by the police department and unredeemed by the owner thereof for a
period of forty five (45) days shall thereafter be subject to sale by the chief
of police to the highest bidder for cash as hereinafter provided, and the
proceeds of the sale shall be applied first to all removal and storage charges
accumulated against each article, which shall be deposited with the treasurer
and the balance of the sum, if any, shall be deposited with the treasurer and
shall be kept in a separate fund for a period of one year from the date of
receipt, and if at the end of the year the former owner of the property has not
made satisfactory proof of claim as provided in section
10.56.050 of this chapter, then the balance of the proceeds of sale shall be
credited to the general fund. (Prior code §10-221)
10.56.050: PROOF OF OWNERSHIP:
   A.   Any person claiming to be the owner of any impounded property as
provided in this chapter, shall make written application therefor to the police
department and shall furnish to the department such additional proof as may be
required to establish the ownership. If he presents to said department proof of
his ownership of the impounded property prior to the date of actual sale
thereof pursuant to the provisions of this chapter, then the property itself
shall be delivered to the owner under the conditions provided in this chapter;
but if the property has been sold, then the department shall endorse its
findings of ownership with a copy of the written application addressed to the
clerk, and the owner may present the application and findings to the clerk, and
if presented within one year after the sale, then such balance of the proceeds
of sale, after deductions as provided in this chapter, shall be paid to the
owner.
   B.   Any appeal from the removal, storage and publication costs, if any,
assessed by the police department as provided in this chapter shall be in the
same manner as provided by law. (Prior code §10-222)
10.56.060: SALE OF IMPOUNDED PROPERTIES:
Whenever the chief of police shall in his discretion decide to offer impounded
properties for sale, he shall make a complete and detailed list of such
properties to be included in a publication notice of the sale. The notice of
publication of sale shall be published at least three (3) times in a newspaper
of general circulation, the publication to be at least five (5) days before the
sale. The bids, when received, shall be accepted or rejected as to each
separate item of property, and only cash bids shall be acceptable to the chief
of police. (Prior code §10-223)
CHAPTER 10.60
VEHICLES; LOAD AND USE LIMITS 1
SECTION:
10.60.010: Weight Restriction
10.60.020: Streets Where Certain Vehicles Prohibited
10.60.030: Wheels Injurious To Pavement
 
Notes
1 1. IC §§ 49-906, 49-720.
10.60.010: WEIGHT RESTRICTION:
When signs are erected giving notice thereof, no person shall operate any
vehicle with a gross weight in excess of the amounts specified. (Prior code
§10-216(1))
10.60.020: STREETS WHERE CERTAIN VEHICLES PROHIBITED:
   A.   The traffic engineer is authorized to determine and designate those
heavily traveled streets, upon which shall be prohibited the use of the roadway
by motor driven cycles, bicycles, horsedrawn vehicles, or other nonmotorized
traffic and shall erect appropriate signs giving notice thereof.
   B.   When signs are so erected giving notice thereof, no person shall
disobey the restrictions stated on such signs. (Prior code §10-216(2))
10.60.030: WHEELS INJURIOUS TO PAVEMENT 2 :
It is unlawful for any person to drive any vehicle with projecting metallic
lugs, points, cleats or bars on the wheels, tracks or treads, across, over or
upon any paved or oiled street or any bridge crossing or culvert in the city of
Kamiah without using on the street, bridge crossing or culvert for the purpose
of securing its safety, four (4) pieces of plank each of which shall be at
least ten feet (10') in length, twelve inches (12") in width and two inches
(2") in thickness, two (2) of which pieces of plank shall at all times be under
the wheels, tracks or treads of such vehicles. (Ord. 4 §7, 1957: prior code
§10-227)
 
Notes
2 2. See also section
  12.08.010 of this code.
CHAPTER 10.64
RAILROADS 1
SECTION:
10.64.010: Blocking Streets
 
Notes
1 1. IC § 50-306.
10.64.010: BLOCKING STREETS:
It is unlawful for the directing officer or the operator of any railroad train
to direct the operation of or to operate the same in such manner as to prevent
the use of any street for purposes of travel for a period of time longer than
ten (10) minutes, except that this provision shall not apply to trains or cars
in motion other than those engaged in switching. (Prior code §10-210(3)(a))
CHAPTER 10.68
EMERGENCY VEHICLES 1
SECTION:
10.68.010: Driver Privileges
10.68.020: Permitted Acts Of Driver
10.68.030: Responsibility Of Driver
10.68.040: Safety Of All Persons
 
Notes
1 1. IC §§ 49-526, 49-731, 49-731A.
10.68.010: DRIVER PRIVILEGES:
The driver of an authorized emergency vehicle, when responding to an emergency
call or when in the pursuit of an actual suspected violator of the law or when
responding to but not upon returning from a fire alarm, may exercise the
privileges set forth in this chapter, but subject to the conditions stated in
this chapter. (Prior code §10-203(7)(a))
10.68.020: PERMITTED ACTS OF DRIVER:
The driver of an authorized emergency vehicle may:
   A.   Park or stand, irrespective of the provisions of this chapter;
   B.   Proceed past a red or stop signal or stop sign, but only after slowing
down as may be necessary for safe operation;
   C.   Exceed the prima facie speed limits so long as he does not endanger
life or property;
   D.   Disregard regulations governing direction of movement or turning in
specified directions. (Prior code §10-203(7)(b))
10.68.030: RESPONSIBILITY OF DRIVER:
The exemptions granted in this chapter to an authorized emergency vehicle shall
apply only when the driver of any vehicle while in motion sounds audible signal
by bell, siren, or exhaust whistle as may be reasonably necessary, and when the
vehicle is equipped with at least one lighted lamp displaying a red light
visible under normal atmospheric conditions from a distance of five hundred
feet (500') to the front of such vehicle, except that an authorized emergency
vehicle operated as a police vehicle need not be equipped with or display a red
light visible from in front of the vehicle. (Prior code §10-203(7)(c))
10.68.040: SAFETY OF ALL PERSONS:
The provisions of this chapter shall not relieve the driver of an authorized
emergency vehicle from the duty to drive with due regard for the safety of all
persons, nor shall such provisions protect the driver from the consequences of
his reckless disregard for the safety of others. (Prior code §10-203(7)(d))
CHAPTER 10.69
SNOWMOBILES
SECTION:
10.69.010: Purpose
10.69.020: Defined
10.69.030: Operation
10.69.040: Hours Of Operation
10.69.050: Motor Vehicle License Required
10.69.060: Offenses By Persons Owning Snowmobiles
10.69.070: Required Equipment
10.69.080: Driving Regulations
10.69.090: Violation; Penalty
10.69.010: PURPOSE:
The purpose of this chapter is to regulate the operation of snowmobiles within
the city limits. (Ord. 10-79 §1, 1979)
10.69.020: DEFINED:
The term "snowmobile" means every self-propelled device upon a combination of
skis, skids, tracks or endless belts, in and upon or by which any person or
property is or may be transported or drawn upon snow or snow covered surface
areas, and expressly includes devices known as "snowmobiles" or "skimobiles".
(Ord. 10-79 §2, 1979)
10.69.030: OPERATION:
It is lawful to operate a snowmobile upon all the city streets of the city of
Kamiah upon the condition and subject to the restrictions set forth in this
chapter. (Ord. 10-79 §3, 1979)
10.69.040: HOURS OF OPERATION:
It shall be unlawful for any person to operate a snowmobile within the city
limits between the hours of ten o'clock (10:00) P.M. and ten o'clock (10:00)
A.M. of the following day. Special permission may be granted by the mayor for
any late hour group performance activity, upon request from an officer of the
group concerned. (Ord. 10-79 §4, 1979)
10.69.050: MOTOR VEHICLE LICENSE REQUIRED:
No person who does not hold a valid motor vehicle operator's license shall
drive or operate a snowmobile in the city. (Ord. 10-79 §5, 1979)
10.69.060: OFFENSES BY PERSONS OWNING SNOWMOBILES:
It is unlawful for any person to knowingly permit, allow or encourage the
operation or driving of a snowmobile by a person who does not hold a valid
motor vehicle operator's license. (Ord. 10-79 §6, 1979)
10.69.070: REQUIRED EQUIPMENT:
No snowmobile shall be operated in the city unless it is equipped with the
following:
   A.   At least one and not more than two (2) headlamps sufficient to render
clearly discernible, persons and vehicles at a distance of two hundred fifty
feet (250') ahead;
   B.   Taillamps, which when lighted emit a red light plainly visible at a
distance of two hundred fifty feet (250') to the rear;
   C.   At least one brake which may be operated by hand or foot;
   D.   A muffler in good working order and in constant operation to prevent
excessive or unusual noise and annoying smoke, and no person shall use a
muffler cutout, bypass, or similar device. (Ord. 10-79 §7, 1979)
10.69.080: DRIVING REGULATIONS:
Regulations for operation of snowmobiles are as follows:
   A.   It is unlawful to drive, operate or park a snowmobile on any sidewalk
in the city;
   B.   No snowmobile shall be operated at a speed in excess of fifteen (15)
miles per hour in the city;
   C.   No snowmobile shall carry passengers or weights in excess of the
capacity recommended by the manufacturer thereof;
   D.   No sled, toboggan, trailer or any other device shall be towed by a
snowmobile except by means of a rigid tow bar connecting the same to such
device;
   E.   No person on skis shall be towed behind a snowmobile;
   F.   It shall be unlawful to drive or operate a snowmobile while under the
influence of intoxicating liquor;
   G.   All snowmobiles shall be operated in single file on the extreme right
hand side of the street;
   H.   No person shall operate a snowmobile carelessly and heedlessly, or
without due caution and circumspection and at a speed or in a manner as to
endanger or be likely to endanger any person or property. (Ord. 3-84 §1, 1983:
Ord. 10-79 §8, 1979)
10.69.090: VIOLATION; PENALTY:
Any person convicted of a violation of this chapter shall be punished by a fine
not to exceed three hundred dollars ($300.00) or imprisonment in the city or
county jail not more than thirty (30) days or by both such fine and
imprisonment. (Ord. 10-79 §9, 1979)
CHAPTER 10.72
BICYCLES AND SKATEBOARDS
SECTION:
10.72.010: Effective Regulations
10.72.020: Duties And Responsibilities
10.72.030: Parking
10.72.040: Riding Bicycles And Operating Skateboards On Sidewalks
10.72.050: Juveniles; Violations
10.72.060: Equipment Required
10.72.010: EFFECTIVE REGULATIONS:
   A.   It is unlawful and a misdemeanor for any person to do any act forbidden
or fail to perform any act required under this chapter.
   B.   The parent of any child and the guardian of any ward shall not
authorize or knowingly permit a child or ward to violate the provisions of this
chapter.
   C.   The following regulations applicable to bicycles shall apply wherever a
bicycle is operated upon any public thoroughfare or public path set aside
exclusively for the use of bicycles. (Ord. 4-84 §1, 1984)
10.72.020: DUTIES AND RESPONSIBILITIES:
Every person riding a bicycle shall be granted all of the rights and shall be
subject to all of the duties applicable to the driver of a motor vehicle except
as to those provisions of law which by their nature can have no application.
(Ord. 4-84 §2, 1984)
10.72.030: PARKING:
It is unlawful for any person to park a bicycle in such a manner as to
interfere with or obstruct pedestrian traffic. (Ord. 4-84 §3, 1984)
10.72.040: RIDING BICYCLES AND OPERATING SKATEBOARDS ON SIDEWALKS:
It is unlawful for any person to ride a bicycle or operate a skateboard on any
sidewalk within the "business district" of the city of Kamiah as that term is
defined in section
10.04.010 of this title. Before this provision shall become enforceable, the
city shall post at conspicuous places within the business district signs
indicating that bicycles and skateboards shall not be operated on any sidewalk.
Furthermore, before any person shall be prosecuted for a violation of this
chapter, said person shall be entitled to one warning from the police authority
or other authorities of the city of Kamiah. Records of all warnings shall be
kept by the city clerk or the city marshal's office for further reference. If
any person violates the provisions of this section after receiving a warning as
is hereinabove set forth, such person shall be deemed to have committed an
infraction of the law and shall be prosecuted accordingly. (Ord. 88-7 §2, 1988:
Ord. 4-84 §4, 1984)
10.72.050: JUVENILES; VIOLATIONS:
Any juvenile violating this chapter shall be processed pursuant to the youth
rehabilitation act of the state of Idaho for the violation. (Ord. 4-84 §5,
1984)
10.72.060: EQUIPMENT REQUIRED:
   A.   Every bicycle when in use at nighttime shall be equipped with a lamp on
the front which shall emit a white light visible from a distance of at least
five hundred feet (500') to the front, and a red reflector on the rear of a
type which shall be visible from all distances from fifty feet (50') to three
hundred feet (300') to the rear when directly in front of lawful upper beams of
headlamps of a motor vehicle. A lamp emitting a red light visible from a
distance of two hundred fifty feet (250') to the rear may be used in addition
to the red reflector.
   B.   Every bicycle shall be equipped with a brake which shall enable the
operator to make the braked wheel skid on dry, level, clean pavement. (Ord. 88-
6 §1, 1988: Ord. 4-84 §6, 1984)
CHAPTER 10.76
COMPRESSION BRAKES
SECTION:
10.76.010: Use Prohibited
10.76.020: Posting
10.76.030: Violations; Penalty
10.76.010: USE PROHIBITED:
No person operating a motor vehicle, including a motorcycle, within the
incorporated limits of the city of Kamiah, which vehicle is equipped with a
compression brake, shall use that brake within the city at any time. (Ord.
2016-4, 2016)
10.76.020: POSTING:
Prior to enforcing the provisions of this chapter, the city marshal of the city
of Kamiah shall post an appropriate sign prohibiting the use of compression
brakes at the existing five (5) entrances to the city of Kamiah and then file
with the city clerk an affidavit that he has properly erected said warning
signs at the entrances. (Ord. 2016-4, 2016)
10.76.030: VIOLATIONS; PENALTY:
After the compression brake prohibition signs have been erected by the city
marshal or his designee, any person who violates the provisions of this chapter
shall be considered guilty of an infraction and shall be punishable by a fine
of fifty dollars ($50.00). (Ord. 2016-4, 2016)

CHAPTER 12.12
TREES, HEDGES AND SHRUBBERY
SECTION:
12.12.010: Tree Trimming Required
12.12.020: Hedges And Shrubbery Maintained
12.12.030: Trees Outside Property Line
12.12.040: Injury To Trees And Shrubbery
12.12.010: TREE TRIMMING REQUIRED:
Any owner or occupant of any real property shall trim all trees on property
owned or occupied by him overhanging any public thoroughfare so that branches
thereon will not interfere with pedestrians or public travel. Particular
attention shall be given to intersections so that there is a clear visibility
at the intersection unimpeded by branches. (Ord. 1-85 §1, 1985)
12.12.020: HEDGES AND SHRUBBERY MAINTAINED:
Any owner or occupant of any real property shall maintain all hedges and
shrubbery adjacent to public sidewalks so that no part of said hedges and/or
shrubbery shall extend over any part of a public sidewalk in the
municipalities. (Ord. 1-85 §2, 1985)
12.12.030: TREES OUTSIDE PROPERTY LINE:
   A.   The governing body of the municipality is provided full and complete
authority over all trees that are outside the property lines of privately owned
real property. Should the property owner adjacent to any trees desire to
exercise concurrent control over such trees they should be trimmed in
accordance with section
12.12.010 of this chapter or the trees will be subject to removal by the city.
   B.   The city shall reserve the right to agree with any property owner in
relation to the maintenance of any trees outside the property line so that the
concurrent control of the tree may be exercised by the property owner and will
be, by the city, required to be trimmed. (Ord. 1-85 §3, 1985)
12.12.040: INJURY TO TREES AND SHRUBBERY:
It is declared unlawful for any person, not the owner thereof, or without the
lawful authority to do so, to wilfully injure, deface, disfigure or destroy any
tree or shrub, or to injure, destroy, cut or pick any flower or plant located
either on private ground or on any public place or thoroughfare. (Ord. 1-85 §4,
1985)
CHAPTER 12.14
PUBLIC TREES
SECTION:
12.14.010: Title
12.14.020: Purpose
12.14.030: Definitions
12.14.040: Creation And Establishment Of Urban Forestry Committee
12.14.050: Permits; Maintenance And Removal Of Trees
12.14.060: Other Provisions
12.14.070: Penalties
12.14.010: TITLE:
This chapter shall be known as the KAMIAH TREE ORDINANCE. (Ord. 2008-1 §1,
2007)
12.14.020: PURPOSE:
The purpose of this chapter is to establish and maintain an optimum amount,
species variety, and age diversity of tree cover on public property in the
city, and to maintain city trees in a healthy and minimally hazardous condition
through good arboricultural practices. (Ord. 2008-1 §1, 2007)
12.14.030: DEFINITIONS:
ADMINISTRATOR: A city council member, as appointed and overseen by the mayor,
who is to carry out the terms of this chapter.
PRIVATE TREE: Any tree, shrub or other woody vegetation on private property.
PUBLIC PROPERTY: Property owned by the city of Kamiah either in fee simple
absolute, or implied or expressly dedicated to the public for present or future
use, for purposes of vehicular or pedestrian traffic, or for public easements.
PUBLIC TREE: Any tree, shrub or other woody vegetation on public property.
SHRUB: A multiple stemmed, woody plant whose height at maturity is between
three feet (3') and fifteen feet (15').
TOPPING: The practice of cutting back large diameter branches of a mature tree
to stubs.
TREE: A woody perennial plant with one main stem or trunk. (Ord. 2008-1 §1,
2007)
12.14.040: CREATION AND ESTABLISHMENT OF URBAN FORESTRY COMMITTEE:
There is hereby created and established an urban forestry committee for the
city of Kamiah, which shall consist of five (5) members, citizens and residents
of this community, who shall be appointed by the mayor with the approval of the
city council. The tree administrator will also serve as a member of the urban
forestry committee.
   A.   Term Of Office: The term of the five (5) persons to be appointed by the
mayor shall be six (6) years. In the event that a vacancy shall occur during
the term of any member, his successor shall be appointed for the unexpired
portion of the term.
   B.   Compensation: Members of the board shall serve without compensation.
   C.   Duties And Responsibilities: It shall be the responsibility of the
committee to develop and/or update an urban forestry plan for the care,
preservation, pruning, planting, replanting, and removal of trees and shrubs on
public property. Such plan will be presented to the city council, and upon
their acceptance and approval, shall constitute the official comprehensive city
tree plan for the city of Kamiah.
   D.   Tree Administrator: The tree administrator is hereby charged with the
responsibility for the enforcement of this chapter and may serve notice to any
person or entity in violation thereof or institute legal proceedings as may be
required, and the city attorney is hereby authorized to institute appropriate
proceedings to that end.
   E.   Operation: The committee shall choose its own officers, make its own
rules and regulations, and keep a record of its proceedings. A majority of the
members shall be a quorum for the transaction of business. (Ord. 2008-1 §1,
2007)
12.14.050: PERMITS; MAINTENANCE AND REMOVAL OF TREES:
   A.   Violations: It shall be a violation of this chapter for any person to
abuse, destroy, poison, or mutilate any public tree, or the root of any public
tree. It shall be a violation of this chapter to top any public tree.
   B.   Permits:
      1.   Permits shall be required to remove, prune, or plant any public
tree. Permits for removal shall be issued only if established, to the
administrator's satisfaction, that there is need for the removal. Costs of
removal, pruning, or planting shall be borne by the requesting party. Such
permit application shall be made five (5) working days before the intended
activity. The tree administrator may grant the permit or grant a permit on
conditions when such is consistent with the provisions of this chapter, the
urban forestry plan, and other applicable laws and public policy. No such
permit shall be valid for a period greater than ninety (90) days after the date
of its issuance.
         a.   Commercial Permits: Any person or entity contracting to do the
specified work for compensation will be required to obtain a commercial permit.
            (1)   Cost: The cost of a commercial permit will be one hundred
dollars ($100.00) plus a five dollar ($5.00) charge for each tree serviced. Any
changes or amendments to such permit charges may be made and fixed by city
council resolution.
            (2)   Requirements: Any person or entity obtaining a commercial
permit must do the following:
               (A)   Provide proof of insurance along with the permit
application.
               (B)   Agree to follow all permit rules and abide by all safety
regulations required by the industry, OSHA, the state of Idaho and Lewis
County.
         b.   Private Permits: Any citizen of Kamiah can qualify for this type
of permit.
            (1)   Cost: The cost of a private permit will be two dollars
($2.00). Any changes or amendments to such permit charges may be made and fixed
by city council resolution.
            (2)   Requirements: Any person obtaining a private permit must do
the following:
               (A)   Sign a release and a waiver relieving the city of Kamiah
of any property damage or personal injury that might occur as a result of the
work for which the permit was obtained.
               (B)   The private citizen will be responsible for coordinating
any traffic control, that would be necessary to complete the project in a safe
manner, with the city maintenance prior to the project.
      2.   Public utilities are exempted from obtaining a permit, however, the
utility must observe good arboricultural practices as specified by the
International Society of Arboricultural Specialists.
      3.   All fees obtained from the issuance of said permits shall be used to
maintain city trees and for any expenses associated with the enforcement of
this chapter.
   C.   Adequate Maintenance: Owners of property adjacent to a public tree
shall provide adequate maintenance for that tree. Adequate maintenance shall
include sufficient water and supportive staking if necessary.
   D.   Removal: The tree administrator, or city maintenance, may remove, or
may cause the removal of, public trees or branches which provide a hazard to
the public health, safety, or welfare, or public trees which should be removed
to further sound community forestry goals. The city of Kamiah shall bear all
costs as budgeted for removal of public trees unless a private party has
requested removal, and received a permit for removal from the tree
administrator. In that case, the entire cost of removal will be incurred by the
private party requesting removal. (Ord. 2008-1 §1, 2007)
12.14.060: OTHER PROVISIONS:
   A.   Upon the discovery of an epidemic disease or pest in any public or
private tree, the administrator shall serve notice upon the owner of the tree
which shall require that the owner eradicate, remove or otherwise control such
conditions within a given time frame. All costs will be incurred by the owner
of the tree.
   B.   A variance shall be required when a property owner wants to deviate
from the rules and regulations of this chapter. All requests for variances
shall be directed to the urban forestry committee and approved by the city
council. (Ord. 2008-1 §1, 2007)
12.14.070: PENALTIES:
Any person, partnership, firm, corporation or other legal entity who violates
any provision of this chapter is guilty of an infraction and punishable by a
fine not to exceed one hundred dollars ($100.00). All such violations which are
of a continuing nature shall constitute a separate offense for each day of such
continuance. Any violation of this chapter shall also constitute a public
nuisance and may be enjoined and abated as provided by law. (Ord. 2008-1 §1,
2007)
CHAPTER 12.16
FENCES
SECTION:
12.16.010: Barbed Wire And Electric Fences
12.16.010: BARBED WIRE AND ELECTRIC FENCES:
It is unlawful for any person to erect or maintain any electric fence or any
fence constructed in whole or in part of barbed wire, or to use barbed wire as
a guard to any parking lot or parcel of land. (Prior code §6-105)
CHAPTER 12.20
SNOW AND ICE REMOVAL 1
SECTION:
12.20.010: Duty Of Owner
12.20.020: Notice To Owner
12.20.030: Failure To Comply
 
Notes
1 1. IC § 50-317.
12.20.010: DUTY OF OWNER:
The owner, tenant or occupant of any premises, within the municipality,
abutting or adjoining any public sidewalk shall remove all snow and ice from
any such sidewalk. (Prior code §9-301)
12.20.020: NOTICE TO OWNER:
It shall be the duty of the municipality to notify any owner, tenant or
occupant of property described in section
12.20.010 of this chapter to remove or otherwise correct the objectionable
matter legislated against in section
12.20.010 of this chapter, which notice shall be sent by registered mail to the
last known address of such owner, tenant or occupant, notifying him that he has
a period of twenty four (24) hours from and after receipt of such notice,
within which to correct or otherwise remove the objections set forth in said
notice. (Prior code §9-302)
12.20.030: FAILURE TO COMPLY:
Upon failure of the owner, tenant or occupant of the premises to comply with
the terms and conditions of the notice, then and in that event the municipality
shall have the right to remove such snow and ice and assess the cost thereof
against the premises abutting the sidewalk. Such assessment shall be certified
to the county assessor or other proper county officials having charge of the
making of the assessment roll, and such assessment shall be placed on the
assessment roll and collected in the same manner as other municipal taxes are
collected. (Prior code §9-303)
CHAPTER 12.24
STREETS AND ALLEYS IN ADDITIONS TO CITY
SECTION:
12.24.010: Requirements
12.24.010: REQUIREMENTS:
Streets and alleys laid out in any addition to the municipality shall be
contiguous and correspond in directions and width to the streets and alleys of
the municipality to which they are an addition thereto. (Prior code §9-401)
CHAPTER 12.28
SIDEWALKS
SECTION:
12.28.010: Intent
12.28.020: Inspection
12.28.030: New Construction; Improvement Of Old Construction
12.28.040: Ordered To Be Constructed, Reconstructed Or Repaired
12.28.050: Work Not Completed
12.28.060: Statement Of Costs Of Work
12.28.070: Recovery Of Money Expended By The City
12.28.080: Order For Work Revoked; Hearing
12.28.090: Construction To Grade Required
12.28.100: Cement Sidewalks Required
12.28.110: Repaired Sidewalks To Be Of Cement
12.28.120: Width And Location
12.28.130: Survey For Grade; Construction Permit Required
12.28.140: Specifications For Construction
12.28.150: Deposit For Survey And Administrative Costs
12.28.160: City Held Harmless
12.28.010: INTENT:
It is the intent of the governing body of the city to have all sidewalks within
the city kept in a reasonably safe condition for general use by the public.
(Ord. 5-81 §1, 1981)
12.28.020: INSPECTION:
The superintendent of streets shall inspect all sidewalks, where any sidewalk
is so damaged or defective as to require, in his judgment, the construction of
a new walk and in all cases where there is no sidewalk and, in the judgment of
the superintendent of streets, a sidewalk is necessary, the superintendent of
streets shall report such fact to the mayor and council with his
recommendation. If, after considering such report and recommendation, the mayor
and council deem it necessary, they shall order such sidewalk to be
constructed. (Ord. 5-81 §2(A), 1981)
12.28.030: NEW CONSTRUCTION; IMPROVEMENT OF OLD CONSTRUCTION:
For all new construction, or substantial improvement of old construction within
the meaning of the uniform building code within the city for which a building
permit is required, the applicant for such building permit, before its
issuance, shall provide reasonable plans for the construction of and be
required to agree to install sidewalks on the property as are required by this
chapter; provided, however, the council may waive the requirements of sidewalks
in any case where sidewalk construction is inappropriate or impracticable upon
a petition for waiver being submitted to the council in writing. (Ord. 5-81 §2
(B), 1981)
12.28.040: ORDERED TO BE CONSTRUCTED, RECONSTRUCTED OR REPAIRED:
When any sidewalk is ordered to be constructed, reconstructed or repaired under
the provisions of this chapter, the superintendent of streets shall serve a
notice in writing upon the property owner or any resident agent of the property
owner, directing such sidewalk to be constructed, reconstructed or repaired of
the materials and according to the specifications in force in the district
where such sidewalk is to be constructed, reconstructed or repaired and
describing the premises adjacent to which such construction is to be made. The
service of such notice may be made by delivery of a copy thereof to the owner,
his agent, or, if neither is to be found within the city, by mailing a copy
thereof to the owner at his last known post office address and service by mail
shall be deemed complete upon the expiration of five (5) days from the date of
the mailing of such notice. (Ord. 5-81 §3, 1981)
12.28.050: WORK NOT COMPLETED:
If the work of construction, reconstructing or repairing sidewalks is not begun
in accordance with the notice provided for in section
12.28.040 of this chapter within thirty (30) days after the service of such
notice or if, having been begun, such work is not completed within a reasonable
time thereafter, then such sidewalk shall be constructed, reconstructed,
repaired or completed, as the case may be, by the street superintendent under
the general direction and supervision of the city council. (Ord. 5-81 §4, 1981)
12.28.060: STATEMENT OF COSTS OF WORK:
Upon the completion of the construction or repair of sidewalks, the cost
thereof shall be paid out of any unappropriated money in the general fund of
the city or such other fund as may be designated by the mayor and council. As
soon as may be thereafter, the superintendent of streets shall serve upon the
owner of such property or his agent, in the same manner as the notice to
construct sidewalks is authorized to be served, an itemized statement of the
cost of such construction, reconstruction or repair. If the cost thereof be not
paid within five (5) days after such service, the superintendent of streets
shall deliver a copy of such itemized statement to the city attorney, who shall
proceed to collect the same. (Ord. 5-81 §6, 1981)
12.28.070: RECOVERY OF MONEY EXPENDED BY THE CITY:
   A.   Upon receipt of the statement provided for in section
12.28.060 of this chapter, the city attorney shall bring suit in any court
having jurisdiction for the recovery of money expended by the city in the
construction, reconstruction or repair of sidewalks or shall file a lien upon
the property abutting upon such sidewalk.
   B.   Such lien shall be verified and shall be filed and foreclosed as in the
case of other liens under the general laws of the state. From the date of the
filing of the same, the cost of such construction, maintenance or repairs shall
be and remain a lien upon the property described as in the case of other liens.
(Ord. 5-81 §7, 1981)
12.28.080: ORDER FOR WORK REVOKED; HEARING:
At any time after the service of the notice to construct, reconstruct, or
repair as provided by section
12.28.040 of this chapter, and before the expiration of the time specified
therein, the owner or agent upon whom such service was made may appear before
the mayor and council at any general or special meeting and show cause why the
order for such construction, reconstruction, or repair should be revoked. The
council shall hear and determine such application informally. Such application
shall not extend the period within which the work is to be begun unless
otherwise ordered by the council. (Ord. 5-81 §8, 1981)
12.28.090: CONSTRUCTION TO GRADE REQUIRED:
All sidewalks ordered constructed by the city council shall be constructed to
an established grade; provided, that owners desiring to construct any sidewalks
by private subscription may obtain a permit from the city council to construct
such sidewalks upon specifications approved by it. Such sidewalks may be laid
upon the then traveled surface of the street within the space reserved for
sidewalk purposes, but shall only be permitted to remain so long as kept in
good condition and until the street is improved to the official grade, when
they must be put on the official grade and be constructed to conform to the
sidewalk specifications. (Ord. 5-81 §9, 1981)
12.28.100: CEMENT SIDEWALKS REQUIRED:
When any street or avenue in the city shall be graded to an established grade,
the sidewalks thereafter constructed on both sides of such street or avenue
shall be constructed of cement in accordance with the specifications for the
construction of such sidewalks. (Ord. 5-81 §10, 1981)
12.28.110: REPAIRED SIDEWALKS TO BE OF CEMENT:
When the street superintendent shall report any sidewalk along any street or
avenue which has already been put to grade to be in a damaged or defective
condition requiring repair or reconstruction and such report shall be confirmed
by a resolution of the mayor and council, then such sidewalk shall be
constructed of cement in accordance with the specifications for such
construction on file in the office of the city clerk. (Ord. 5-81 §11, 1981)
12.28.120: WIDTH AND LOCATION:
All sidewalks constructed of cement shall be constructed of such width and in
such location as the mayor and council may provide by resolution. (Ord. 5-81
§12, 1981)
12.28.130: SURVEY FOR GRADE; CONSTRUCTION PERMIT REQUIRED:
No cement sidewalk shall be constructed without first obtaining a survey for
grade and a permit for construction from the city clerk. (Ord. 5-81 §13, 1981)
12.28.140: SPECIFICATIONS FOR CONSTRUCTION:
All concrete sidewalks and curbs shall be constructed under the direct
supervision of the street superintendent and in accordance with specifications
on file in the office of the city clerk. (Ord. 5-81 §14, 1981)
12.28.150: DEPOSIT FOR SURVEY AND ADMINISTRATIVE COSTS:
Every application to the city clerk for a permit to construct a sidewalk shall
be accompanied by a deposit of one hundred dollars ($100.00) for every fifty
(50) linear feet or portion thereof on the front of the lot or lots abutting on
the sidewalk to cover the costs for survey for grade and other administrative
costs. If the sidewalk is constructed within a period of nine (9) months from
the date of application, the city clerk is authorized to refund such deposit to
the applicant or his successor. If the sidewalk is not constructed within such
period of time, there shall be no refund of the deposit fee thereafter and such
fee shall be retained by the city clerk in the general fund of the city. (Ord.
5-81 §15, 1981)
12.28.160: CITY HELD HARMLESS:
Any person constructing a sidewalk shall save the city harmless from all suits
and actions and damages of every nature resulting from such construction. (Ord.
5-81 §5, 1981)
CHAPTER 12.32
CITY SWIMMING POOL
SECTION:
12.32.010: Applicability
12.32.020: Fees
12.32.010: APPLICABILITY:
The city owns a swimming pool which is used for recreation and for instruction
of swimmers in water safety and swimming lessons. (Ord. 2010-7 §1, 2010)
12.32.020: FEES:
The following fees for use of the city swimming pool shall be charged, payable
to the "City of Kamiah", in advance, and set by resolution of the city council
of Kamiah:
   A.   Afternoon Pass: Fee shall be set by resolution of the city council of
Kamiah.
   B.   Night Pass: Fee shall be set by resolution of the city council of
Kamiah.
   C.   Swimming Lessons: Fee shall be set by resolution of the city council of
Kamiah.
   D.   Season Passes: Fee shall be set by resolution of the city council of
Kamiah.
   E.   Family Season Passes: Fee shall be set by resolution of the city
council of Kamiah.
   F.   Family Hour Swim: Fee shall be set by resolution of the city council of
Kamiah.
   G.   Lap Swim And Aerobic Class: Fee shall be set by resolution of the city
council of Kamiah.
   H.   Pool Rental For Private Parties:
      1.   Fee shall be set by resolution of the city council of Kamiah.
      2.   All requests for pool rental will require approval of the pool
manager or assistant pool manager.
      3.   Pool rental fees must be paid seventy two (72) hours in advance; no
refunds seventy two (72) hours prior to rental reservation time. Refund only
issued day of reservation if pool is closed due to unforeseen circumstances.
      4.   The pool is normally only available for rental as follows:
         a.   Between nine o'clock (9:00) P.M. and twelve o'clock (12:00)
midnight, Monday through Saturday.
         b.   Sundays, with a four (4) hour limit.
         c.   Holidays, with a four (4) hour limit, if lifeguards are
available.
   I.   Compliance To Regulations: All persons using the city swimming pool
must follow the health and safety regulations as established by the pool
management, the lifeguards and the city council.
   J.   Termination: Failure to obey health and safety regulations will be
reason to terminate daily or seasonal passes, swimming lessons or pool rental
without refund of fees paid. (Ord. 2010-7 §1, 2010)
CHAPTER 12.36
CITY PARKS
SECTION:
12.36.010: Purpose
12.36.020: Permit Required; Application
12.36.030: Application Review
12.36.040: Alcoholic Beverages
12.36.050: Permit Application Fee
12.36.060: [Reserved] (Rep. by Ord. 2019-1, 2019)
12.36.070: Exemption
12.36.080: Tobacco Use Prohibited
12.36.090: Hours Of Operation/Camping Prohibited
12.36.095: Animals In The City Parks; Prohibitions And Penalties
12.36.100: Violation
12.36.010: PURPOSE:
The Kamiah City Park, adjacent to U.S. Highway 12 and the Clearwater River, and
Dupont Park adjacent to the Kamiah swimming pool on Idaho Street, are declared
to be valuable city assets and the use of these parks shall be controlled. It
is in the public interest and welfare that the consumption of alcoholic
beverages and tobacco products should be prohibited in the use of Dupont Park.
To further the purposes of this chapter, the city council may adopt by
resolution operational policies for the use of Kamiah city parks. (Ord. 2019-1,
2019: Ord. 2011-2, 2011)
12.36.020: PERMIT REQUIRED; APPLICATION:
Any person, group, or organization who desires to use the city park pit area
and/or the city park stage area or electricThe Kamiah City Park, adjacent to
U.S. Highway 12 and the Clearwater River, and Dupont Park adjacent to the
Kamiah swimming pool on Idaho Street, are declared to be valuable city assets
and the use of these parks shall be controlled. It is in the public interest
and welfare that the consumption of alcoholic beverages and tobacco products
should be prohibited in the use of Dupont Park. To further the purposes of this
chapter, the city council may adopt by resolution operational policies for the
use of Kamiah city parks. (Ord. 2019-1, 2019: Ord. 2011-2, 2011)
12.36.030: APPLICATION REVIEW:
The city clerk and authorized law enforcement, upon receipt of the application
for a permit, shall review the application and may impose reasonable
requirements toupon issuance of the permit, to protect and preserve the park.
Such reasonable requirements may include, but are not limited to, use and
cleanup of the restroom facilities, use and cleanup of litter containment
facilities and ultimate cleanup to the park. (Ord. 2019-1, 2019: Ord. 2011-2,
2011)
12.36.040: ALCOHOLIC BEVERAGES:
Alcoholic beverages are allowed in the Kamiah City Park in accordance with the
laws of the state of Idaho. Catering permits must be obtained before alcoholic
beverages may be sold in the park. The fee for said catering permit shall be
determined by resolution of the city council. The regulation of alcohol and the
sale thereof in the city park may be declared a nuisance pursuant to city of
Kamiah ordinance and prosecuted pursuant to said ordinance. Alcoholic beverages
of any kind are not allowed in Dupont Park. (Ord. 2019-1, 2019: Ord. 2011-2,
2011)
12.36.050: PERMIT APPLICATION FEE:
A permit application fee shall be determined by resolution of the city council
and will be assessed to any person, group, or organization who applies for a
permit for the city park pit area and a fee, the amount of which shall be
determined by resolution of the city council, will be assessed to any person,
group or organization who applies for a permit for the city park stage. (Ord.
2019-1, 2019: Ord. 2011-2, 2011)
12.36.060: [RESERVED]:
(Rep. by Ord. 2019-1, 2019)
12.36.070: EXEMPTION:
Family groups using the park for family gatherings, and not using the cooking
pit area or the city park stage area, shall be exempt from the permit
requirement even though they are a group, provided that all park activity shall
cease one-half (1/2) hour after sunset or as otherwise set forth in the park
operational policies adopted by the city council. (Ord. 2019-1, 2019: Ord.
2011-2, 2011)
12.36.080: TOBACCO USE PROHIBITED:
The consumption and use of tobacco products is prohibited within twenty-five
(25) feet of the swimming pool in Dupont Park at all times. (Ord. 2019-1, 2019:
Ord. 2011-2, 2011)
12.36.090: HOURS OF OPERATION/CAMPING PROHIBITED:
The city parks will be available for use from sunrise to sunset, unless
otherwise provided in a permit. Camping in city parks is prohibited except as
may be allowed pursuant to a special permit issued as provided in this chapter.
No persons or vehicles of any kind shall be allowed in any park after sunset.
Appropriate signage shall be posted in the parks establishing the times that
the parks are open to the public and that camping is prohibited. (Ord. 2019-1,
2019: Ord. 2011-2, 2011: Ord. 2002-2 §8, 2002)
12.36.095: ANIMALS IN THE CITY PARKS; PROHIBITIONS AND PENALTIES:
   A.   It shall be unlawful for any person to take or allow any animal,
whether domestic, livestock or any other animal, upon the premises of any city
park owned by the city.
   B.   The prohibition in this section does not apply to a licensed or
otherwise qualified service animal necessary to assist an individual with a
disability or to an animal used by a police officer in the line of duty.
      C.   Upon payment of a fee established by resolution by the city council,
a vendor or others with special circumstances may apply to the City Clerk for
an exemption from the prohibitions contained in this section. The exemption may
be granted upon conditions necessary for the protection of the city parks and
public. If an exemption is granted, the City Clerk shall issue a certificate
stating the exemption and its conditions.
      D.   All parks shall be conspicuously posted with notices that no animals
are allowed in the park and that a violation of the prohibition is a
misdemeanor.
      E.   Law enforcement officers are authorized to enforce this subsection
and to eject from a city park any person violating this subsection.
      F.   Any person violating any provision of this subsection shall be
guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction thereof, shall be subject to a
fine not to exceed one thousand dollars ($1,000.00) or imprisonment in the
county jail for a period not to exceed six (6) months or both fine and
imprisonment. (Ord. 2019-04, 2019)
12.36.100: VIOLATION:
Any person, group or organization, using the park after hours or without a
permit, after being warned to disperse by authorized law enforcement, and
failing to do so, shall be guilty of a misdemeanor. (Ord. 2019-1, 2019: Ord.
2011-2, 2011: Ord. 2002-2 §9, 2002)

PUBLIC SERVICES
CHAPTER 13.04
WATER SERVICE 1
SECTION:
