13.04.090: Extensions To System
13.04.100: Service Connection Charge
13.04.110: Rates; Schedule
13.04.120: Outside Corporate Limits; Individual Residents Rates
13.04.130: Extraordinary Costs For Supplying Outside Residents
13.04.140: Surplus Water; Supply To Nonresidents
13.04.150: Nonresident Municipal Corporation; Negotiation Of Water Rates
13.04.160: Waiver Of Water Bill For Hardship Cases
13.04.170: Antisyphon Devices And Shutoff Valves
13.04.180: Bulk Water
13.04.190: Turn Off/On Request; Charges For Turn On
 
Notes
1 1. IC §§ 50-323, 50-1030.
13.04.010: APPLICATION FOR CONNECTION; FEES:
   A.   Any person or entity desiring to have premises connected with the water
supply system of the city shall make application to the city clerk and pay the
sum of one thousand five hundred dollars ($1,500.00) plus costs of the water
meter and all incidental installation materials including the costs of pipe and
the installation thereof for all footage in excess of sixty three feet (63')
from the existing water source. Payment of fees shall be made to the city
clerk. Upon application, and payment of fees, the city shall tap the water
system and main, and place the water to the property line except as hereinabove
limited.
   B.   Where, at the time a building permit is applied for, if the proposed
building or structure as shown by the plans accompanying the building permit
shows that one tapping of the water main or source will service more than one
commercial or residential unit, then only one thousand five hundred dollars
($1,500.00) shall be necessary for each ten (10) units so proposed. The
following schedule shall apply to multiple units on one tapping of the water
main:
 
0 to 10 units   $1,500.00  
11 to 20 units  3,000.00   
21 to 30 units  4,500.00   
Over 30 units   1,500.00  (for each 10 units or part of 10 units)
 
Provided further, that should a multiple-unit complex require more than one
tapping of the water main, the above schedule shall apply for each tapping.
   C.   No proration of the water connection fee shall be allowed for uneven
numbers of commercial or residential units.
   D.   In the event that no building permit is required then, nevertheless,
plans of the proposed structure shall be submitted to the city with the
application for water service. If no application is given to the city, the city
shall not be obligated to provide water service.
   E.   The above set forth fees shall apply to independent mobile homes in the
same way as they apply to permanent structures. It is intended that the above
special rates shall apply to only multiple-family dwellings, motels, hotels,
business malls or trailer courts, as the same are usually understood and
defined. The special rates shall not apply to separate single-family dwellings
or mobile home units. (Ord. 98-3 §1, 1997: Ord. 96-5 §1, 1996: Ord. 4-94 §1,
1994: Ord. 1-79 §1, 1979: Ord. 2-76 §1, 1976: Ord. 3-75 §1, 1975: Ord. 3 §1,
1957: prior code §3-102)
13.04.020: HOURS FOR SPRINKLING; CITY TO SHUT OFF WATER SUPPLY:
The water superintendent shall have the power to regulate the hours for
sprinkling and in an emergency prohibit the same. The city reserves the right
to shut off at any time the water supply for repairs, extensions, nonpayment of
rates or other reasons; and the city shall not be responsible for any damage
such as bursting of boilers, breaking of pipes or fixtures, stoppage of water
supply or any other damage resulting from the shutting off of water. It shall
be a misdemeanor for persons to use water for sprinkling during the hours that
the same has been prohibited by the water superintendent or to use any waters
when the use thereof has been prohibited during an emergency. (Ord. 38, 1963:
Ord. 3 §2, 1957: prior code §3-103)
13.04.030: OWNER RESPONSIBILITY:
Pipes and hydrants within any premises must be kept in good repair and kept
from freezing at owner's expense, and the owner will be responsible for all
damage from leaks and breaks. (Ord. 3 §3, 1957: prior code §3-104)
13.04.040: PAYMENT OF WATER BILLS:
   A.   All utility bills shall be paid to the collector designated by the
council on or before the tenth day of the month following the period of service
billed. All accounts shall become delinquent at four o'clock (4:00) P.M. on the
tenth day of the month if not paid as aforesaid. Whenever any customer becomes
delinquent the city clerk shall so notify the owner of the premises by means of
the monthly utility billing statement of notice of intent to discontinue water
services from the premises to which said services are furnished. Said utility
billing statement shall state that water services will be discontinued and will
remain cut off until all past due charges, penalties, and fees have been paid.
Actual discontinuance of services shall not occur until at least ten (10) days
have expired after the utility billing statement has been mailed and shall not
occur until the next business day after the tenth day has passed. After the ten
(10) days have expired the public works superintendent is then authorized to
discontinue service until all fees for water, sewer, and garbage, including any
penalties, have been paid.
Upon a discontinuance of service an additional charge of twenty five dollars
($25.00) shall be added for reopening the service in addition to all other
costs, penalties, fees and charges herein mentioned.
   B.   In addition, in the event that the service has been discontinued for
failure to pay, besides the penalties set forth in subsection A of this
section, the city council may in its discretion impose and require a deposit
equal to the previous unpaid balance. The deposit thereunder required may then
be applied to future potential arrearages should they occur with the same
customer.
   C.   In addition, in the event there is any delinquency for the payment of
any utility bill, there shall be a penalty set by resolution of the city
council of the city of Kamiah per bill that shall be added to each billing and
must be paid in addition to all other charges provided in this code. (Ord.
2011-6, 2011)
13.04.050: INTERFERENCE WITH SYSTEM PROHIBITED:
   A.   Interference Prohibited: Any person who shall interfere with, molest,
injure or destroy any fire hydrant, pipe, main, meter, service box or other
appurtenance of the city water system, or shall open any fire hydrant, cap, or
make any connection with any water main, lateral or pipe without first
obtaining permission from an authorized agent of the city or from the fire
department, as the case may be; who shall divert or appropriate water from any
hydrant, main, lateral or water pipe, without first paying therefor the charges
specified by the code, shall be subject to the penalties set out in this
section. It is to be specifically included that no person shall be permitted to
adjust, change or turn on any water valve that has been turned off by the city
for any reason whatsoever, including, but not limited to, the turning off of
the same because of a failure to pay city water bills.
   B.   Meter Adjustments: Any adjustment whatsoever of a meter shall only be
done with the express consent of the city official in charge of the water
department. Furthermore, all city water system taps shall be accomplished by
the city or under the supervision of the water superintendent.
   C.   Penalties: Any person doing any of the above prohibited acts shall be
subject to a civil penalty of two hundred dollars ($200.00) which shall be
accessible and collectible in the small claims division of the district court
within the state of Idaho, and in addition thereto, such person shall be
subject to a triple charge for all water that can reasonably be proven to have
been used after the improper diversion or improper adjustment of any valve. The
penalties set forth herein shall be in addition to all other remedies permitted
by this code and shall constitute additional sums to which the city would be
entitled, a lien, pursuant to this code. (Ord. 2011-4, 2011: Ord. 1-93 §1,
1992: Ord. 3 §5, 1957: prior code §3-106)
13.04.060: MOVING WATER SERVICE FEE:
There shall be a reasonable charge for time and materials for the moving of a
water service after original installation is made on present property. (Ord. 4-
75 §1, 1975: Ord. 3 §6, 1957: prior code §3-107)
13.04.070: DAMAGE TO SYSTEM; RESPONSIBILITY FOR REPAIR AND CHARGES:
All damages done to the city's water system, such as breaking pipes, water
meters, fire hydrants or any other equipment, shall be repaired or replaced by
the city and charges for the same will be made to the person or persons
incurring damage. (Ord. 3 §7, 1957: prior code §3-108)
13.04.080: BILLINGS:
   A.   All water charges shall be directly billed to the property owner as is
shown by either the real property records in the county where water service is
used, or contract purchasers of property that satisfactorily demonstrate
ownership to the city clerk. If any property is used as a rental by the
property owner, the owner shall nevertheless be the person billed for water
service. It shall be the responsibility of the property owner to see that water
meters are protected against freezing during the winter months.
   B.   In the event of a nonpayment of a water bill, in addition to the other
remedies provided for in this chapter, the city shall be entitled to a lien on
the real estate served by the water for all unpaid bills. Such lien shall be
filed for all claimed unpaid amounts within six (6) months of the last action
on the account, and then foreclosed in the district court, in and for Lewis
County, within one year of the filing of the lien. The lien hereunder provided
for may be joined with a lien for unpaid garbage or sewer services as otherwise
provided in this code. (Ord. 6-85 §1, 1985: Ord. 2-81 §1, 1981: Ord. 34-67,
1967: Ord. 3 §8, 1957: prior code §3-109)
13.04.090: EXTENSIONS TO SYSTEM:
All extensions to the city's water system mains shall be supervised by the city
water superintendent, and once they are connected to the present system, they
become the property of the city. (Ord. 3 §9, 1957: prior code §3-110)
13.04.100: SERVICE CONNECTION CHARGE:
Every service connection shall be metered and charged the rate set forth in
section
13.04.110 of this chapter. (Ord. 3 §10, 1957: prior code §3-111)
13.04.110: RATES; SCHEDULE:
   A.   Charges for the use of water within the city, as the same may from time
to time be increased or decreased, and any place where water is furnished by
the city, will be based upon a fee per cubic foot, as set by resolution of the
city council of the city of Kamiah. There is also a minimum base rate which
will be assessed to any individual property or multiple resident property,
individual business or multiple business property, and vacant lots with water
meter(s). Minimum base rate outside the city limits will be set by resolution
of the city council of the city of Kamiah.
   B.   Within any building that houses more than one independent business, the
deeded property owner of that building, or the contract purchaser of that
building, shall pay the minimum charges set forth for each independent business
within the building as specified in subsection A of this section.
   C.   Concerning any building which houses multiple businesses, or multiple
independent tenants, the owner or contract purchaser of that building and real
estate shall be charged the regular minimum fee for each independent business.
In addition, any actual water used by the common meter shall then be billed to
the deeded owner or contract purchaser as from time to time would be used by
the building.
   D.   The deeded property owner or the contract purchaser of any building or
real estate as set forth in subsection B and/or C of this section who is not
receiving metered water services from the city shall pay the monthly base rate
as set by resolution pursuant to subsection E of this section.
   E.   Water rates shall be set by resolution of the city council of the city
of Kamiah, and shall be the rates applied to the formula for nonresidents of
the city pursuant to section
13.04.120 of this chapter. The current water rates shall remain in effect until
the passage of a resolution by the city council of the city of Kamiah.
   F.   The deeded owner or property purchaser must, as a condition of
receiving continued service, sign an agreement with the city to be responsible
for the bill for water services, even if the property is rented to another.
Owners who shall live out of state or out of the Kamiah area may appoint an
agent to act on his/her behalf for purposes of entering into said agreement
with the city.
   G.   In the event payment for water service is made by check, and the check
be returned or dishonored for any reason, the city may, as a condition of
continuing water service to the property of the maker of said check, collect
from said maker any bank charges made by said bank against the city for
handling or processing said check or checks.
   H.   For all unpaid charges, the city shall be entitled to file a lien in
the county auditor's office where the services are provided. Lien filing and
foreclosure may be joined with actions for other unpaid utility services,
pursuant to section
13.04.080 of this chapter.
   I.   In the event of the transfer and/or selling of real property the
charges for service shall be prorated on a daily basis to include metered
consumption. (Ord. 2016-5, 2016)
13.04.120: OUTSIDE CORPORATE LIMITS; INDIVIDUAL RESIDENTS RATES:
The following rates shall apply to individual residents outside of the
incorporated limits of the city unless the same are within a duly incorporated
water district or other municipal corporation as is controlled hereinafter: All
such nonresident individuals shall pay water rates exactly double the rates
charged city residents set forth in section
13.04.110 of this chapter, except base minimum rate which will increase in the
city limits will remain the same rate increase outside of the corporate city
limits, effective with the passage of ordinance 2001-1. (Ord. 2001-1 §2, 2000:
Ord. 4-76 §1, 1976: prior code §3-101(2))
13.04.130: EXTRAORDINARY COSTS FOR SUPPLYING OUTSIDE RESIDENTS:
The city council may, in its discretion, in addition to the water rates for
persons outside the city limits, provide for the payment of extraordinary costs
of supplying water to outside residents by adding to any monthly water bill a
pro rata share of such extraordinary costs. Such costs may include, but are not
limited to, additional electricity bills, or extraordinary repair bills. Such
additional costs, however, if added to a monthly water bill, shall only exactly
reimburse the city for costs actually expended, and prior to the inclusion of
any monthly bill the council shall pass a motion to include the same on a bill,
with record of such motion being reflected by the council minutes. (Ord. 4-76
§1, 1976: prior code §3-101(3))
13.04.140: SURPLUS WATER; SUPPLY TO NONRESIDENTS:
The city shall not, under any circumstances, supply a nonresident or a
nonresident organization or corporation with other than surplus water. For
purposes of this chapter, "surplus water" is defined as follows: That amount of
water that exists above the minimum amount necessary for fire protection as
shown by the Idaho survey and rating bureau which states that the minimum fire
flow for Kamiah should be one thousand seven hundred fifty (1,750) gallons per
minute for two (2) hours, or approximately two hundred ten thousand (210,000)
gallons. Based on the existing storage of four hundred thousand (400,000)
gallons, when the storage tanks drop to half full, the city no longer has
surplus water, as of February 17, 1976. (Ord. 4-76 §1, 1976: prior code §3-101
(4))
13.04.150: NONRESIDENT MUNICIPAL CORPORATION; NEGOTIATION OF WATER RATES:
Notwithstanding the other provisions of the ordinance relating to the sale of
surplus water to nonresidents of the city of Kamiah, the city council reserves
the right to negotiate freely water rates with nonresident municipal
corporations, including water districts, as the council may determine is in the
best interest for the city. Such water rates may, in the council's discretion,
also reflect additional services rendered to any nonresident municipal
corporation, such as, but not limited to, billing services, meter readings, and
extraordinary costs of supplying water to such municipal corporation. Any
negotiated water rate with any such municipal corporation shall be reflected in
the minutes of the council, prior to the entry of a contract for water service
to any such municipal corporation. (Ord. 4-76 §1, 1976: prior code §3-101(5))
13.04.160: WAIVER OF WATER BILL FOR HARDSHIP CASES:
   A.   In the event the council determines that any billing for water service
would work an undue hardship on any individual, the council may, in whole or in
part, waive the water bill.
   B.   Application for waiver of a water bill shall be made in writing to the
city clerk by the person seeking a waiver. The council shall be guided in
hardship cases by the standards set for hardship by the state of Idaho for
waiving real property taxes in hardship cases. (Ord. 4-76 §1, 1976: prior code
§3-101(6))
13.04.170: ANTISYPHON DEVICES AND SHUTOFF VALVES:
For any new tapping of the Kamiah water system which is intended to be
connected to new construction or a new place of use within the Kamiah water
system, any person desiring to connect to the Kamiah water system shall, in
addition to all other requirements of this code, be responsible for placing in
the water service line between the city water meter and the expected place of
use an antisyphon device, also known as a check valve, and in addition, a
shutoff valve in that service pipeline. This requirement shall apply to all new
water taps after the effective date of this section and shall thus allow the
property owners to shut off service to their particular place of use
independent of any change in the metering device. This section shall in no way
alter the noninterference provisions with the water system otherwise appearing
in this code. All materials used for a shutoff valve and the antisyphon device
shall be of a quality approved by the Kamiah water superintendent.
The owner of any property desiring to tap into the Kamiah water system for fire
flow purposes shall pay a hookup fee and for the water service line to said
property including parts and labor of city maintenance necessary to hook up
said line. All fees shall be set by resolution of the Kamiah city council.
(Ord. 2010-6 §1, 2010)
13.04.180: BULK WATER:
   A.   Sale Of Bulk Water: The city of Kamiah shall sell bulk water to
businesses, governmental entities and private individuals desiring the same for
road repair, building of new roads and emergency need for water.
   B.   Price Of Bulk Water: The price for bulk water shall be a price per
cubic foot as determined by resolution of the city council. Any change or
amendment to the per cubic foot price shall also be by resolution of the city
council. (Ord. 2010-1 §1, 2009)
13.04.190: TURN OFF/ON REQUEST; CHARGES FOR TURN ON:
Water shall be turned off/on upon written and/or verbal request from property
owner or contract purchaser of a property and shall pay to the clerk a service
fee of twenty five dollars ($25.00) in addition to payment of all other water
base rate and consumption charges. There shall be no charge whenever water
service is turned off and/or on for routine city service or an emergency during
normal business hours. When turn off and/or turn on is required after business
hours, regardless of the reason for the request, a thirty five dollar ($35.00)
fee will be assessed. A fee of fifty dollars ($50.00) shall be paid to the
clerk by the property owner when a previously existing meter must be replaced
due to a request for removal by the property owner or removal necessitated by
delinquency. The city of Kamiah will waive the fifty dollar ($50.00) fee for
the first time a meter is pulled. Fee will be assessed and payable to the clerk
for any other subsequent requests for meter to be removed. (Ord. 2016-6, 2016)
CHAPTER 13.06
CROSS CONNECTION CONTROL
SECTION:
13.06.010: Definitions
13.06.020: Installation And Maintenance
13.06.030: Backflow Prevention Devices
13.06.040: Inspection
13.06.050: Improper Connection
13.06.060: Violations; Penalties
13.06.010: DEFINITIONS:
As used in this chapter, the following words shall have the following meanings:
BACKFLOW: The flow, other than the intended direction of flow, of any foreign
liquids, gases or substances into the distribution system of a public water
supply.
BACKFLOW PREVENTION DEVICE: A device to counteract back pressure or prevent
back siphonage.
CONTAMINATION: The entry into or presence in a public water supply of any
substance which may be deleterious to health and/or quality of the water.
CROSS CONNECTION: Any physical arrangement whereby a public water supply is
connected, directly or indirectly, with any other water supply system, sewer,
drain, conduit, pool, storage reservoir, plumbing fixture or other device which
contains or may contain contaminated water, sewage or other waste or liquids of
unknown or unsafe quality which may be capable of impairing contamination to
the public water supply as a result of backflow.
ENGINEER: A professional engineer registered in the state of Idaho, retained to
provide engineering service to the city.
HEALTH OFFICER: The state of Idaho department of health and welfare, division
of environment local representative or his authorized agent.
PUBLIC WATER SUPPLY: Any system of water supply intended or used for human
consumption or other domestic uses, including source, treatment, storage,
transmission and distribution facilities, where water is furnished to any
collection or number of individuals, or is made available to the public for
human consumption or domestic use.
SUPERVISOR: The city water department supervisor. (Ord. 2-84 §1, 1984)
13.06.020: INSTALLATION AND MAINTENANCE:
No water service connection to any premises shall be installed or continued in
use by the city unless the water supply is protected by backflow prevention
devices as may be required by this chapter. The installation or maintenance of
a cross connection which will endanger the water quality of the potable water
supply of the city of Kamiah shall be unlawful and is prohibited. Any such
cross connection now existing or hereafter installed is declared to be a public
nuisance and the same shall be abated. The control or elimination of cross
connections shall be in accordance with this chapter and the regulations set
forth in section 1-8306 of the "Idaho Regulations For Public Drinking Water
Systems", together with the latest edition of appropriate manuals of standard
practice pertaining to cross connection control approved by the engineer.
Council shall have the authority to establish requirements more stringent than
state regulations if he deems that the conditions so dictate. The city shall
adopt rules and regulations as necessary to carry out the provisions of this
chapter. (Ord. 2-84 §2, 1984)
13.06.030: BACKFLOW PREVENTION DEVICES:
   A.   Backflow prevention devices shall be installed at the service
connection or within any premises where, in the judgment of the city, the
nature and extent of activities, or the material stored on the premises, would
present an immediate and dangerous hazard to health and/or be deleterious to
the quality of the water should a cross connection occur; even though such
cross connection does not exist at present, the backflow prevention devices
shall be installed under circumstances including, but not limited to, the
following:
      1.   Premises having an auxiliary water supply, unless the quality of the
auxiliary supply is in compliance with the Idaho drinking water regulations and
is acceptable to the city.
      2.   Premises having internal cross connections that are not correctable,
or intricate plumbing arrangements which make it impracticable to ascertain
whether or not cross connections exist.
      3.   Premises where entry is restricted so that inspections for cross
connections cannot be made with sufficient frequency or at sufficiently short
notice to assure that cross connections do not exist.
      4.   Premises having a repeated history of cross connections being
established or reestablished.
      5.   Premises on which any substance is handled under pressure so as to
permit entry into the public water supply, or where a cross connection could
reasonably be expected to occur. This shall include the handling of process
waters and cooling waters.
      6.   Premises where materials of a toxic or hazardous nature are handled
in such a way that if back siphonage should occur, a serious health hazard
might result.
      7.   The following types of facilities will fall into one of the above
categories where a backflow prevention device is required to protect the public
water supply. A backflow prevention device shall be installed at these
facilities unless the city determines that no hazard exists:
         a.   Sewage treatment plants;
         b.   Chemical or other industrial plants;
         c.   Agricultural chemical storage, formulation and distribution
facilities;
         d.   Petroleum storage facilities;
         e.   Underground sprinkling devices or systems.
      8.   Other premises, as specified by city, where backflow prevention
devices are required to protect the public water supply.
   B.   The types of protective device required shall depend on the degree of
hazard which exists:
      1.   An air gap separation or a reduced pressure principle backflow
prevention device shall be installed where the public water supply may be
contaminated with sewage, industrial waste of a toxic nature, or other
contaminant which could cause a health or system hazard.
      2.   In the case of a substance which may be objectionable but not
hazardous, a double check valve assembly, air gap separation, or a reduced
pressure principle backflow prevention device shall be installed.
   C.   Backflow prevention devices required by this chapter shall be installed
at the meter, at the property line of the premises when meters are not used, or
at a location designated by the city. The device shall be located so as to be
readily accessible for maintenance and testing, and furthermore, where no part
of the device will be submerged.
   D.   Backflow prevention devices required by this chapter shall be installed
under the supervision of, and with the approval of, the supervisor.
   E.   Any protective device required by this chapter shall be a model
approved by the city. A double check valve assembly or a reduced pressure
principle backflow prevention device will be approved if it has successfully
passed performance test of the University of Southern California engineering
center or other testing laboratories satisfactory to the engineer. These
devices shall be furnished and installed by and at the expense of the customer.
   F.   Backflow prevention devices installed pursuant to this chapter, except
atmospheric vacuum breakers, shall be inspected and tested annually, or more
often if necessary. Inspections, tests and maintenance shall be at the
customer's expense. Whenever the devices are found to be defective, they shall
be repaired or replaced at the customer's expense. Inspections, tests, repairs
and records thereof shall be accomplished under the city's supervision by
certified testers.
   G.   No underground sprinkling device will be installed without adequate
backflow prevention devices at the point from which the water for irrigation is
taken from the public water supply.
   H.   Failure of the customer to cooperate in the installation, maintenance,
testing or inspection of backflow prevention devices required by this chapter
shall be grounds for the termination of water service to the premises, or in
the alternative, the installation of an air gap separation at the customer's
expense. (Ord. 2-84 §3, 1984)
13.06.040: INSPECTION:
   A.   No water shall be delivered to any structure hereafter built within the
city of Kamiah or within areas served by city water until the same shall have
been inspected by the city for possible cross connections and been approved as
being free of same.
   B.   Any construction for industrial or other purposes which is classified
as hazardous facilities pursuant to section
13.06.030 of this chapter, where it is reasonable to anticipate intermittent
cross connections, or as determined by the city, shall be protected by the
installation of one or more backflow prevention devices at the point of service
from the public water supply or any other location designated by the city.
   C.   Inspections shall be made periodically of all buildings, structures or
improvements of any nature now receiving water through the city's system, for
the purpose of ascertaining whether cross connections exist. Such inspections
shall be made by the city. (Ord. 2-84 §4, 1984)
13.06.050: IMPROPER CONNECTION:
In the event an improper cross connection is not corrected within the time
limit set by the city, or, in the event the city is refused access to any
property for the purpose of determining whether or not cross connections exist,
delivery of water to the property shall cease until the deficiency is corrected
to the city's satisfaction. In addition, the city may effect the necessary
repairs or modifications at the expense of the property owner and refuse
delivery of water to the property until the cost thereof shall have been paid.
(Ord. 2-84 §5, 1984)
13.06.060: VIOLATIONS; PENALTIES:
Any person who violates, disobeys, omits, neglects, refuses to comply with or
resists the enforcement of any of the provisions of this chapter or the rules
and regulations adopted by the city, shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor
and, upon conviction thereof, shall for each offense be punished by a fine in
any sum not exceeding three hundred dollars ($300.00) or imprisonment for a
term not exceeding ninety (90) days or by both such fine and imprisonment.
(Ord. 2-84 §6, 1984)
CHAPTER 13.08
WELLS
SECTION:
13.08.010: Domestic Water Wells
13.08.020: Penalty
13.08.010: DOMESTIC WATER WELLS:
   A.   It shall be unlawful for any person to dig, or drill a water well in
the city limits after the effective date hereof, however, this shall not apply
to Kamiah School District which shall be allowed one water well to be used
exclusively for irrigation purposes.
   B.   Any person owning property upon which there exists an already existing
domestic water well will at no time connect any piping from that well to piping
which is connected to the city's municipal water system. (Ord. 99-3 §1, 1999:
Ord. 99-1 §1, 1999)
13.08.020: PENALTY:
Any person violating the terms of this section after it becomes effective,
shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and shall be punished in accordance with the
punishment terms as specified in the Idaho Code for general misdemeanors.
Furthermore, the city shall be permitted to seek injunctive relief to prohibit
continued use of any cross connected well, or to stop the use of any newly dug
well; or to stop continued digging thereof; and to require mandatory capping
and sealing of any well dug in violation of the terms of this section. (Ord.
99-3 §1, 1999: Ord. 99-1 §1, 1999)
CHAPTER 13.12
SEWER SERVICE
