15.04.050: ADMINISTRATION AND ENFORCEMENT:
   A.   Administrative Authority: The building official, or his designee, shall
be responsible for administering and enforcing this chapter, the codes adopted
by this chapter, and other related city ordinances. The building official may
establish procedures for permit applications, plan checking, issuance of
permits, and field inspections, and may collect fees, as approved by resolution
of the city of Kamiah, for services associated with the administration of
building permits.
   B.   Interdepartmental And Interagency Coordination: To ensure effective
coordination with other departments, agencies and organizations with
jurisdiction, the building official may request comment and/or require approval
from affected agencies prior to issuance of permits. Applications shall meet
the following requirements:
      1.   Demonstrate the proposal meets the requirements of this chapter, the
codes adopted by this chapter, and the requirements of all other applicable
city ordinances. With the application, the applicant shall provide orders of
decision approving any associated applications, such as those for variances,
conditional use permits, temporary hardship permits, final subdivision plats,
planned unit developments, or zone changes.
      2.   Demonstrate the proposal has received required permits and approvals
from North Central district health department and sewer and water districts.
      3.   Demonstrate the proposal has received required access, approach, or
encroachment permits or approvals from the highway district, Idaho department
of transportation, the airport department, and the fire district, as
applicable.
      4.   For mobile or manufactured home setting permits, proved verification
from the Lewis County assessor's appraisal division that applicable taxes have
been paid.
      5.   For encroachments into surface water or wetlands, demonstrate the
proposal has received required encroachment permits from the Idaho department
of lands, Idaho department of water resources, or the U.S. army corps of
engineers.
      6.   Demonstrate the proposal has received approval for all relevant
requirements from the fire district as applicable.
   C.   Correction Of Existing Violations: Applications for permits authorized
by this chapter may not be accepted until all violations of city ordinances are
corrected. Under certain circumstances where compliance would require the
granting of permits to cure existing violations, this requirement may be
waived.
   D.   Effective Standards: Permits shall be governed by the laws and
regulations in effect at the time a complete permit application is received.
   E.   Approval To Enter And Inspect: The property owner or authorized agent's
signature on a permit application shall constitute approval for the department
to enter onto and inspect the property and structures associated with a permit
or application. (Ord. 2010-5 §11, 2010)
15.04.060: APPEAL FROM ADMINISTRATIVE RULINGS:
Any affected person, agency or organization may appeal a decision made by the
building official by submitting, within twenty eight (28) days of the decision,
a written request for a public hearing before the city of Kamiah council, an
explanation of the grounds for the appeal, and applicable fees. An "affected
person" is defined as one having an interest in real property which may be
affected by the decision. The final decision on the appeal shall be made by the
city of Kamiah council.
Decisions that may be appealed include, but are not limited to, the denial of a
permit or certificate of occupancy due to the refusal of a jurisdiction, other
than city of Kamiah, to approve the permit or certificate.
The application for appeal shall be based on a claim that the true intent of
this building code or the rules legally adopted hereunder has been incorrectly
interpreted, the provisions of this building code do not fully apply or an
equally good or better form of construction is proposed. The city of Kamiah
council shall have no authority to waive requirements of the codes as adopted
in this chapter. (Ord. 2010-5 §12, 2010)
15.04.070: REMEDIES AND PENALTIES:
   A.   Violation: Pursuant to Idaho Code section 39-4126, any person who
violates any provisions of this chapter, or the codes adopted by this chapter,
is guilty of a misdemeanor, and upon conviction, shall be fined double the
building permit fee, or imprisoned for not more than ninety (90) days, or both.
Each structure that is in violation of this chapter, and each day of an ongoing
offense, will be considered a separate violation.
   B.   Stop Work Order: Whenever any terrain modification, construction or
other site work is not in compliance with this chapter, adopted codes,
conditions of approval, or related laws, regulations or requirements, the
building official may order the work stopped by written notice.
Such notice shall be served on any persons engaged in doing or causing such
work to be done, and persons shall stop such work until authorized by the
building official to proceed. Stop work orders may be appealed according to the
procedure outlined in section
15.04.060 of this chapter.
   C.   Remedies: The building official may seek equitable relief from a court
of competent jurisdiction, to restrain conduct in violation of this chapter, or
to compel performance of duties established by this chapter. Said equitable
remedies may be pursued in addition to criminal penalties.
   D.   Withholding Of Permits: The building official may withhold permits,
including building permits, on lots or parcels of land with violations of city
ordinances. The building official may also suspend issuance of permits,
including building permits, to applicants who have demonstrated a record of
unresolved noncompliance with city ordinances.
If a permit is withheld, the building official shall set forth the nature of
noncompliance in writing. The applicant may submit a written response to the
compliance issues raised by the building official. Upon consideration of the
response and the full record of performance, the building official shall issue
a final ruling in the case, which may include a list of conditions which must
be met before any additional permits may be issued. The decision of the
building official may be appealed to the city council in accordance with
section
15.04.060 of this chapter. Such appeals must be filed within twenty eight (28)
days of the date of the building official's final decision.
   E.   Compliance Agreements: The building official may enter into compliance
agreements on a case by case basis, subject to the following provisions or
conditions:
      1.   The building official finds that the violations that are the subject
of the compliance agreement do not pose an imminent threat to people or
property.
      2.   The party responsible for compliance agrees to remedy the violation
(s) in an expeditious manner by a certain date.
      3.   The party responsible for compliance agrees to hold the building
official and the city of Kamiah harmless and to defend against any claims
arising through operation of the compliance agreement. The responsible party
shall provide evidence of general liability coverage for personal injury and
property damage for the premises subject to the compliance agreement, with the
city of Kamiah named as an additional insured.
      4.   The responsible party shall pay any costs and/or attorney fees
incurred to enforce a compliance agreement.
   F.   Notice Of Building Ordinance Violation: If a permit expires prior to
the final inspection, or if the applicant fails to obtain a certificate of
occupancy or certificate of completion as required by this chapter, or if the
building official determines that an applicant has failed to comply with the
provisions of this chapter, the codes adopted by this chapter, or other city
ordinances, the building official may issue a notice of building ordinance
violation, subject to the following provisions:
      1.   The building official shall prepare and mail, via certified mail, a
notice of building ordinance violation. The notification shall include:
         a.   The property owner and the legal description of the parcel.
         b.   The nature of the violation.
         c.   The remedial action that must be undertaken to resolve the
violation.
         d.   The length of time allotted to resolve the violation.
      2.   The property owner shall have forty five (45) days from the date the
notice is mailed to resolve the violation. If resolution does not occur within
those forty five (45) days, the notice of building ordinance violation shall be
filed in the county recorder's office and a copy mailed to the owner, via
certified mail.
      3.   The notice of building ordinance violation shall also advise the
owner of the appeal process. The city may consider a written appeal, submitted
by the property owner, and received no later than thirty (30) days after the
notice of building violation was mailed. The appeal shall be heard by the city
of Kamiah council on a date specified by city council. If the appeal is denied,
the board shall specify an exact number of days to gain compliance with the
ordinance before the notice of building violation is recorded. If the appeal is
approved, the city will specify actions to be taken by the building official to
release the violation. The city may elect to add or remove conditions of
remedial action.
      4.   At such time the building ordinance violation is resolved, the owner
shall pay the fee specified in the current adopted fee schedule and the
building official shall file in the office of the recorder a release of notice
of building ordinance violation. The release shall contain all of the
information contained in the notice of building ordinance violation, as well as
the corrective action taken to resolve the violation. A copy of the release
shall be mailed to the owner, via certified mail. (Ord. 2015-1, 2015: Ord.
2010-5 §13, 2010)
CHAPTER 15.08
ELECTRICAL CODE 1
SECTION:
15.08.010: Conformance Required
15.08.020: Municipality Not Responsible
15.08.030: Permit; Fee
 
Notes
1 1. IC ch. 54-10.
15.08.010: CONFORMANCE REQUIRED:
All electrical wiring, installation of electrical fixtures, apparatus, or
electrical appliances for furnishing light, heat or power or other electrical
work introduced or placed in or upon or in any way connected with any building
or structure within the municipal limits shall be in conformity with the
national electrical code as adopted by the Fire Protection Association in 1987
and all subsequent amendments thereto and any person desiring to do such work
shall secure a permit from the state of Idaho electrical board prior to such
work.
One copy of the current national electrical code shall be on file with the city
clerk in accordance with section 50-901 Idaho Code at all times and shall be
open to public inspection during office hours. (Ord. 98-9A(a), 1998: Ord. 89-
7 §§1, 2, 1989: Ord. 6-78, 1978: Ord. 5-74, 1974: prior code §4-301)
15.08.020: MUNICIPALITY NOT RESPONSIBLE:
This chapter shall not be construed to relieve from or lessen the
responsibility of any person owning, operating or installing any electric
wires, appliances, apparatus, construction or equipment for damages to anyone
injured or damaged either in person or property by any defect therein; nor
shall the municipality or any agent thereof be held as assuming such liability
by reason of inspection authorized herein or certificate of inspection issued
by the clerk. (Prior code §4-302)
15.08.030: PERMIT; FEE:
Any person may apply to the clerk for an electrical permit by furnishing
information required by the electrical inspector and by paying in advance a
permit fee of two dollars ($2.00). (Prior code §4-303)

15.12.010: ADOPTION:
There is adopted for the purposes of establishing minimum standards of design,
materials and workmanship for all plumbing hereafter installed, altered or
repaired and to establish methods of procedure within the limits of this
municipality, as provided by the uniform plumbing code, 1997 edition, and all
persons doing plumbing work or having the same done shall apply to the clerk
and submit a plan of plumbing in detail, and upon the approval thereof the
clerk shall issue a permit as provided in section
15.12.020 of this chapter.
The city clerk shall retain in her office open to public inspection one copy of
said code, which shall be in conformity with the requirements of Idaho Code
section 50-901, as amended. (Ord. 98-9A(a), 1998: Ord. 89-8 §§1, 2, 1989: Ord.
4-74, 1974: prior code §4-201)
15.12.020: PERMIT; FEE:
It is unlawful for any person to commence or to carry on the work of laying,
repairing, altering or connecting any sewer pipe with the public sewer, without
first having a permit issued by the clerk to do so. The permit fee shall be one
dollar ($1.00), payable to the clerk. (Prior code §4-202)
CHAPTER 15.16
TRAILERS AND TRAILER PARKS
SECTION:
15.16.010: Definitions
15.16.020: Parking Regulations
15.16.030: Permanent Occupancy
15.16.040: Zoning
15.16.050: Location To Be Well Drained And Graded
15.16.060: Units And Cabin Plots
15.16.070: Electric Service Outlet
15.16.080: Parking Area
15.16.090: Recreation Areas
15.16.100: Water Supply
15.16.110: Waste And Garbage Disposal
15.16.120: Applicability Of Plumbing, Electrical And Building Codes
15.16.130: Replacement Of Nonconforming Manufactured/Mobile Home
15.16.140: Administration And Enforcement
15.16.010: DEFINITIONS:
Whenever used in this chapter, unless a different meaning appears from the
context, the following meanings shall apply:
AUTOMOBILE TRAILER, TRAILER COACH, TRAILER OR MOBILE HOME: Any vehicle or
structure so designed and constructed in such manner as will permit occupancy
thereof as a dwelling or sleeping quarters for one or more persons, or the
conduct of any business or profession, occupation or trade, or use as a selling
or advertising device, and so designed that it is or may be mounted on wheels
and used as a conveyance on highways or City streets, propelled or drawn by its
own or other motive power, excepting a device used exclusively upon stationary
rails or tracks.
COMMERCIAL COACH: A modular building equipped with the necessary service
connections and made to be readily movable as a unit on its own running gear,
and originally designed to be used without a permanent foundation.
DEPARTMENTS: The City of Kamiah Building and Planning Department.
INDEPENDENT TRAILER COACH OR MOBILE HOME: Any vehicle which has a toilet, a
bathtub or shower.
MANUFACTURED HOME: A structure that:
   A.   Is constructed twenty five (25) years from the present date and
certified as meeting current manufactured home construction and safety
standards of the Department of Housing and Urban Development, and
   B.   Is transportable in one or more sections, and
   C.   When in the traveling mode, is eight (8) body feet or more in width or
is forty (40) body feet or more in length, or when erected on site, is three
hundred twenty (320) or more square feet, and
   D.   Is built on a permanent chassis and designed to be used as a dwelling
with or without a permanent foundation when connected to the required
utilities, and
   E.   Includes the plumbing, heating, air conditioning, and electrical
systems contained therein.
Such term shall also include any structure meeting all the requirements of this
definition except the size requirements, and with respect to which the
manufacturer voluntarily files a certification required by the Secretary of
Housing and Urban Development, and complies with the standards established
under 42 USC section 5401 et seq.
MOBILE HOME: A factory assembled structure or structures generally constructed
prior to twenty five (25) years from the present date and certified as meeting
current manufactured home construction and safety standards of the Department
of Housing and Urban Development, and equipped with the necessary service
connections and made so as to be readily movable as a unit or units on their
own running gear, and designed to be used as a dwelling unit or units with or
without a permanent foundation.
MODULAR BUILDING: Any building or building component, other than a manufactured
or mobile home, which is of closed construction and is either entirely or
substantially prefabricated or assembled at a place other than the building
site.
TOURIST CAMP: Any park, tourist park, camp, court, site, lot, parcel, or tract
of land upon which one or more camp cottages or cabins are located and
maintained for the accommodation of transients by the day, week, or month,
excluding motels, whether a charge is made or not.
TRAILER CAMP: Any park, trailer park, trailer court, court, camp, site, lot,
parcel, or tract of land designed, maintained or intended for the purpose of
supplying a location or accommodation for any trailer coach or mobile home, and
upon which any trailer coaches are parked and shall include all buildings used
or intended for use as a part of the equipment thereof whether a charge is made
for the use of the trailer camp and its facilities or not. "Trailer camp" does
not include automobile or trailer sales lots on which unoccupied trailers are
parked for the purpose of inspection and sale.
UNIT: A section of ground in a trailer camp of not less than one thousand eight
hundred (1,800) square feet of unoccupied space in an area designated as the
location for only one automobile and one trailer. (Ord. 2017-5, 2017)
15.16.020: PARKING REGULATIONS:
   A.   It is unlawful within the limits of the City for any person to park any
coach or trailer on any street, alley, or highway, or other public place, or on
any tract of land owned by persons, occupied or unoccupied, within the City,
except as provided in this chapter.
   B.   Emergency or temporary stopping or parking is permitted on any street,
alley or highway for not longer than four (4) hours subject to any other and
further prohibitions, regulations or limitations imposed by the traffic and
parking regulations for that street, alley or highway.
   C.   No person shall park or occupy any coach or trailer on the premises of
any occupied dwelling or on any lot which is not a part of the premises of any
occupied dwelling either of which is situated outside an approved trailer camp;
except, parking of only one (1) unoccupied coach or trailer in any accessory
private garage building, or in a rear yard in any district is permitted
providing no living quarters shall be maintained or any business practiced in
the coach or trailer while such coach or trailer is so parked or stored with
the exception that permits, not to exceed a two (2) week period, will be issued
to allow sleeping occupation of a coach or camper trailer parked on private
ground, at a charge of one dollar ($1.00) for each permit, issued by the Clerk.
A Variance Committee will be set up to handle the zoning problems for the
trailer courts. (Ord. 2020-02 §1, 2020; Ord. 2017-5, 2017)
15.16.030: PERMANENT OCCUPANCY:
Automobile trailer coaches shall not be used as a permanent place of abode or a
permanent dwelling or for indefinite periods of time; except as herein set
forth. Special permits for temporary occupancy of automobile trailer/coaches
may be granted when housing is destroyed in a natural disaster such as a fire
or flood. Such permits shall be issued by variance through Planning and Zoning.
(Ord. 2017-5, 2017)
15.16.040: ZONING:
   A.   No trailer or tourist camp shall be located within the limits of the
City unless City water and sewer connections and fire protection are available.
   B.   No occupied trailer or camp cottage or cabin cottage or cabin or other
building shall be located within the City limits within the recognized setback
line for the zoning district in which such trailer or cabin is located not less
than ten feet (10') from any other building or vehicle or the boundary line of
the tract on which located. (Ord. 2017-5, 2017)
15.16.050: LOCATION TO BE WELL DRAINED AND GRADED:
Every trailer or tourist camp shall be located on a well drained area, and the
premises shall be properly graded so as to prevent the accumulation of
stormwaters or other waters. (Ord. 2017-5, 2017)
15.16.060: UNITS AND CABIN PLOTS:
Units and cabin plots shall be clearly designated and the camp so arranged that
all units and cabin plots shall face upon a driveway of not less than sixteen
feet (16') in width, giving easy access from all units to a public street. Such
driveway shall be graveled and maintained in good condition, saving natural
drainage into a City street catch basin where possible, be well lighted at
night, and shall be unobstructed. (Ord. 2017-5, 2017)
15.16.070: ELECTRIC SERVICE OUTLET:
Every trailer unit shall be furnished with an electric service outlet. Such
outlet shall be equipped with an externally operated weatherproof utility
switch or fuse block of not less than sixty (60) to thirty (30) combination
amperes capacity, and a heavy duty and a duplex outlet receptacle contained
therein. (Ord. 2017-5, 2017)
15.16.080: PARKING AREA:
The parking area shall be the same as the number of trailer coach spaces. These
must be provided in special parking areas. (Ord. 2017-5, 2017)
15.16.090: RECREATION AREAS:
At least one hundred (100) square feet per trailer coach space must be made
available in one or more areas for recreational uses. These areas should be
located so as to be free of traffic hazards. (Ord. 2017-5, 2017)
15.16.100: WATER SUPPLY:
An adequate supply of pure water, furnished through a pipe distributed system
connected directly with the City water main, with supply faucets located not
more than two hundred feet (200') from any trailer or cabin, shall be furnished
for drinking and domestic purposes. (Ord. 2017-5, 2017)
15.16.110: WASTE AND GARBAGE DISPOSAL:
   A.   All waste from showers, toilets, laundries, faucets and lavatories
shall be wasted into a sewer system extended from and connected with the City
sewer system.
   B.   A system of sanitary sewerage shall be provided in all trailer courts,
and all waste and soil lines discharging from buildings and trailer coaches
shall be in accordance with local practices and be approved by local
administrative authorities having jurisdiction.
   C.   Each faucet site shall be equipped with facilities for drainage of
waste and excess water into the sewer. In no case shall any wastewater be
thrown or discharged upon the surface of the ground or disposed of by means
other than as provided in this chapter.
   D.   Every unit shall be provided with a substantial fly tight metal garbage
depository from which the contents shall be removed by the City garbage
collection service. (Ord. 2017-5, 2017)
15.16.120: APPLICABILITY OF PLUMBING, ELECTRICAL AND BUILDING CODES:
All plumbing, electrical, building and other work on or at any camp licensed
under this chapter shall be in accordance with the provisions of the Code
regulating such work unless the provisions are specifically made inapplicable
under the terms of this chapter. (Ord. 2017-5, 2017)
15.16.130: REPLACEMENT OF NONCONFORMING MANUFACTURED/MOBILE HOME:
   A.   Replace With Conforming Units: Nonconforming manufactured homes located
on individual lots which are removed from the property shall be replaced only
by conforming units.
   B.   Destruction Of Nonconforming Unit: If a nonconforming manufactured home
is destroyed by any cause to an extent exceeding fifty percent (50%) of fair
market value, as indicated by the records of the County Assessor, a future
structure or use on the site shall conform to this chapter.
   C.   Upgrading Of Nonconforming Units: An owner of a nonconforming unit must
show what upgrades and remodeling were done and have a certified property
inspector signed statement that the home has met safety standards as set by the
Department of Housing and Urban Development.
   D.   Conditional Use Permit: Once a certified property inspector- signed
statement is received verifying upgrades and remodeling, a conditional use
permit will be required. Conditional uses may be permitted by the commission
only after proper application, review approval and conditions of approval are
met. (Ord. 2017-5, 2017)
15.16.140: ADMINISTRATION AND ENFORCEMENT:
The building official, or his designee, shall be responsible for administering
and enforcing this chapter, the codes adopted by this chapter, and other
related City ordinances. The building official may establish procedures for
permit applications, plan checking, issuance of permits, as approved by
resolution of the City of Kamiah, for services associated with the
administration of replacement of nonconforming manufactured mobile home.
Pursuant to Idaho Code, any person who violates any provisions of this chapter
is guilty of a misdemeanor and upon conviction, shall be fined not more than
three hundred dollars ($300.00) or imprisoned for not more than ninety (90)
days, or both. Each day of an ongoing offense will be considered a separate
violation. (Ord. 2017-5, 2017)
CHAPTER 15.20
AIRPORT HANGARS
SECTION:
15.20.010: Permit Required; Lease
15.20.020: Permit Application
15.20.030: Location Of Hangars
15.20.040: Rental Fee
15.20.050: Condemnation Of Hangars; Notice
15.20.060: Livestock Prohibited Thereon
15.20.070: Power To Lease
15.20.080: Tie Down Rental Fee
15.20.090: Unlicensed Aircraft Fee; Storage; Airport Related Parking
15.20.100: Short Term Visitors; Fee Exemption
15.20.110: Police To Monitor Airport; Keep Records
15.20.120: Storage Lien
15.20.130: Storage Of Petroleum Fuels
15.20.140: Land Lease Fee
15.20.010: PERMIT REQUIRED; LEASE:
It is unlawful for any person, firm, or corporation to erect any hangar or
other building upon the Kamiah airport, owned by the city of Kamiah, Idaho,
without first having obtained a permit for such erection or construction, and
having also obtained a lease upon the space where the same is to be erected.
(Ord. 2013-3, 2013)
15.20.020: PERMIT APPLICATION:
All applications for a permit to build and erect a private hangar upon the
airport must be made to the city clerk of the city of Kamiah, in writing, the
same to specify the kind of materials to be used, the size of the hangar and a
general description of the type and construction and the location desired. All
such applications shall be approved by the mayor and by the city council before
being granted, and the application must be accompanied by the annual rental
fee. (Ord. 2013-3, 2013)
15.20.030: LOCATION OF HANGARS:
No hangars shall be located or constructed nearer than fifty feet (50') from
the main airstrip of the airport, and the right is reserved by the city to
designate the exact spaces where all hangars shall be constructed, and none
shall be erected except upon such designated spaces. (Ord. 2013-3, 2013)
15.20.040: RENTAL FEE:
The annual rental fee for each such hangar shall be determined by a resolution
of the city council, which shall be payable in advance each month in an amount
to be determined by resolution of the city council. (Ord. 2013-3, 2013)
15.20.050: CONDEMNATION OF HANGARS; NOTICE:
The city reserves the right to condemn any hangar built upon the airport not
built according to specifications and for which a permit has been issued, or
which is not kept in a good state of repair and appearance, and the city also
reserves the right and privilege of giving any owner written notice to repair,
recondition or remove any such hangar within thirty (30) days, and in the event
that compliance is not made with the notice, then the city may remove the same
without liability to the owner thereof, and this provision shall also apply for
the nonpayment of rentals. (Ord. 2013-3, 2013)
15.20.060: LIVESTOCK PROHIBITED THEREON:
It is unlawful for any livestock of any kind attended or unattended to be
allowed on the airport. (Ord. 2013-3, 2013)
15.20.070: POWER TO LEASE:
There is vested in the city council the power to lease any and all of the
facilities of the Kamiah airport to competent persons, partnerships, or
corporations upon such terms and conditions for such periods of time as the
council shall deem to be reasonable. (Ord. 2013-3, 2013)
15.20.080: TIE DOWN RENTAL FEE:
There is hereby imposed a tie down rental fee in an amount to be determined by
a resolution of the city council per month for each licensed aircraft that is
tied down on the Kamiah Municipal Airport. Tie down fees shall either be paid
monthly at a monthly rate in an amount to be determined by a resolution of the
council, or annually at a rate in an amount to be determined by a resolution of
the city council per year payment. Payments shall be made through the city
clerk's office, and the clerk shall be authorized to issue receipts for
payment. Rental shall be due in advance and paid at the beginning of each month
for the next succeeding month, or in advance for an entire year following
payment of the yearly fee. Any changes or amendments to such tie down rental
fee may be made and fixed by council resolution. (Ord. 2013-3, 2013)
15.20.090: UNLICENSED AIRCRAFT FEE; STORAGE; AIRPORT RELATED PARKING:
Unlicensed aircraft shall likewise pay a fee as set forth in section
15.20.080 of this chapter, but shall not be permitted to use the main tie down
area on the Kamiah Municipal Airport, but shall locate their aircraft in the
storage area on the north side of the storage hangar of said airport. Any
changes or amendments to such unlicensed aircraft fee may be made and fixed by
city council resolution.
The Kamiah city council shall designate a parking area at the airport for
airport related parking only. There shall be a daily, weekly and monthly fee
for said parking which shall be set by resolution of the Kamiah city council.
(Ord. 2013-3, 2013)
15.20.100: SHORT TERM VISITORS; FEE EXEMPTION:
There shall be no fee for short term visitors or vacationers, it being
specified that a short term visitor is one who would be on the airport for less
than ten (10) consecutive days. (Ord. 2013-3, 2013)
15.20.110: POLICE TO MONITOR AIRPORT; KEEP RECORDS:
The city police are hereby authorized to monitor the use of the Kamiah
Municipal Airport to keep records of the use of the airport, and to report to
the city clerk information concerning all persons not complying with the terms
of this chapter. (Ord. 2013-3, 2013)
15.20.120: STORAGE LIEN:
In the event that an airplane owner would fail to pay the tie down fees set
forth herein for two (2) consecutive months, the city shall have the right to
collect its funds either through the small claims court of any court having
jurisdiction of the parties, or may claim the storage lien provided in Idaho
Code section 45-805, and proceed to foreclose its lien for storage under that
section of the Idaho Code, and at the same time retain possession of the
aircraft until its claim has been satisfied. (Ord. 2013-3, 2013)
15.20.130: STORAGE OF PETROLEUM FUELS:
The tie down rental set forth in this chapter shall not include the right to
store petroleum fuels on the Kamiah Municipal Airport. Fuels shall be
transported to aircraft when refueling is necessary, and then removed to a safe
and authorized place, pursuant to appropriate fuel regulations. (Ord. 2013-3,
2013)
15.20.140: LAND LEASE FEE:
The annual land lease fee shall be fixed by resolution of the city council,
which fee shall be payable in advance each month or annually in an amount to be
determined by resolution of the city council. (Ord. 2013-3, 2013)
CHAPTER 15.24
FLOOD HAZARD AREAS
