development. However, this title shall not apply to any of the following:
   A.   The sale or exchange of land between adjoining property owners, or an
adjustment of lot or property lines, where such sale, exchange or adjustment
does not create additional lots, shall not be deemed a subdivision.
   B.   An allocation of land in the settlement of an estate or a court decree
for the distribution of property.
   C.   The unwilling sale of land as a result of legal condemnation as defined
and allowed in the Idaho Code.
   D.   Widening of existing streets to conform to the Kamiah comprehensive
plan.
   E.   The acquisition of street rights of way by a public agency in
conformance with the Kamiah comprehensive plan.
   F.   The exchange of land for the purpose of straightening property
boundaries which does not result in the change of present land usage.
SURVEYOR: Any person who is licensed in the state as a public land surveyor to
do professional surveying.
TECHNICAL REVIEW COMMITTEE: The technical review committee, appointed by the
city council, to assist with the technical evaluation of subdivisions, and to
make recommendations to the commission. The membership of the committee shall
include, but not be limited to, persons that are engaged in either private or
public work with specific knowledge in the following areas:
   A.   Road design and construction.
   B.   Sewer and water facility design and construction.
   C.   Health requirements for water and sewer facilities.
   D.   Environmental planning criteria such as: geology, water systems,
vegetation, noise, etc.
   E.   Solid waste.
   F.   Recreational and open space.
USABLE LOT AREA: That portion of a lot usable for residential construction use,
excluding areas which are covered by water, excessively steep, or are included
in certain types of easements.
UTILITIES: Installations for conducting water, sewage, gas, electricity,
television, storm water and similar facilities providing service to and used by
the public.
VARIANCE: A modification of the strict terms of the relevant regulations where
such modification will not be contrary to the public interest and where, owing
to conditions peculiar to the property and not the result of this action of the
applicant, a literal enforcement of this title would result in unnecessary and
undue hardship.
VICINITY MAP: A small scale map showing the location of a tract of land in
relation to a larger area. (Ord. 2001-5 Art. II §2, 2001)
CHAPTER 16A.12
PROCEDURE FOR SUBDIVISION APPROVAL
SECTION:
16A.12.010: Subdivision Approval Required
16A.12.020: Land Held In Joint Ownership
16A.12.030: Preapplication
16A.12.040: Simple Subdivision Procedure
16A.12.050: Preliminary Plat
16A.12.060: Amended Subdivision Plat
16A.12.070: Final Plat
16A.12.080: Combined Plat Procedure
16A.12.010: SUBDIVISION APPROVAL REQUIRED:
No part of a proposed simple subdivision shall have been previously processed
under the simple subdivision regulations within the past ten (10) years and a
simple subdivision shall not be granted within the boundaries of a previously
recorded platted subdivision.
Any person desiring to create a "subdivision" as herein defined shall submit
all required applications to the administrator. No final plat shall be filed
with the county recorder or improvements made on the property until the plat
has been acted upon by the commission and approved by the city council. No lots
shall be sold until the plat has been recorded in the office of the county
recorder and accepted by the county assessor. (Ord. 2001-5 Art. III §1, 2001)
16A.12.020: LAND HELD IN JOINT OWNERSHIP:
Property held by two (2) or more owners with undivided interests shall be
considered a single ownership and any subdivision of that property to divide
interests or separate ownership shall be subject to the same subdivision
standards as are provided for property held by a single owner. (Ord. 2001-
5 Art. III §2, 2001)
16A.12.030: PREAPPLICATION:
   A.   Application: The subdivider shall submit a completed preapplication to
enable the administrator to review and comment on the proposed subdivision.
      1.   The preapplication shall include:
         a.   A completed application form.
         b.   Vicinity map, which may be a freehand pencil sketch showing the
relationship of the proposed subdivision to existing community facilities, and
other developments which serve or influence it.
         c.   Sketch plan, which may be a freehand pencil sketch made directly
on a print of a topographic survey and which shall describe in simple form, the
proposed layout of streets, lots and other features in relation to existing
conditions.
         d.   Map details, showing the development name, if any, and location,
highways and roads, features of terrain such as rock outcrops, tree masses, and
watercourses on and adjacent to the proposed subdivision, scale, north arrow,
date, perimeter boundary line of proposed subdivision, existing and proposed
public utilities, sanitary sewer facilities and railroads, if any.
A preapplication conference will be held before the planning and zoning
commission. The purpose of the conference is to discuss the proposed
subdivision concept, its conformity with the comprehensive plan, its
relationship to surrounding development, any site conditions that may require
special consideration or treatment, and the requirements of the subdivision
ordinance, zoning and development ordinance and other county ordinances.
At the preapplication conference, the applicant will receive a preapplication
conference checklist of items required to be submitted with the subdivision
application and preliminary plat, as well as notes of major concerns expressed
in the conference.
   B.   Fee: None required.
   C.   Administrator Action: The administrator shall check the preapplication
for its general conformance or nonconformance with this title and place the
preapplication conference on the commission agenda for action at the next
regularly scheduled meeting. At the commission meeting, the commission members
shall be polled so the developer can have the benefit of their comments. If the
developer chooses to proceed, the administrator will provide the necessary
forms and checklists for the following steps to the developer.
   D.   Time Limitation: A completed preliminary plat and application must be
submitted to the administrator within six (6) months after the preapplication
conference. (Ord. 2001-5 Art. III §3, 2001)
16A.12.040: SIMPLE SUBDIVISION PROCEDURE:
The purpose of the simple subdivision regulation is to provide a simplified and
abbreviated procedure for the platting of small and uncomplicated subdivisions.
It may be used when the proposed subdivision will consist of not more than four
(4) parts total.
After a simple subdivision application is filed, adjacent land in the same
ownership must follow the regular platting procedure if they are to be
subdivided, and must include lots already subdivided to indicate how all lots
fit into the original parcel.
Land may be subdivided under the simple subdivision regulations provided that
no part of said proposed subdivision shall have been previously processed under
the simple subdivision regulations within the past ten (10) years. Simple
subdivisions shall not be granted within the boundaries of a previously
recorded plat.
New roads or easement access within the subdivision must meet the minimum
design standards set forth in this title in addition to standards adopted by
the highway district. New roads rights of way shall be dedicated to public use.
   A.   Application: The subdivider shall file with the administrator a
completed subdivision permit application, required fees and supporting data as
required, at least fifteen (15) days prior to the commission meeting where the
application for simple subdivision will be considered.
      1.   Required Supporting Data:
         a.   Sketch Plan: A sketch plan, legal description and a vicinity map
showing the relationship of the proposed subdivision to the surrounding area
extending one-half (1/2) mile minimum from subdivision boundaries.
         b.   Written Statement: A written statement that the proposed source
of water meets state of Idaho water quality standards for a public water
supply; or, if no source of water is proposed, a written statement that there
is no known or proposed source of water on the land being subdivided.
         c.   Adjoining Property Owners: The name and address of each adjoining
property owner, whether or not separated by a public right of way, as shown in
the county assessor's records.
         d.   Hillside Subdivisions: For hillside subdivisions, the information
specified in section 16A.32.030 of this title.
         e.   Agency Review: The administrator will transmit one copy of the
application and supporting data to the departments and agencies having
jurisdiction or interest in the development for review and comment. Such
departments and agencies shall have fifteen (15) days from the date of document
transmission within which to provide their written response. Permits required
by other agencies shall be a condition of the subdivision permit. No
subdivision permit will be issued until required agency permits are received.
Failure to receive jurisdiction response shall not be the basis for denying
plat approval.
   B.   Administrator Action: Upon the determination that the proposed
subdivision is in compliance with the requirements of this title, land use or
zoning ordinance and comprehensive plan, the administrator shall place the
application on the commission agenda for action at the next regularly scheduled
meeting. The administrator shall refer the simple subdivision application to as
many agencies as deemed necessary.
   C.   Hearing Procedures: The commission will hold a public hearing of the
application, supporting data, the report of the administrator and any comments
on the proposed subdivision received from other public agencies. The commission
may request review by any qualified professional person, and may conduct, or
cause to be conducted, investigations, tests and site evaluations as it deems
necessary to verify the information contained in the application or shown on
the plat. The applicant grants the commission or its agent permission to enter
upon the land in question for these purposes by virtue of the subdivision
application.
Within forty five (45) days after the public hearing, the commission will
approve, approve subject to modifications as it deems necessary, or deny the
application. If conditions are placed on a simple subdivision approval, all
conditions must be met within one year of the original public hearing. Approved
applications shall be referred to the board for review and final approval.
   D.   Commission's Findings: In determining the acceptance of a proposed
simple subdivision, the commission shall consider the standards set forth in
this title and at least the following:
      1.   Conformance of the subdivision with the comprehensive plan.
      2.   Availability of public services to accommodate the proposed
development.
      3.   Public financial capability of supporting services for the proposed
development.
      4.   Other health, safety or environmental problems that may be brought
to the commission's attention.
If simple subdivision approval is denied, the applicant will be provided with a
written statement from the administrator containing the specific reasons for
denial. The applicant may reapply for simple subdivision approval provided that
all deficiencies that caused the original application to be denied have been
substantially corrected.
   E.   City Council Action: After approval by the commission, the simple
subdivision application will be scheduled for action by the city council at its
next available meeting date. The city council will review the recommendation of
the commission and comments from the concerned persons and agencies. Within
thirty (30) days of the date of the city council meeting at which the simple
subdivision application is first considered, the city council shall approve,
approve conditionally, disapprove or table the simple subdivision for
additional information.
   F.   Compliance With Ordinance: Application for a simple subdivision shall
be considered acknowledgment by the applicant that the proposed subdivision
will comply with the design standards and all other relevant provisions of the
Kamiah city subdivision ordinance.
   G.   Fee: The simple subdivision application fee as established by the city
council shall be paid by the subdivider to the administrator. Proof of such
payment shall be submitted prior to the plat being placed on the agenda for the
commission meeting.
   H.   Appeals: The subdivider, or any other person or aggrieved party who
appeared in person or writing before the commission may appeal the commission's
decision by submitting said appeal in writing to the Kamiah city council within
fifteen (15) days from such commission action. (Ord. 2001-5 Art. III §4, 2001)
16A.12.050: PRELIMINARY PLAT:
   A.   Preliminary Plat Application: The subdivider shall file with the
administrator a completed subdivision permit application, preapplication
conference checklist, the preliminary plat checklist, together with the
required fees, at least fifteen (15) days prior to the commission meeting where
the application will be considered.
The applicant must submit all items on the checklists with the application.
Should items be found to be missing or deficient, the application will be
withdrawn from scheduling until the required information is submitted.
The application for a preliminary plat shall be made on forms supplied by the
Kamiah planning department office, and shall contain the following information:
      1.   The name of the proposed subdivision;
      2.   The names, addresses and telephone numbers of the subdivider(s) and
the engineer or surveyor who prepared the plat;
      3.   The name and address of each adjoining property owner, whether or
not separated by a public right of way, as shown in county assessor's records;
      4.   The legal description of the subdivision;
      5.   A statement of the intended use of the proposed subdivision, such as
single-family residential, two-family or multiple-family housing; commercial;
or industrial; recreational/agricultural; sites for parks; playgrounds;
schools; churches;
      6.   The land use and existing zoning of the proposed subdivision and the
surrounding land;
      7.   A copy of any proposed restrictive covenants and/or deed
restrictions, which will appear on the final plat, and which must appear on the
final plat prior to approval and recommendations;
      8.   Any dedications to the public and/or easements, together with a
statement of location, dimensions and purpose of such;
      9.   A statement as to whether or not a variance will be requested with
respect to any provision of this title;
      10.   Appropriate information that sufficiently details the proposed
development within any special development area, such as a floodplain;
      11.   A written description of the proposed development, including:
         a.   Type of water system to be used including information on main
size and pressure and, if public, the excess capacity available from such
public system; the nearest main, and the estimated water demand of the
development or buildings;
         b.   Type of sewage treatment system to be used and, if public, the
existing excess capacity available from such public system; the nearest
location to the building site of a trunk or connecting sewer line; and the
expected demand of the development or buildings;
         c.   Type of drainage system proposed to handle surface, underground
and runoff waters;
         d.   Type of fire protection systems to be used (such as hydrants, wet
standpipes, etc.); distance to the nearest fire station and its average
response time;
         e.   Total development area; type of housing or development proposed;
number of units including employee housing; the distance from proposed
development to the nearest elementary and secondary schools; the distance to
existing school bus routes;
         f.   Estimated traffic count increase on adjacent streets resulting
from the proposed development; description of type and condition of roads to
serve such development; total number of motor vehicles expected to use or be
stationed in such development; hours of principal daily usage of adjacent
roads; on site and off site parking to be supplied; location of alternate
transit means (bus routes, bike paths, etc.); any auto disincentive techniques
incorporated in such proposed development;
         g.   Location relative to proposed or existing parks, playgrounds,
hospitals, airports, mass transit systems and estimated increased usage of such
facilities by reason of the proposed development;
         h.   Location relative to the proposed development of police
facilities, and their average response time; estimate of additional police
personnel needed by reason of the proposed development;
         i.   Location relative to proposed development of retail and service
outlets by reason of the proposed development;
         j.   Effects of proposed development on adjacent land and land uses in
the vicinity of the project; and
         k.   The proposed construction schedule, including, if applicable, a
schedule for phased construction.
   B.   Form Of Contents Of Preliminary Plat: The contents of the preliminary
plat and related information shall be in such a form as required by the
commission; however, additional maps or data deemed necessary by the
administrator may also be required. The subdivider shall submit to the
administrator at least the following:
      1.   Eight (8) copies of the preliminary plat of the proposed
subdivision, drawn in accordance with the requirements hereinafter stated; each
copy of the preliminary plat shall be on good quality paper, shall have
dimensions of not less than twenty four inches by thirty six inches (24" x
36"), shall be drawn to a scale of not less than one inch to one hundred feet
(1" = 100'), shall show the drafting date, and shall indicate thereon, by
arrow, the generally northerly direction; and
      2.   Eight (8) sets of preliminary engineering plans (not meant to be
cross sections or detailed designs) for streets, water, sewers, sidewalks,
other required public improvements and private roads; however, such engineering
plans shall contain sufficient information and detail to enable the
administrator to make a determination as to the conformance of the proposed
improvements to applicable regulations, ordinances and standards.
   C.   Requirements Of Preliminary Plats: The following shall be shown on the
preliminary plat:
      1.   A map of the entire area scheduled for development if the proposed
subdivision is a portion of a larger holding intended for subsequent stages of
development;
      2.   A vicinity map showing the relationship of the proposed plat to the
surrounding area (1/4 mile minimum radius, scale optional);
      3.   A site utilization map including:
         a.   Proposed methods of preserving natural terrain and open space,
and undergrounding of utilities;
         b.   Motor vehicle circulation, parking, bus and transit stops and
improvements proposed to ensure privacy from such areas;
         c.   Any major street or road links, school sites, pathways, foot,
bicycle or equestrian trails and greenbelts;
         d.   General description and location of surrounding existing land
uses and identifications of zone boundary lines, if any;
         e.   A showing of any sites proposed for parks, playgrounds, schools,
churches or other public uses.
      4.   Streets, street names, private roads, private road names, right of
way and roadway widths, including adjoining streets or roadways;
      5.   Lot lines and blocks showing the dimensions, areas and numbers of
each;
      6.   Contour lines, shown at five foot (5') intervals for suburban
subdivisions or not more than two feet (2') in areas susceptible to a 100-year
flood;
      7.   Any proposed or existing utilities, including, but not limited to,
storm and sanitary sewers, irrigation laterals, ditches, drainages, bridges,
culverts, water mains and fire hydrants, telephone, TV, and electric cables.
   D.   Administrator Action: Upon the determination that the proposed
subdivision is in compliance with the requirements of this title, zoning
ordinance and comprehensive plan, the administrator shall place the application
on the commission agenda for action at the next regularly scheduled meeting.
The administrator shall refer the preliminary plat application to as many
agencies as deemed necessary.
   E.   Public Notification:
      1.   Notification Of Property Owners: The subdivider shall notify all
adjoining property owners within three hundred feet (300') of the proposed
subdivision, of his intent and the time and place of hearing by the commission
at least fifteen (15) days prior to the hearing date by certified mail. Proof
of said notification shall be presented to the commission at the time the
developer presents his preliminary plat.
      2.   Failure To Notify: The subdivider's failure to comply with the
notification provision shall not invalidate the commission's action, provided
the spirit of the procedure is observed.
   F.   Commission Action: The commission will hold a public hearing of the
application, the preliminary plat, the report of the administrator and any
comments on the proposed subdivision received from other public agencies. The
commission may request investigations, examinations, tests and site evaluations
as it deems necessary to verify the information contained in the application or
shown on the plat. The applicant grants the commission or its agent permission
to enter upon the land in question for these purposes by virtue of the
subdivision application.
Within forty five (45) days after the public hearing, the commission will
approve, approve subject to modifications as it deems necessary, or deny the
application. If conditions are placed on preliminary plat approval, all
conditions must be met within one year of original preliminary plat hearing.
If the preliminary plat approval is denied, the applicant will be provided with
a written statement from the administrator containing the specific reasons for
the denial. The applicant may reapply for preliminary plat approval provided
that all deficiencies that caused the original application to be denied have
been substantially corrected.
   G.   Review Agencies: The administrator shall transmit one copy of the
preliminary plat, or other documents submitted, for review and recommendation
to the pertinent departments and agencies.
   H.   Appeals: Any person who appeared in person or writing before the
commission may appeal in writing the decision of the commission relative to the
final action taken by the commission. Such appeal must be submitted to the city
council within fifteen (15) days from such commission action.
   I.   Commission's Findings: In determining the acceptance of a proposed
subdivision, the commission shall consider the standards set forth in this
title and at least the following:
      1.   Conformance of the subdivision with the comprehensive plan.
      2.   Availability of public services to accommodate the proposed
development.
      3.   Public financial capability of supporting services for the proposed
development.
      4.   Other health, safety or environmental problems that may be brought
to the commission's attention.
      5.   The preliminary plat shall be submitted to the commission for
approval, conditional approval, disapproval or tabled for additional
information. Approved preliminary plats shall be referred to the city council
for review and final approval.
         a.   City Council Action: After approval by the commission, the
preliminary plat will be scheduled for action by the city council at its next
available meeting date. The city council will review the recommendation of the
commission and comments from the concerned persons and agencies. The city
council finding the plat to be in order shall approve, approve conditionally,
disapprove or table the preliminary plat for additional information within
thirty (30) days of the date of the regular city council meeting at which the
preliminary plat is first considered.
         b.   Fee: The preliminary plat application fee as established by the
city council of two hundred fifty dollars ($250.00) plus ten dollars ($10.00)
per lot shall be paid by the subdivider to the administrator. Proof of such
payment shall be submitted prior to the plat being placed on the agenda for the
commission meeting. (Ord. 2001-5 Art. III §5, 2001)
16A.12.060: AMENDED SUBDIVISION PLAT:
An amended plat is required to effect a change in the configuration of any part
of a recorded subdivision plat. An amended plat requires at least partial
vacation of a recorded subdivision plat and may include vacation of an entire
plat. The administrator shall determine the nature of the required vacation.
If the new plat appears to be a simple design change with no apparent impacts,
then the new plat may be accepted as a final plat and shall follow final plat
procedures. If the proposed new plat has major changes which create new impacts
on roads, water, sewer, easements or neighboring properties, then the new plat
shall comply with the procedures described above as required by the
administrator. This may be all steps, including the preapplication conference.
   A.   Fee: The amended subdivision application fee as established by the city
council shall be paid by the subdivider to the administrator. Proof of such
payment shall be submitted prior to the plat being placed on the agenda for the
commission meeting. (Ord. 2001-5 Art. III §6, 2001)
16A.12.070: FINAL PLAT:
   A.   Final Plat Submittal: A final plat must conform to an approved
preliminary plat. If a preliminary plat is approved with conditions, the final
plat submittal must satisfy those conditions.
The final plat, fees and all required accompanying material shall be filed with
the administrator at least fifteen (15) days prior to the planning and zoning
commission meeting where the final plat will be considered.
The applicant must submit all items on the final plat checklist. Should items
noted as submitted be found to be missing or deficient, the final plat will be
withdrawn from scheduling until the required information is submitted.
   B.   Mylar Submittal: The subdivider will submit two (2) reproducible copies
of the final plat and when applicable, two (2) copies of the final engineering
construction drawings for streets, water, sewers, sidewalks and other public
improvements, one of which, shall be a reproducible Mylar copy.
   C.   Content Of Final Plat: The final plat shall include and be in
compliance with all items required under title 50, chapter 13, of the Idaho
Code and shall be drawn at such a scale and contain lettering of such size as
to enable the same to be placed on one sheet of eighteen inch by twenty four
inch (18" x 24") drawing paper, with no part of the drawing nearer to the edge
than one inch (1"). The reverse of said sheet shall not be used for any portion
of the drawing, but may contain written matter as to dedications,
certifications and other information. The final plat shall include at least the
following:
      1.   A written application for approval of such final plat as stipulated
by the planning and zoning commission;
      2.   Proof of current ownership of the real property included in the
proposed final plat;
      3.   Such other and further information as the planning and zoning
commission may deem necessary to establish whether or not all proper parties
have signed and/or approved said final plat;
      4.   Conformance with the approved preliminary plat and meeting all
requirements or conditions thereof;
      5.   Conform to all requirements and provisions of this title; and
      6.   Acceptable engineering practices and local standards.
In addition to the above items, the plat shall show the following:
      7.   The outline of any property, other than streets or alleys, which is
offered for dedication to public use, fully dimensioned by lengths and
bearings, with the area marked "Public" and showing the proposed site;
      8.   A title which shall include the name of the subdivision, name of
city, if appropriate, county and state, and the location and description of the
subdivision referenced to quarter-quarter section, section, township and range;
      9.   Scale, north arrow and the date;
      10.   Certification and signature by the registered engineer or surveyor
who prepared the plat certifying to the accuracy of the survey and plat; and to
the maximum percentage of grade of all streets and roads;
      11.   Certification of owner, including dedication of all street rights
of way and sites for public use, and grants of any existing or proposed
easements;
      12.   All covenants, and deed restrictions required by the city council
and the planning and zoning commission for final plat approval;
      13.   Certification and signature of the Lewis County clerk/recorder
verifying that all required bonds of the subdivider have been properly filed;
      14.   Certification and signature of the chairman of the Kamiah planning
and zoning commission, verifying the commission's approval;
      15.   Certification and signature of the city clerk, if required by an
ordinance or the Idaho Code, verifying that the subdivision meets the city
requirements and has been approved by the city council;
      16.   Certification and signature of the chairman of the overlaying
highway district verifying that the subdivision plat has been accepted by the
district and meets highway district standards;
      17.   Certification and signature of the Lewis County treasurer,
verifying that all tax liens against the property within the plat have been
duly paid;
      18.   Certification and signature of the mayor of Kamiah verifying the
city council's approval;
      19.   Certification and signature of the city engineer verifying the
accuracy and completeness of the survey data contained in the final plat;
      20.   A duly acknowledged certification by a representative of the city
of Kamiah or the state board of health that there have been approved plans and
specifications for either public water and/or public sewer facilities or
individual water and/or sewage facilities for the particular land. The owner
shall have the obligation of submitting to the city of Kamiah or the state
board of health all information necessary concerning the condition of the
property, and the plans and specifications proposed for the facilities referred
to. Until the sanitary restrictions have been satisfied by the filing of said
certificate, no owner shall construct any building or shelter on said premises
which necessitates the supplying of water or sewer facilities for persons using
such premises.
   D.   Review Agencies: The administrator shall transmit one copy of the final
plat, or other documents submitted, for review and recommendations to the
departments and agencies as he deems necessary to ensure compliance with the
preliminary approval and/or conditions of preliminary approval. Such agency
review shall also include the construction standards of improvements,
compliance with health standards, the cost estimate for all improvements and
the legal review of the performance bond.
   E.   Administrator Action: Upon determination that the final plat and all
required material has been submitted and conforms with the approved preliminary
plat, the administrator shall place the application on the commission agenda
for action at the next regularly scheduled meeting.
   F.   Planning And Zoning Commission Action: If the commission finds that the
plat conforms to the approved preliminary plat, and complies with all
requirements of the subdivision ordinance and other applicable regulations,
then it shall refer the final plat to the city council with a recommendation
for approval.
   G.   City Council Action: After approval by the commission, the final plat
will be scheduled for action by the city council at its next available meeting
date. The city council will review the recommendation of the commission and
comments from the concerned persons and agencies. The city council finding the
final plat to be in order shall approve, approve conditionally, disapprove or
table the final plat for additional information within thirty (30) days of the
date of the regular city council meeting at which the plat is first considered.
   H.   Fee: The final plat is two hundred fifty dollars ($250.00) plus ten
dollars ($10.00) per lot, plus an administrative fee of twenty five dollars
($25.00) per hour and professional fees as determined by the Kamiah city
council to recover costs incurred by the city as a result of processing the
subdivision request.
   I.   Approval Period: Final plat shall be filed with the county clerk/
recorder within fifteen (15) months after written approval by the city council;
otherwise, such approval shall become null and void unless prior to such
expiration date an extension of time is granted by the city council.
A subdivision permit is issued upon signature and recordation of the final
plat. A subdivision permit lapses and becomes null and void one year following
the date on which it was issued, unless one of the following is true:
      1.   The bonding mechanism approved by the city sets a longer time
period;
      2.   Prior to the expiration date, construction of required improvements
has been commenced and diligently pursued to completion;
      3.   The city council approves an extension prior to the expiration date
and just cause is shown for the requested extension.
      4.   Also, the city council may revoke a subdivision permit upon failure
to comply with the conditions of approval of a final plat, upon violation of
any of the provisions of the subdivision ordinance, or for misrepresentations
or material omissions made to the planning and zoning commission.
   J.   Recording The Final Plat: Following approval of the final plat by the
city council, the subdivider shall file the approved plat with the county
recorder. At the time the plat is recorded, the subdivider shall:
      1.   Prepay fees or post a surety bond for construction of improvements.
      2.   Pay all property taxes due.
      3.   Pay the fee for recording as established by Idaho Code. (Ord. 2001-
5 Art. III §7, 2001)
16A.12.080: COMBINED PLAT PROCEDURE:
   A.   Requirements: The developer may request that a subdivision application
be processed as both a preliminary plat and a final plat (combined plat) if all
the following exist:
      1.   The proposed subdivision does not exceed ten (10) lots.
      2.   No major development considerations are involved such as development
in a floodplain, planned unit development, large scale development, or the
like; and
      3.   All required information for both preliminary and final plat is
complete and in acceptable final plat form.
   B.   Consideration: A request to process the subdivision under the combined
plat procedure shall be considered by the commission at its next regularly
scheduled meeting following application. Applications shall be received by the
administrator at least fifteen (15) days prior to commission meeting where the
application will be considered.
   C.   Commission Action And Procedure: If the commission grants the
developer's request for the subdivision to be processed as a combined plat, the
preliminary plat procedure shall be followed. Recommendation shall be made to
the city council following the public hearing as specified for a final plat.
(Ord. 2001-5 Art. III §8, 2001)
CHAPTER 16A.16
GENERAL DESIGN STANDARDS
SECTION:
16A.16.010: General Standards For All Subdivisions
16A.16.020: Easement Requirements For All Subdivisions
16A.16.010: GENERAL STANDARDS FOR ALL SUBDIVISIONS:
All plats submitted pursuant to the provisions of this title, and all
subdivisions, improvements and facilities done, constructed or made in
accordance with said provisions shall comply with the minimum design standards
set forth hereinafter in this section; provided however, that any higher
standards adopted by any highway district or state agency shall prevail over
those set forth herein.
In order to ensure the reasonable and beneficial development of land within the
jurisdiction of this title, the commission and city council shall give full
consideration to the following:
   A.   Comprehensive Plan: The intent and design of the proposed plat shall be
in accordance with the provisions of the city of Kamiah comprehensive plan.
   B.   Frontage Roads: Where a subdivision abuts or contains an arterial
street, there shall be frontage roads approximately parallel to and on each
side of such arterial street; or such other treatment as is necessary for the
adequate protection of residential properties and to separate through traffic
from local traffic.
   C.   Addressing: Streets within a subdivision shall be named and each lot
addressed as required by the city of Kamiah road naming and addressing
ordinance.
   D.   Dedications: Within a proposed subdivision, arterial and collector
streets shall be dedicated to the public in all cases; in general, all other
streets shall also be dedicated to public use.
   E.   Preservation: Design and development of subdivisions shall preserve,
insofar as possible, the natural terrain, natural drainage, existing topsoil
and trees. The design shall, insofar as possible, provide for or preserve solar
access.
   F.   Hazards: Land which has been determined to be subject to hazardous
conditions such as flood threats, poor drainage, steep slopes, no potable water
supply, or other features likely to be harmful to the safety and general health
of the future residents, shall be subdivided until the hazards have been
eliminated; or until plans for their elimination are approved by the health
department and/or the commission.
   G.   Central Water System: Any central water system shall be adequate in
size and capacity to fully provide for the proposed population of the
subdivision.
   H.   Sewage Treatment And Drainage Systems: Any sewage treatment and
drainage systems shall be adequate in size and capacity to fully provide for
the proposed population; and shall be suitable for the type of soil they are to
be located in and the surrounding terrain of the proposed subdivision.
   I.   Fire Hydrants And Water Mains: Adequate fire protection shall be
required in accordance with the city standards.
   J.   Impact: Full consideration shall be given to the impact of the proposed
subdivision on adjacent uses and land uses in the vicinity of the proposed
subdivision.
   K.   Impact On Community Services: Full consideration shall be given to the
impact of the proposed subdivision on the local economy, schools, parks and
other community services.
   L.   Road Development: Full consideration shall be given to the estimated
cost of road development and expansion resulting from the proposed subdivision.
(Ord. 2001-5 Art. IV §1, 2001)
16A.16.020: EASEMENT REQUIREMENTS FOR ALL SUBDIVISIONS:
Easements shall be provided wherever required for utilities or other public
services, of such size and location as approved by the city council.
   A.   Unobstructed utility easements shall be provided along front lot lines,
rear lot lines, and side lot lines when deemed necessary; total easement width
shall not be less than twelve feet (12').
   B.   Where a subdivision contains a watercourse, drainageway, channel or
stream, an easement may be provided adequate to contain said watercourse and
such further width as necessary for maintenance and/or reconstruction
operations.
   C.   As provided for by section 55-615, Idaho Code, opportunities for solar
access may be retained by easements granted to each lot. Such easements may be
required as a condition of plat approval in order to protect existing
neighboring uses. (Ord. 2001-5 Art. IV §2, 2001)
CHAPTER 16A.20
IMPROVEMENT STANDARDS FOR SUBDIVISIONS
SECTION:
16A.20.010: Construction Drawings
16A.20.020: Plans
16A.20.030: Financial Guarantee Arrangements
16A.20.040: Inspection Of Public Improvements
16A.20.050: As Built Plans Required
16A.20.060: Agency Certification
16A.20.070: Failure To Complete Public Improvement
16A.20.010: CONSTRUCTION DRAWINGS:
The subdivider shall provide the administrator with approved construction
drawings for all improvements in the subdivision, which drawings shall bear the
approval of the appropriate agency or district. (Ord. 2001-5 Art. V §1, 2001)
16A.20.020: PLANS:
Plans for the improvement herein required shall be prepared by an engineer
registered in the state of Idaho. (Ord. 2001-5 Art. V §2, 2001)
16A.20.030: FINANCIAL GUARANTEE ARRANGEMENTS:
Prior to sale of lots within the subdivision, the subdivider shall have
previously constructed all required improvements and secured a certificate of
completion from the appropriate agencies, or shall provide a financial
guarantee of performance acceptable to the council in one or a combination of
the following arrangements for those requirements which are over and beyond the
requirements of any other agency responsible for the administration, operation
and maintenance of the applicable public improvement:
   A.   Surety Bond:
      1.   Accrual: The bond shall accrue to the city covering construction,
operation and maintenance of the specific public improvement;
      2.   Amount: The bond shall be in an amount equal to one hundred ten
percent (110%) of the total estimated cost for completing construction of the
specific public improvement as estimated by and approved by the city council;
      3.   Term Length: The term length in which the bond is in force shall be
for a period to be specified by the city council for the specific public
improvement;
      4.   Bonding For Surety Company: The bond shall be with a surety company
authorized to do business in the state of Idaho, acceptable to the city
council; and
      5.   Escrow Agreement: The escrow agreement shall be drawn and furnished
by the city council.
   B.   Cash Deposit, Certified Check, Negotiable Bond, Or Irrevocable Bank
Letter Of Credit:
      1.   Treasurer, Escrow Agent Or Trust Company: A cash deposit, certified
check, negotiable bond or an irrevocable bank letter of credit, such surety
acceptable by the city council, shall be deposited with an escrow agent or
trust company.
      2.   Dollar Value: The dollar value of the cash deposit, certified check,
negotiable bond or irrevocable bank letter of credit shall be equal to one
hundred ten percent (110%) of the estimated cost of construction for the
specific public improvement as estimated and approved by the city council.
      3.   Escrow Time: The escrow time for the cash deposit, certified check,
negotiable bond or irrevocable bank letter of credit shall be for a period to
be specified by the city council; and
      4.   Progressive Payment: In the case of cash deposits or certified
checks, an agreement between the city council and the subdivider may provide
for progressive payment out of the cash deposit or reduction of the certified
check, negotiable bond or irrevocable bank letter of credit, to the extent of
the cost of the completed portion of the public improvement, in accordance with
a previously entered into agreement.
Important: Permits will not be issued until improvements are constructed or
financial guarantee arrangements as described above are in place. (Ord. 2001-
5 Art. V §3, 2001)
16A.20.040: INSPECTION OF PUBLIC IMPROVEMENTS:
Before approving a final plat and construction plans and specifications for
public improvements, an agreement between the subdivider and the city council
shall be made to provide for checking or inspecting the construction and its
conformity to the submitted plans. (Ord. 2001-5 Art. V §4, 2001)
16A.20.050: AS BUILT PLANS REQUIRED:
Prior to the acceptance by the appropriate agency of any improvements installed
by the subdivider, one set of prints of the "as built" plans and specifications
shall be certified by the subdivider's engineer and filed with the
administrator. (Ord. 2001-5 Art. V §5, 2001)
16A.20.060: AGENCY CERTIFICATION:
Within ten (10) days after completion of improvements and submission of "as
built" plans, the appropriate agencies shall certify the completion and
acceptance of the construction and shall transmit a copy of said certification
to the administrator and subdivider. (Ord. 2001-5 Art. V §6, 2001)
16A.20.070: FAILURE TO COMPLETE PUBLIC IMPROVEMENT:
In the event the subdivider in any case fails to complete such work within the
period of time as required by the conditions of the guarantee for the
completion of public improvements, it shall be the responsibility of the city
council to proceed to have such work completed. In order to accomplish this,
the city council shall reimburse itself for the cost and expense thereof by
appropriating the cash deposit, certified check, irrevocable bank letter of
credit, or negotiable bond which the subdivider may have deposited in lieu of a
surety bond, or may take such steps as may be necessary to require performance
by the bonding or surety company, and as included in a written agreement
between the city council and the subdivider. (Ord. 2001-5 Art. V §7, 2001)
CHAPTER 16A.24
DESIGN STANDARDS FOR SUBDIVISIONS
SECTION:
16A.24.010: Lot Requirements
16A.24.020: Block Requirements
16A.24.030: Sidewalk Requirements
16A.24.040: Street Requirements
16A.24.050: Domestic Water
16A.24.060: Sanitary Sewage Disposal
16A.24.070: Utilities
16A.24.080: Stream Easements
16A.24.090: Noxious Weed Control
16A.24.100: Monumentation
16A.24.010: LOT REQUIREMENTS:
All lots shall conform to the following:
   A.   Minimum lot size shall be adequate to accommodate the requirements of
the health authorities for sewage disposal systems and water facilities; and be
at least 7,187.5 square feet with at least 62.5 feet frontage, except on cul-
de-sacs, which shall have at least fifty feet (50') of frontage in radius area;
   B.   Width, depth, lot area and setback requirements shall be as specified
in the Kamiah zoning and development ordinance;
   C.   No lot shall be divided by road, street or alley; and
   D.   All lots in a residential subdivision shall front on a public street.
(Ord. 2001-5 Art. VI §1, 2001)
16A.24.020: BLOCK REQUIREMENTS:
Blocks shall be designed with due regard for the following:
   A.   Provision of adequate building sites suitable to the special
requirements of the type of use contemplated;
   B.   Blocks shall be reasonable in length and the total design provide for
convenient access and circulation for emergency vehicles (not in excess of
1,800 feet);
   C.   Pedestrian crosswalks shall be provided for pedestrian access to
schools, playgrounds, shopping areas and other such facilities; and
   D.   Blocks shall be designed to provide two (2) tiers of lots, except where
lots back onto an arterial street, natural feature or subdivision boundary.
(Ord. 2001-5 Art. VI §2, 2001)
16A.24.030: SIDEWALK REQUIREMENTS:
Sidewalks of not less than four feet (4') in width and constructed of Portland
cement or asphaltic concrete shall be provided on both sides of the street
where:
   A.   The subdivision is adjacent to an existing subdivision within an
incorporated area where sidewalks are provided; or
   B.   Sidewalks are necessary for safe pedestrian movement. (Ord. 2001-5 Art.
VI §3, 2001)
16A.24.040: STREET REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Street and road layout shall conform to the following:
      1.   Highway District Standards: All streets and rights of way within
subdivisions shall be constructed according to highway district standards and
specifications existing at the time the initial subdivision application is
made, even if the subdivider/developer does not intend to immediately petition
for acceptance by the highway district. No private roads shall be allowed in
subdivisions;
      2.   Curbs And Gutters: Vertical curbs and gutters shall be required on
collector and arterial streets. Rolled curbs and gutters may be allowed on
minor streets. All construction shall be in accordance with standards and
specifications adopted by the council;
      3.   Driveways: Driveway openings shall be constructed to public works,
highway district, or state highway department standards;
      4.   Minor Streets: Minor streets shall be so arranged to discourage
their use by through traffic;
      5.   Alleys: Alleys may be required for service access and off street
loading and parking in multiple dwelling or commercial subdivisions;
      6.   Half Streets: Half streets shall be prohibited except where unusual
circumstances make such necessary to the reasonable development of a tract in
conformance with this title and where satisfactory assurance for dedication of
the remaining part of the street is provided;
      7.   Intersections: Intersections of collector streets with major streets
shall be kept at a minimum. Intersections should be as nearly as possible at
right angles, but in no event at less than seventy degrees (70°). "T"
intersections may be used wherever such design will not restrict the free
movement of traffic. No more than two (2) streets shall intersect at any one
intersection;
      8.   Centerlines: Street centerlines of opposing "T" intersections shall
be offset by a distance of at least one hundred twenty five feet (125');
      9.   Street Grades: Street grades shall be such as to provide for the
safe movement of traffic in all weather and to provide adequate drainage.
Grades shall not exceed ten percent (10%);
      10.   Cul-De-Sacs: Cul-de-sac streets shall be no more than five hundred
feet (500') in length and shall terminate with an adequate turnaround having a
minimum street surface radius of forty feet (40');
      11.   Dead End Streets: Dead end streets shall be permitted only when
such streets terminate at the boundary of the subdivision and are necessary to
the future development of adjacent areas and shall include sufficient space or
temporary turnarounds;
      12.   Right Of Way Widths: Right of way widths shall be the greater of
either highway district standards existing on the date of the initial
application for subdivision or as follows:
 
Street Types       Widths (Feet)
Primary arterial   80 - 100
Secondary arterial 60 - 80
Collector          60
Minimum street     60 (40 feet minimum curb to curb)
 
      13.   Street Access: Each lot shall be served with at least one approved
street access;
      14.   Street Names: Street names shall conform to the requirements set
forth in the city of Kamiah road naming and addressing ordinance;
      15.   Street Lighting: Streetlights may be required to be installed at
street intersections throughout the subdivision. A subdivider shall conform to
the requirements of the city and the public utility providing such lighting.
(Ord. 2001-5 Art. VI §4, 2001)
16A.24.050: DOMESTIC WATER:
   A.   Central water distribution systems shall be installed in all
subdivisions. Potable water shall be provided to each lot in a subdivision by
the developer, and shall be an extension of existing public facilities whenever
possible;
   B.   All water systems shall also meet any additional requirements set forth
by the commission. (Ord. 2001-5 Art. VI §5, 2001)
16A.24.060: SANITARY SEWAGE DISPOSAL:
   A.   Sewage disposal systems shall be provided in all subdivisions, and
shall be an extension of existing facilities whenever possible;
   B.   Construction plans and specifications for any alternate system of
sewage collection and/or treatment shall be approved by the north central
district health department. (Ord. 2001-5 Art. VI §6, 2001)
16A.24.070: UTILITIES:
   A.   All existing water routes, either for irrigation or drainage, shall be
maintained through the subdivision from the existing point of entry to the
point of exit from the land, unless the adjoining property owner(s) who are
affected consent to moving either the point of entry or the point of exit. The
subdivider shall be required to install appropriate facilities, throughout the
subdivision, to accommodate the peak existing flows, as determined by the
hydrologic report.
   B.   The subdivider shall submit to the administrator sufficient information
in the form of maps, profiles, hydrological data and other data prepared by an
engineer to indicate the proper drainage of the surface water to natural
drainage courses or into existing storm drains. The location and width of
easements shall be indicated on the plat to be recorded. (Ord. 2001-5 Art. VI
§7, 2001)
16A.24.080: STREAM EASEMENTS:
The reservation of an adequate easement along any stream or surface drainage
course located in the area being subdivided may be required by the commission
for widening, deepening, sloping, improving or protecting the stream or
drainage course. (Ord. 2001-5 Art. VI §8, 2001)
16A.24.090: NOXIOUS WEED CONTROL:
Control of all noxious weeds found growing within the boundaries of the
development shall be the full responsibility of the developer. "Control" means
effective cutting, tillage, cropping, pasturing or treating with chemicals or
other effective methods, or combination thereof, as may be required to prevent
weeds from blooming and maturing seeds, or spreading by root stalks or other
means. In addition, the developer shall maintain graded surfaces throughout the
development that allow access by ground mobile weed control equipment (i.e.,
truck mounted sprayers, mowers, etc.). He shall carry this responsibility from
the first day of construction until all lots or parcels are sold. As lots or
parcels are sold, each individual new owner shall become responsible for weed
control on his own property. (Ord. 2001-5 Art. VI §9, 2001)
16A.24.100: MONUMENTATION:
Following completion of the construction of all improvements and prior to the
release of the performance bond or other guarantee, or prior to the filing of
the final plat in the event improvements are constructed prior to filing,
certain land survey monuments shall be reset or verified by the subdivider's
engineer or surveyor to still be in place. These monuments shall be of the
size, shape and type of materials as shown on the subdivision plat. The
monuments shall be located as follows:
   A.   All angle points in the exterior boundary of the final plat;
   B.   All street intersection points within and adjacent to the final plat;
   C.   All street centerlines ending at a boundary line of the final plat;
   D.   All angle points and points of curve on all streets;
   E.   The point of beginning of the subdivision plat description;
   F.   Section corners and quarter-section corners or reference monuments
thereof. (Ord. 2001-5 Art. VI §10, 2001)
CHAPTER 16A.28
VARIANCES
SECTION:
16A.28.010: Purpose
16A.28.020: Findings
16A.28.010: PURPOSE:
The commission may recommend to the city council as a result of a unique
circumstance such as topographic physical limitations or a planned unit
development a variance from the provisions of this title on a finding that
undue hardship results from the strict compliance with specific provisions or
requirements of this title or the application of such provision or requirement
is impracticable. Variances shall not be granted on the grounds of convenience
or profit, but only where strict application of this title would result in
unnecessary hardship or inequity. (Ord. 2001-5 Art. VII §1, 2001)
16A.28.020: FINDINGS:
No variance shall be favorably acted upon by the city council unless there is a
finding upon recommendations by the commission, as a result of a public
hearing, that all of the following exist:
   A.   That there are such special circumstances or conditions affecting the
property that the strict application of the provisions of this title would
clearly be impracticable or unreasonable; in such cases, the subdivider shall
first state his reasons in writing as to the specific provisions or
requirements involved;
   B.   That the strict compliance with the requirements of this title would
result in extraordinary hardship to the subdivider because of unusual
topography, other physical conditions which are not self-inflicted, or that
these conditions would result in inhibiting the achievement of the objectives
of this title;
   C.   That the granting of a specified variance will not be detrimental to
the public welfare or injurious to other property in the area in which the
property is situated;
   D.   That such variance will not violate the provisions of the Idaho Code.
(Ord. 2001-5 Art. VII §2, 2001)
CHAPTER 16A.32
SPECIAL DEVELOPMENT SUBDIVISIONS
SECTION:
16A.32.010: Purpose
16A.32.020: Subdivisions Within Floodplains
16A.32.030: Hillside Subdivisions
16A.32.040: Cemetery Subdivisions
16A.32.010: PURPOSE:
The purpose of this chapter is to identify various types of developments that
normally pose special concerns. This chapter outlines the plan submittal
requirements and design standards that shall be taken into consideration when
acting on special developments. The provisions of this chapter are in addition
to the plan requirements, design standards, and improvement standards that are
required by previous chapters of this title. (Ord. 2001-5 Art. VIII §1, 2001)
16A.32.020: SUBDIVISIONS WITHIN FLOODPLAINS:
   A.   Flood Areas: For any proposed subdivision that is located within an
area of special flood hazard, the developer shall provide the commission with a
development plan of adequate scale and supporting documentation that will show
and explain at least the following:
      1.   Location of all planned improvements;
      2.   The location of the base flood and the floodway as documented in the
flood insurance rate maps for Lewis County or other such authoritative source;
      3.   The location of the present water channel;
      4.   Any planned rerouting of waterways;
      5.   All major drainageways;
      6.   Areas of known frequent flooding;
      7.   Means of floodproofing buildings; and
      8.   Means of insuring loans for improvements within the floodplain. New
construction and substantial improvements of residential structures within the
floodplain shall comply with the standards and requirements set forth in the
Kamiah flood damage protection ordinance.
   B.   Justification For Development:
      1.   Upon the determination that buildings are planned within the
floodplain or that alterations of any kind are anticipated within the
floodplain area that will alter the flow of water, the developer shall
demonstrate conclusively to the commission that such development will not
present a hazard to life, limb or property and will not have adverse effects on
the safety, use or stability of a public way or drainage channel or the natural
environment.
      2.   No subdivision or part thereof shall be approved if levees, fills,
structures or other features within the proposed subdivision will individually
or collectively significantly increase flood flows, heights or damages. If only
part of the proposed subdivision can be safely developed, the council shall
limit development to that part and shall require that development proceed
consistent with that determination.
Subdivisions shall be reviewed to assure that:
         a.   All such proposals are consistent with the need to minimize flood
damage;
         b.   All public utilities and facilities, such as sewer, gas,
electrical, and water systems, are located and constructed to minimize or
eliminate flood damages; and
         c.   Adequate drainage is provided so as to reduce exposure to flood
hazards. (Ord. 2001-5 Art. VIII §2, 2001)
16A.32.030: HILLSIDE SUBDIVISIONS:
The provisions of this section shall apply to any development proposal for
properties where any average slope exceeds twelve percent (12%) or where
adverse conditions associated with a slope stability, erosion or sedimentation
are present.
   A.   Appearance And Preservation: In order to preserve, retain, enhance and
promote the existing and future appearance, natural topographic features,
qualities and resources of hillsides, special consideration shall be given to
the following:
      1.   Skyline and ridge tops;
      2.   Rolling grassy landforms, including knolls, ridges and meadows;
      3.   Tree and shrub masses, grass, wildflowers and topsoil;
      4.   Rock outcroppings;
      5.   Streambeds, draws and drainage swales, especially where tree and
plant formations occur; and
      6.   Characteristic vistas and scenic panoramas.
   B.   Hillside Development Evaluation:
      1.   All development proposals shall take into account and shall be
judged by the way in which land use planning, soil mechanics, engineering
geology, hydrology, civil engineering, environmental and civic design,
architectural and landscape design are applied in hillside areas, including,
but not limited to:
         a.   Planning of development to fit the topography soils, geology,
hydrology and other conditions existing on the proposed site;
         b.   Orientation of development on the site so that grading and other
site preparation is kept to an absolute minimum;
         c.   Shaping of essential grading to blend with natural landforms and
to minimize the necessity of padding and/or terracing of building sites;
         d.   Division of large tracts into smaller workable units on which
construction can be completed within one construction season so that large
areas are not left bare and exposed during the winter/ spring runoff period;
         e.   Allocation of areas not well suited for development because of
soil, geology or hydrology limitations for open space and recreation uses;
         f.   Minimizing disruption of existing plant and animal life; and
         g.   Consideration of the view from and of the hillside.
Areas having soil, geology or hydrology hazards shall not be developed unless
it is shown that their limitations can be overcome; that the safety, use or
stability of a public way or drainage channel is not jeopardized; and that the
natural environment is not subjected to undue impact.
   C.   Development Plans: The developer shall obtain the following
information:
      1.   Soils Report: For any proposed hillside development a soils report
shall be submitted with the preliminary plat. This report shall include data
regarding the nature, distribution and strength of existing soils, conclusions
and recommendations covering the adequacy of sites to be developed.
      2.   Geology Report: For any proposed hillside development a geology
report shall be submitted with the preliminary plat. This report shall include
an adequate description of site geology and an evaluation of the relationship
between the proposed development and the underlying geology and recommendations
for remedial remedies.
      3.   Hydrology Report: For any proposed hillside development a hydrology
report shall be submitted with the preliminary plat. This report shall include
an adequate description of the hydrology, conclusions and recommendations
regarding the effect of hydrologic conditions on the proposed development, and
opinions and recommendations covering the adequacy of sites to be developed.
      4.   Grading Plan: A preliminary grading plan may be required by the
planning and zoning commission or administrator. When required, the grading
plan shall be submitted with preliminary plat proposal for the following sites
or conditions:
         a.   Average slope of site is twelve percent (12%) or steeper;
         b.   Unstable soil condition;
         c.   Cut or fills adjacent to or encroaching in existing improvements
(canals, roadways, creeks, etc.);
         d.   Site work requiring retaining walls;
         The grading plan will include, but is not limited to, the following:
            • Topographic lines of existing land;
            • Grading lines for important areas;
            • Proposed drainage channels and related construction;
            • Quantities for cut and fill materials; and
            • Site of borrow or waste material.
      5.   Final Grading Plan: A final grading plan shall be submitted with
each final plat and shall include the following information:
         a.   Limiting dimensions, elevations or finish contours to be achieved
by the grading, including all proposed cut and fill slopes, proposed drainage
channels and related construction.
         b.   Detailed plans and locations of all surface and subsurface
drainage devices, walls, dams, sediment basins, storage reservoirs and other
protective devices to be constructed.
         c.   A schedule showing when each stage of the project will be
completed including the total area of soil surface which is to be disturbed
during each stage together with each estimated starting and completion dates.
In no event shall the existing ("natural") vegetation ground cover be
destroyed, removed or disturbed more than fifteen (15) days prior to grading.
(Ord. 2001-5 Art. VIII §3, 2001)
16A.32.040: CEMETERY SUBDIVISIONS:
   A.   Documentation Provided: The developer shall provide the commission with
written documentation that will sufficiently explain the functions of the
proposed cemetery for either animal or human remains.
   B.   Compliance With Idaho Code: The developer shall submit a written
statement that has been prepared by an attorney that adequately assures the
compliance of the proposed cemetery with the procedural management requirements
that are outlined in title 27, Idaho Code. (Ord. 2001-5 Art. VIII §4, 2001)
CHAPTER 16A.36
ADMINISTRATION AND ENFORCEMENT
SECTION:
16A.36.010: Administration
16A.36.020: Detection Of Violations
16A.36.030: Plat Recording
16A.36.040: Enforcement
16A.36.050: Penalties 
16A.36.010: ADMINISTRATION:
The planning and zoning commission shall have the authority to administer this
title under the direction of the city council. The planning and zoning
commission, in the execution of its administrative duties, may establish
procedures and rules necessary for compliance with this title. (Ord. 2001-
5 Art. IX §1, 2001)
16A.36.020: DETECTION OF VIOLATIONS:
When the planning and zoning commission determines that any provision of this
title is being or has been violated, the department shall notify the persons
responsible of the necessary corrective action. If after notification the
persons responsible fail to correct the violation, the planning and zoning
commission shall refer the matter to the prosecuting attorney for appropriate
action. (Ord. 2001-5 Art. IX §2, 2001)
16A.36.030: PLAT RECORDING:
No subdivision plat required by this title or the Idaho Code shall be admitted
to the public land records of Lewis County or recorded by the county recorder
until such subdivision plat has received final approval by the city council. No
public board, agency, commission, official, or other authority shall proceed
with construction or authorize the construction of any of the public
improvements required by this title until the final plat has been recorded. No
building permits for private improvements shall be issued on platted lots until
the final plat has been recorded. (Ord. 2001-5 Art. IX §3, 2001)
16A.36.040: ENFORCEMENT:
No subdivision plat required by this title or the Idaho Code shall be admitted
to the public land records of the county or recorded by the county recorder
until such subdivision plat has received final approval by the city council.
The prosecuting attorney shall, in addition to taking whatever criminal action
deemed necessary, take steps to civilly enjoin any violation of this title.
(Ord. 2001-5 Art. IX §4, 2001)
16A.36.050: PENALTIES:
Penalties for failure to comply with the provisions of this title shall be as
follows:
Violation of any of the provisions of this title or failure to comply with any
of its requirements shall constitute a misdemeanor. Each day such violation
continues shall be considered a separate offense. The landowner, tenant,
subdivider, builder, public official or any other person who commits,
participates in, assists in or maintains such violation may each be found
guilty of a separate offense. Nothing herein contained shall prevent the city
council or any other public official or private citizen from taking such lawful
action as is necessary to restrain or prevent any violation of this title or of
the Idaho Code. (Ord. 2001-5 Art. IX §5, 2001)
CHAPTER 16A.40
AMENDMENTS
SECTION:
16A.40.010: Procedures
16A.40.010: PROCEDURES:
The city council may, from time to time, amend, supplement or repeal the
regulations and provisions of this title in the manner prescribed by sections
67-6509 and 67-6511 of the Idaho Code. A proposed amendment, supplement or
repeal may be originated by the city council, commission or by petition. All
proposals not originating with the commission shall be referred to it for a
report thereon before any action is taken on the proposal by the city council.
(Ord. 2001-5 Art. X, 2001)
TITLE 17
ZONING AND DEVELOPMENT
CHAPTER 17.04
GENERAL PROVISIONS
SECTION:
17.04.010: Title
17.04.020: Authority
17.04.030: Purpose
17.04.040: Scope
17.04.050: Organization And Use Of Title
17.04.060: Administration And Enforcement
17.04.070: Related City Ordinances, Policies, Or Standards
17.04.080: General Provisions Of Title Enumerated
17.04.090: Zoning Map
17.04.010: TITLE:
This title together with the appropriate maps and appendices shall be known as
CITY OF KAMIAH ZONING AND DEVELOPMENT ORDINANCE, hereinafter referred to as
"this title". (Ord. 2007-4, 2007)
17.04.020: AUTHORITY:
This title is adopted pursuant to the authority granted by title 67, chapter 65
of the Idaho Code and article 12, section 2 of the Idaho constitution, as
amended or subsequently codified. The standards of the policies of this title
have been adopted in accordance with the comprehensive plan adopted by
resolution of the city council. (Ord. 2007-4, 2007)
17.04.030: PURPOSE:
The purpose of this title is to provide for the health, safety, and general
welfare of the city and its inhabitants. It is designed to:
   A.   Encourage urban and urban type development within the city and the area
of impact;
   B.   Avoid undue concentration of population and overcrowding of land;
   C.   Ensure that the development of land is commensurate with the physical
characteristics of the land;
   D.   Protect life and property in areas subject to natural hazards and
disasters;
   E.   Ensure that adequate public facilities and services are provided;
   F.   Protect both property rights and property values and to minimize the
conflicts among the uses of land and buildings;
   G.   Establish reasonable standards for development which promote the
orderly and beneficial development of all parts of the city;
   H.   Prevent the pollution of air, soil, streams, rivers and ponds and to
safeguard the water table; and to encourage the wise use and management of
natural resources throughout the city in order to preserve the integrity,
stability and beauty of the city and the value of the land;
   I.   Encourage well planned development, and to ensure equitable handling of
all proposals by providing uniform procedures and standards. (Ord. 2007-4,
2007)
17.04.040: SCOPE:
   A.   This title is to be in full force and effect from and after its
passage, approval, and publication.
   B.   If any one or more of the sections, subsections or any other part of
this title is for any reason held to be unconstitutional or invalid, such
decision shall not affect the validity of the remaining portions of this title
and the same shall remain in full force and effect.
   C.   Regulations of this title shall apply to all real property, structures
or fixtures attached thereto in the city of Kamiah. All persons, the United
States of America, the Nez Perce Tribe, the state of Idaho, Lewis County, the
city of Kamiah and all their respective agencies, boards, departments,
institutions, and local special purpose districts, shall comply with this title
unless otherwise excepted by law.
   D.   Whenever a provision of this title or any provision of any city, state,
federal, or county regulation, resolution, law, rule, or contract contains
restrictions covering the same subject matter, the more restrictive requirement
or higher standard shall govern when authorized by law. (Ord. 2007-4, 2007)
17.04.050: ORGANIZATION AND USE OF TITLE:
   A.   All lands, except as may be classified otherwise, and those classified
otherwise pursuant to Idaho Code and section 67-6526 in the incorporated areas
of the city, are hereby classified into zones. (This is to simplify
requirements and processing procedures, yet manage land development for the
benefit of all residents.) The purpose of the use classification is to grant
landowners maximum flexibility in using and developing their properties in a
way that will protect, retain or enhance the natural beauty characteristics of
the city. All uses in the city have been classified as "allowed" or
"conditional". It is necessary to classify some land uses as conditional so
they can be reviewed and evaluated individually by the commission and commented
upon by neighboring landowners as to compatibility with existing uses and the
physical surroundings of the use.
   B.   Allowed and conditional land uses are listed in section
17.12.020, table 1 of this title.
   C.   Allowed uses are defined in chapter 17.16 of this title.
   D.   Conditional uses are defined and procedures outlined in chapter 17.20
of this title.
   E.   The official zoning and development map shall be on display in the
planning department office. (Ord. 2007-4, 2007)
17.04.060: ADMINISTRATION AND ENFORCEMENT:
   A.   Office Of Planning And Zoning Administrator: There is established in
the city of Kamiah, state of Idaho, the office of the planning and zoning
administrator, which shall be under the jurisdiction of the mayor and the city
council of the city of Kamiah, state of Idaho. The mayor and city council shall
appoint the officers who shall be charged with the administration and
enforcement of this title, but the mayor and city council may, from time to
time, upon passage of a resolution, entrust the administration and enforcement,
in whole or in part, to any other office of the city.
   B.   City Of Kamiah Planning And Zoning Commission: A planning commission
shall implement this title with powers and duties as set forth in Idaho Code.
Said commission shall be appointed by the Kamiah city council. (Ord. 2007-4,
2007)
17.04.070: RELATED CITY ORDINANCES, POLICIES, OR STANDARDS:
Related documents containing land use policies, standards, or regulations,
together with this title, shall apply in the city. (Ord. 2007-4, 2007)
17.04.080: GENERAL PROVISIONS OF TITLE ENUMERATED:
   A.   Agricultural Land: The requirements of this title are intended to be
compatible with chapter 45 of title 22 of the Idaho Code (right to farm
legislation), and this title shall not be construed so as to deprive the owner
of agricultural land of the full and complete use of said land for the
production of any agricultural products.
   B.   Allowed Uses: Those uses which by their nature are compatible with
existing land uses in the zoned districts of Kamiah are allowed uses. Allowed
uses may be established in compliance with the standards and requirements set
forth in this title. Allowed uses shall comply with all other city regulations
and the laws, regulations and standards set forth by other local, state and
federal agencies.
   C.   Building Permits: Any person, firm or corporation desiring to
construct, erect, move or remodel a building exceeding one hundred twenty (120)
square feet in floor area shall first obtain a permit from the city and shall
pay a fee as required by the city.
   D.   Conditional Uses: Conditional uses are those uses which by their nature
possess characteristics such as to require review and appraisal by the
commission to determine whether or not the use would cause any damage, hazard,
or other detriment to persons, property, or natural resources in the vicinity.
   E.   Land Previously Subdivided: Any lot or parcel of land, which was of
record on the effective date hereof, which was in conformance with prior
subdivision regulations may be used as a dwelling site provided the building
placement and health requirements are met and that safe access can be
accomplished.
   F.   Nonconforming Uses: No nonconforming use of buildings, structures or
land shall be extended or enlarged, except when required by a county or state
health officer, and except that any dwelling situated on a nonconforming lot
may be enlarged so long as the use does not change and does not violate
required setbacks.
      1.   Continuation: The nonconforming use of buildings, structures and
land may be continued to the same extent and character as that which exists on
the effective date hereof.
   G.   Sewage Disposal And Water Systems: All sewage disposal facilities must
be installed and operating before a building shall be occupied. No building
shall be occupied as a residence or a commercial, civic, or industrial
establishment unless and until an approved and permitted supply of water and
sewage disposal system is installed and operating on the premises.
   H.   Lots Below Minimum Space Requirements: After the effective date hereof,
no parcel of land which has less than the minimum width and area requirements
may be created from a larger parcel of land for the purpose, whether immediate
or future, of building or development.
   I.   Sale Or Lease Of Required Space: No space needed to meet the width,
yard, area coverage, parking or other requirements of this title for a lot or
building may be sold or leased apart from such lot or building unless other
space so complying is provided. (Ord. 2007-4, 2007)
17.04.090: ZONING MAP:
This title consists of this text and the official zoning map which shall be
designated as the "city of Kamiah zoning map", as hereby adopted by the city
council as part of this title. Zoning boundaries shall be the centerline of
streets, alleys, waterways, and/or railroad rights of way unless such
boundaries are otherwise indicated on the zoning map. The official city of
Kamiah zoning map shall be that which is on display in the planning department
office. (Ord. 2007-4, 2007)
CHAPTER 17.08
DEFINITIONS
SECTION:
17.08.010: Defined Terms
17.08.010: DEFINED TERMS:
   A.   The planning and zoning commission reserves the right to define terms
not specified herein for the purpose of taking action on individual zoning
matters. The standards for such determination shall be:
      1.   Words and terms not specifically defined in this section shall be
interpreted according to Standard English usage and practice, as established in
"Webster's New World Dictionary Of The American Language",  tenth college
edition.
      2.   Colloquial words and terms shall be interpreted as having the same
definition as a Standard English word or term having the most similar
definition to that ascribed by local custom and usage.
   B.   The following terms shall be defined as follows:
   ACCESSORY BUILDING: Any structure not intended for human occupancy but that
serves an accessory function to the principal building on the property.
   ACCESSORY USE: Any use incidental and subordinate to the principal use of
the same premises.
   ADMINISTRATOR: An official of the city, who is authorized by the city
council to administer this title.
