hereof shall be hereafter deemed a lawful use.
   D.   A nonconforming use, if changed to a conforming use, may not thereafter
be changed back to a nonconforming use.
   E.   Normal repairs may be made to a lawful nonconforming structure, and
nothing in this title shall be deemed to prevent the strengthening or restoring
to a safe condition of any building or part thereof.
   F.   When a building or other structure containing a nonconforming use is
damaged by fire or by any other cause the building or structure may be replaced
on the existing foundation. The foundation may be enlarged if the current
setbacks established in this title can be met. (Ord. 2007-4, 2007)
17.36.030: NONCONFORMING UNDER PERMIT AUTHORITY:
Nothing contained in this regulation shall require any change in the plans,
construction, alteration or designated use of a structure upon which
construction has commenced and/or for which a permit has been obtained prior to
the effective date hereof. However, if the designated use will be
nonconforming, the construction for such use shall be commenced within six (6)
months of permit issuance and it shall be in operation within two (2) years
from the effective date hereof, otherwise, future use of the property shall be
in conformance with the requirements set forth in this title. (Ord. 2007-4,
2007)
CHAPTER 17.40
SIGNAGE
SECTION:
17.40.010: Purpose
17.40.015: Permit Required
17.40.020: General Signage Standards
17.40.030: Exempt Signs
17.40.040: Signs Allowed On Same Premises
17.40.050: Signs In The Revitalization Area Of The City
17.40.060: Violations
17.40.070: Penalties
17.40.010: PURPOSE:
The purpose of this chapter is to permit signage and yet preserve the character
and scenic beauty of the City, and to prevent unsafe sign obstructions for the
traveling public. (Ord. 2018-2, 2018)
17.40.015: PERMIT REQUIRED:
A sign permit must be secured from the City for any sign except those exempted
in section
17.40.030 of this chapter. Application for the sign permit will be filed with
the City.
Accompanying the application will be:
   A.   Height, width, and elevation of the proposed sign drawn to scale.
   B.   The color scheme of the sign.
   C.   A plot plan of the property on which the sign will be placed showing
the location of the sign on the property. If the sign is to be attached to the
face of the building the elevation shall also show the outline of the building
and the materials of which the sign will be constructed. This may be shown on
one of the required drawings. (Note special requirements for the revitalization
district.)
   D.   If the requirements of the provisions herein are met a sign permit
shall be issued to the applicant by the City with the approval of the building
inspector. The fee shall be set following the building permit and plan review
fees taken from section 109 of the International Building Code.
   E.   There will be no sign permit fee to repair or replace a sign if the
sign is the same size and style as the original. (Ord. 2018-2, 2018)
17.40.020: GENERAL SIGNAGE STANDARDS:
   A.   No sign shall be constructed, altered, maintained, or used except as
provided in this chapter.
   B.   No sign shall protrude over or into a street right-of-way.
   C.   Signs shall be maintained in sound repair at all times.
   D.   Signs may be luminous, reflecting or illuminating with Planning and
Zoning Commission approval.
   E.   Businesses not located within the Kamiah School District limits shall
not be allowed to place a sign within Kamiah City limits.
   F.   Roof signs may be allowed on a case by case basis.
   G.   No off premises signs will be allowed without the permission of the
owner of the property.
   H.   This chapter will not apply to the City Impact Area.
   I.   All signage on State highways shall first be approved by the Idaho
Department of Transportation and then approved by the City.
   J.   The Planning and Zoning Board will review all signs for size, content,
lettering, color, substrate, and placement locations.
   K.   There shall be no perpendicular signs on the front of the building
unless they are a silhouette type sign and project three feet (3') or less from
the building. The size of the perpendicular sign cannot exceed thirty six
inches (36") in width and twenty four inches (24") in height. A minimum of
seven feet (7') in height is required from the bottom of the sign to the
sidewalk elevation.
   L.   Signs must be of a high standard of workmanship.
   M.   All signs must be sketched in detail and to scale for the fronts of
buildings. All signs must follow the permitting system.
   N.   The building inspector will review the drawings to ensure that the
installation of the sign meets the Building Code standards.
   O.   Roof signs may be allowed in the revitalization district but must
follow the Western Victorian theme.
   P.   The City Clerk or the Planning Administrator shall notify the Planning
Commission to schedule a review of the proposed sign drawings at the next
scheduled meeting of the commission. Upon approval, the City Clerk or building
inspector will issue a permit to allow the sign. (Ord. 2018-2, 2018)
17.40.030: EXEMPT SIGNS:
   A.   Window signs.
   B.   Memorial signs.
   C.   Temporary signs or banners will be allowed for up to sixty (60) days.
   D.   Political signs must be removed thirty (30) days after election.
   E.   Signs advertising the sale, retail or lease of property. The number of
signs shall be limited to two (2) signs per parcel or building, one for owner
and the other for the realtor.
   F.   Informational signs are allowed but must be removed seven (7) days
following the beginning of the intended use project.
   G.   Signs required by law.
   H.   Temporary sandwich board signs ("A" board). (See standards below.)
      1.   Street and sidewalk signs shall be not larger than twenty four
inches by forty eight inches (24"x48") high.
      2.   Street signs may not be placed nearer than twenty feet (20') from
any street intersection along centerline and must be spaced at least twelve
feet (12') apart. Signs shall not hinder access (either ingress or egress) to
business entrances or exits. Sidewalk signs must allow for forty eight inches
(48") of clear pedestrian walk space.
      3.   Each business or organization shall be allowed only one sandwich
board in the street and one sandwich board sign on the sidewalk.
      4.   Sandwich signs shall only be allowed on Idaho and Main Streets in
the C-1 (Commercial District) zoned section of Kamiah.
      5.   Signs shall be removed at close of business each day or no later
than nine o'clock (9:00) P.M.
      6.   Signs shall be maintained in sound repair at all times.
      7.   No sign shall be allowed that is in violation of State or Federal
regulations or contain sexually oriented content or personal messages.
      8.   Each sandwich board sign (both sidewalk and street) shall be of a
professional design with the Western Victorian theme for the framework.
      9.   A drawing must be submitted to City Hall before the sign is made. It
will be approved/disapproved as to the regulation of this chapter by City Hall
staff.
      10.   The City has the right to require the removal of signs that do not
comply with this chapter. Owners will be notified of the need to remove the
noncompliant sign. If owners refuse to remove the non-compliant sign, the City
has the right to remove it.
      11.   Temporary signs advertising events shall only be up a week ahead of
the event and taken down right after the event occurs.
      12.   Handwritten sidewalk or street signs will not be allowed unless a
menu or day's activities are being changed. Occasional community street signs
may be handwritten.
      13.   If a sign is placed in the street that does not follow the above
regulations, a letter will be sent to the owner stating that they have two (2)
days to remove the sign from the street. If the sign is not removed the
Marshal's Office will remove it and issue them a citation.
      14.   All sandwich board signs on the right-of-way of Highway 12 must be
approved by the Idaho Department of Transportation and then approved by the
City. (Ord. 2018-2, 2018)
17.40.040: SIGNS ALLOWED ON SAME PREMISES:
   A.   Commercial:
      1.   Freestanding: One sign, not to exceed fifty (50) square feet in area
and twelve feet (12') high.
      2.   Attached to a building: The size and number of signs must be
reasonable for the area of the wall on which the sign is attached.
A variance to enlarge the signage area may be requested from the Planning and
Zoning Commission.
      3.   Multiple businesses: Total signage for all occupants must be
reasonable for the area of the wall on which the sign is attached.
         a.   Where an occupant has an entrance on an alley additional signs
may be permitted if signs are visible in such alley.
   B.   Industrial:
      1.   One sign, of reasonable size for the area of placement, with a
minimum setback of fifteen feet (15') from the property line.
      2.   The requirements for multiple occupancies are the same as in the
Commercial District. (Ord. 2018-2, 2018)
17.40.050: SIGNS IN THE REVITALIZATION AREA OF THE CITY:
[https://export.amlegal.com/media/89d384cf29bcbb7f8c61c93736cf7b2a2b9e609d/
IMAGES/0-0-0-1724.png]
 
   A.   Backlit, translucent or neon signs may be allowed if in the Western
Victorian theme.
   B.   Signs may have indirect lighting only.
      1.   A business may obtain special approval from the Governing Body for
an internally lit sign.
   C.   Signs may have stationary lights but no blinking lights bordering them.
   D.   Signs shall be cut from wood or of composition (substrate) or metal
resembling wood and painted.
   E.   The overall effect of the sign must be in keeping with the design theme
which has been adopted for this location and is outlined in the following
diagram (except for National Corporation Branding or business logos):
[https://export.amlegal.com/media/89d384cf29bcbb7f8c61c93736cf7b2a2b9e609d/
IMAGES/0-0-0-1726.png]
 
(Ord. 2018-2, 2018)
17.40.060: VIOLATIONS:
It shall be unlawful for any person or firm or corporation to erect, move,
construct, alter or install signs in violation of this chapter. (Ord. 2018-2,
2018)
17.40.070: PENALTIES:
Each violation of this chapter is a misdemeanor. Each day that the violation
continues after notification shall constitute a separate offense, and each
violation shall be punishable as provided by Idaho Code. (Ord. 2018-2, 2018)
CHAPTER 17.44
KAMIAH AIRPORT STANDARDS
SECTION:
17.44.010: Definitions
17.44.020: Airport Zones
17.44.030: Height Limitations
17.44.040: Use Restrictions And Nonconforming Uses
17.44.050: Permits
17.44.010: DEFINITIONS:
As used in this chapter unless the context otherwise requires the words used in
this chapter shall be defined as set forth below:
AIRPORT: The Kamiah municipal airport.
AIRPORT ELEVATION: The highest point of an airport's usable landing area
measured in feet from mean sea level.
AIRPORT HAZARD: Any structure or object of natural growth located on or in the
vicinity of a public airport, or any use of land near an airport, which
obstructs the airspace required for the flight of aircraft in landing or
takeoff at such landing or takeoff of aircraft.
APPROACH, TRANSITIONAL, HORIZONTAL, AND CONICAL ZONES: Apply to areas under the
approach, transitional, horizontal and conical surfaces.
BOARD OF ADJUSTMENT: A board consisting of three (3) members appointed by the
city council of Kamiah.
HEIGHT: For the purpose of determining the height limits in all zones set forth
in this chapter and shown on the zoning map, the datum shall be mean sea level
elevation unless otherwise specified.
NONCONFORMING USE: Any preexisting structure, object of natural growth, or use
of land which is inconsistent with the provisions of this chapter or an
amendment thereto.
PERSON: An individual, firm, partnership, corporation, company, association,
joint stock association, or governmental entity. It includes a trustee,
receiver, assignee, or similar representative of any of them.
RUNWAY: A defined area on an airport prepared for landing and takeoff of
aircraft along its length.
RUNWAY, UTILITY: "Utility runway" means a runway that is constructed for and
intended to be used by propeller driven aircraft of twelve thousand five
hundred (12,500) pounds' maximum gross weight and less.
RUNWAY, VISUAL: "Visual runway" means a runway intended solely for the
operation of aircraft using visual approach procedures with no straight in
instrument approach procedure and no instrument designation indicated on an FAA
approved airport layout plan, a military service's approved military airport
layout plan, or by any planning document submitted to the FAA by competent
authority.
STRUCTURE: An object constructed or installed by man, including, but without
limitations, buildings, towers, smokestacks, earth formation, and overhead
transmission lines.
SURFACE, APPROACH: "Approach surface" means a surface longitudinally centered
on the extended runway centerline and extending outward and upward at a slope
of twenty feet (20') horizontally for each foot vertically, for a distance of
five thousand feet (5,000') beginning at the end of the primary surface. The
width of the approach surface expands uniformly from two hundred fifty feet
(250') wide at the end of the primary surface to one thousand two hundred fifty
feet (1,250') wide at the distance of five thousand feet (5,000') from the end
of the primary surface.
SURFACE, CONICAL: "Conical surface" means a surface extending outward and
upward at a slope of twenty feet (20') horizontally for each foot vertically,
beginning at the periphery of the horizontal surface and extending a horizontal
distance of four thousand feet (4,000').
SURFACE, HORIZONTAL: "Horizontal surface" means a horizontal plane one hundred
fifty feet (150') above the established airport elevation, the perimeter of
which is constructed by swinging arcs of five thousand foot (5,000') radii from
the center of each end of the primary surface and connecting the adjacent arcs
by lines tangent to those arcs.
SURFACE, PRIMARY: "Primary surface" means a surface longitudinally centered on
a runway. The primary surface extends two hundred feet (200') beyond each end
of that runway. The width of the primary surface is two hundred fifty feet
(250'). The elevation of any point on the primary surface is the same as the
elevation of the nearest point on the runway centerline.
SURFACE, TRANSITIONAL: "Transitional surface" means a surface extending outward
and upward at right angles to the runway centerline at a slope of seven feet
(7') horizontally for each foot vertically beginning at the sides of the
primary surface and the sides of the approach surfaces, and ending where it
penetrates the horizontal surface. (Ord. 2007-4, 2007)
17.44.020: AIRPORT ZONES:
   A.   Created: In order to carry out the provisions of this chapter, there
are created and established certain zones for existing and future planned
airport conditions as they apply to a particular airport. These zones include
all the land lying within the primary zones, approach zones, transitional
zones, horizontal zones and conical zones. Such zones are shown on the Kamiah
municipal airport hazard zoning map consisting of one sheet prepared by J-U-
B Engineers, Inc., and dated January 1977, which is attached to the ordinance
codified herein and made part hereof. Whenever the zoning map shows zones for
future planned airport improvements, the more stringent future planned zones
govern. Their limitations and boundaries shall be adapted for present zoning
purposes.
   B.   Airport Zones Enumerated: The various zones are established and defined
as follows:
      1.   Utility Runway Visual Approach Zones: Utility runway visual approach
zones are established as the area beneath the approach surfaces. The inner edge
of this approach zone coincides with the width of the primary surface and is
two hundred fifty feet (250') wide. The approach zones expand outward uniformly
to a width of one thousand two hundred fifty feet (1,250') at a horizontal
distance of five thousand feet (5,000') from the primary surface, its
centerline being the continuation of the centerline of the runway.
      2.   Transitional Zones: Transitional zones are established as the area
beneath the transitional surfaces. These surfaces extend outward and upward at
ninety degree (90°) angles to the runway centerline and the centerline extended
at a slope of seven feet (7') horizontally for each foot vertically from the
sides of the primary approach surfaces to where they intersect the horizontal
surface.
      3.   Horizontal Zone: The horizontal zone is established as the area
below the horizontal surface. The horizontal zone perimeter is constructed by
swinging arcs of five thousand foot (5,000') radii from the center of each end
of the primary surface of each runway, and connecting the adjacent arcs by the
drawing lines tangent to those arcs. The horizontal zone does not include the
approach transitional zones.
      4.   Conical Zone: The conical zone is established as the area below the
conical surface. The conical zone is the area that commences at the periphery
of the horizontal zone and extends outward therefrom a horizontal distance of
four thousand feet (4,000'). (Ord. 2007-4, 2007)
17.44.030: HEIGHT LIMITATIONS:
   A.   Compliance With Established Limits: Except as provided in this chapter,
no structure or tree shall be erected, altered, allowed to grow, or be
maintained in any zone created by this chapter to a height in excess of the
applicable height limit established in this section for such zone. Such
applicable height limitations are established for each of the zones in question
as set forth in this section.
   B.   Zones:
      1.   Utility Runway Visual Approach Zone: In the utility runway visual
approach zone height limitation slopes upward horizontally twenty feet (20')
for each foot vertically, beginning at the end of and at the same elevation as
the primary surface and extending to a horizontal distance of five thousand
feet (5,000') along the extended runway centerline.
      2.   Transitional Zones: In transitional zones height limitation slopes
upward and outward seven thousand feet (7,000') horizontally for each foot
vertically beginning at the sides of and at the same elevation as the primary
surface and the approach surface, and extending to a height of one hundred
fifty feet (150') above the airport elevation which is one thousand two hundred
six feet (1,206') above mean sea level.
      3.   Horizontal Zone: In the horizontal zone height limitation is one
hundred fifty feet (150') above the airport elevation or a height of one
thousand three hundred fifty six feet (1,356') above mean sea level.
      4.   Conical Zone: In the conical zone height limitation slopes upward
and outward twenty feet (20') horizontally for each foot vertically beginning
at the periphery of the horizontal surface and at one hundred fifty feet (150')
above the airport elevation and extending to the height of three hundred fifty
feet (350') above the airport elevation.
   C.   Excepted Height Limitations:
      1.   Nothing in this chapter shall be construed as prohibiting the
growth, construction, or maintenance of any tree or structure to a height up to
thirty feet (30') above the surface of the land.
      2.   Where an area is covered by more than one height limitation, the
more restrictive limitation shall prevail. (Ord. 2007-4, 2007)
17.44.040: USE RESTRICTIONS AND NONCONFORMING USES:
   A.   Use Restrictions: Notwithstanding any other provisions of this chapter,
no use may be made of land or water within any zone established by this chapter
in such a manner as to create electrical interference with navigational signals
or radio communication between the airport and aircraft, make it difficult for
pilots to distinguish between airport lights and others, result in glare in the
eyes of the pilots using the airport, impair visibility in the vicinity of the
airport or otherwise in any way create a hazard or endanger the landing,
takeoff, or maneuvering of aircraft intending to use the airport.
   B.   Nonconforming Uses; Regulations Not Retroactive: The regulations
prescribed by this chapter shall not be construed to require the removal,
lowering, or other changes or alteration of any structure or tree not
conforming to the regulations as of the effective date hereof, or otherwise
interfere with the continuance of a nonconforming use. Nothing in this chapter
shall require any change in the construction, alteration, or intended use of
any structure, the construction or alteration of which was begun prior to the
effective date hereof, and is diligently prosecuted.
   C.   Nonconforming Uses; Marking And Lighting: Notwithstanding the
provisions of subsection B of this section, the owner of any existing
nonconforming structure or tree is required to permit the installation,
operation, and maintenance thereon of such markers and lights as shall be
deemed necessary by the city planning commission chairman to indicate to the
operators of any aircraft in the vicinity of the airport the presence of such
airport hazards. Such markers and lights shall be installed, operated, and
maintained at the expense of the city of Kamiah, Idaho. (Ord. 2007-4, 2007)
17.44.050: PERMITS:
   A.   Future Uses:
      1.   No material change shall be made in the use of land and no structure
or tree shall be erected, altered, planted, or otherwise established in any
zone created by this chapter unless a permit therefor shall have been applied
for and granted.
      2.   However, a permit for a tree or structure of less than seventy five
feet (75') of vertical height above the ground shall not be required in the
horizontal and conical zones or in any approach and transitional zones beyond a
horizontal distance of four thousand two hundred feet (4,200') from each end of
the runway except when such tree or structure, because of terrain, land
contour, or topographic features, would extend above the height limit
prescribed for the respective zone.
      3.   Each application for a permit shall indicate the purpose for which
the permit is desired with sufficient particulars to determine whether the
resulting use, structure, or tree would conform to the regulations herein
prescribed. If such a determination is in the affirmative, the permit shall be
granted.
   B.   Existing Uses: No permit shall be granted that would allow the
establishment or creation of an airport hazard or permit a nonconforming use,
structure, or tree to become a greater hazard to air navigation than it was on
the effective date hereof or any amendments thereto or than it is when the
application for a permit is made. Except as indicated, all applications for
such permit shall be granted.
   C.   Nonconforming Uses Abandoned Or Destroyed: Whenever the city planning
commission determines that a nonconforming tree or structure has been abandoned
or more than eighty percent (80%) torn down, physically deteriorated, or
decayed, no permit shall be granted that would allow such structure or tree to
exceed the applicable height limit or otherwise deviate from the zoning
regulations.
   D.   Variances: Any person desiring to erect or increase the height of any
structure, or permit the growth of any tree, or use his property not in
accordance with the regulations prescribed in this chapter, may apply to the
city planning commission for a variance from such regulations. Such variances
shall be allowed where it is duly found that a literal application or
enforcement of the regulations would result in practical difficulty or
unnecessary hardship and relief granted would not be contrary to the public
interest but will do substantial justice and be in accordance with the spirit
of this chapter.
   E.   Hazard Marking And Lighting: Any permit or variance granted may, if
such action is deemed advisable to effectuate the purpose of this chapter and
be reasonable in the circumstances, be so conditioned as to require the owner
of the structure or tree in question to permit the city of Kamiah, at its own
expense, to install, operate, and maintain thereon such markers and lights as
may be necessary to indicate to pilots the presence of airport hazard. (Ord.
2007-4, 2007)
CHAPTER 17.48
APPEALS
SECTION:
17.48.010: General Provisions
17.48.020: Administrator Appeals
17.48.030: Commission Appeals
17.48.040: Council Appeals
17.48.050: Request For Hearing By Affected Persons
17.48.060: Fees
17.48.010: GENERAL PROVISIONS:
   A.   Any decision may be appealed in accordance with Idaho Code and
procedures established herein.
   B.   All appeals must be written, accompanied by a fee as set forth by
resolution of the city council, and submitted to the administrator prior to the
deadlines set forth herein. If the deadline falls on a weekend or holiday the
appeal period is automatically extended to the next workday. Each appeal must
clearly state the name, address and phone number of the person or organization
appealing and the specific issues, items or conditions that are being appealed
and state the error of procedure or law which forms the basis of the appeal.
   C.   After review following a public hearing or not, in the council's
discretion, the commission or council may grant, amend, sustain or deny a
permit; or delay such a decision for up to one hundred twenty (120) days, or,
upon finding that special conditions warrant, for up to two hundred seventy
(270) days, for further study or hearing. (Ord. 2007-4, 2007)
17.48.020: ADMINISTRATOR APPEALS:
   A.   Decisions of the administrator regarding interpretation of this title
may be appealed to the commission by any affected person aggrieved by such
decision. Such appeal must be submitted to the commission in writing within
fifteen (15) days from such administrator's decision.
   B.   A properly submitted appeal shall be placed on the commission agenda
for review at the next regularly scheduled meeting.
   C.   The commission shall, within forty five (45) days following the review,
issue a written decision affirming, reversing or modifying the administrator's
decision. The written decision shall contain the reasons for such a decision.
(Ord. 2007-4, 2007)
17.48.030: COMMISSION APPEALS:
   A.   Decisions of the commission may be appealed to the city council by any
affected person or the administrator. Such appeal must be submitted to the
council in writing within fifteen (15) days from such commission decision.
   B.   A properly submitted appeal shall be placed on the council agenda for
review at the next regularly scheduled meeting.
   C.   The council may hold a public hearing to review the commission's
proceedings and decisions and may obtain additional information from the
administrator, the applicant, the appellant, or the public. If the council
requests a public hearing, the noticing requirements as set forth in section
17.20.090 of this title shall be followed.
   D.   Within forty five (45) days following the initial council review of the
appeal, or following a public hearing of the appeal, the council shall issue a
written decision affirming, reversing or modifying the commission's decision or
finding that special conditions warrant a delay, or may delay such a decision
for up to two hundred seventy (270) days. The written decision shall contain
the reasons for such decision. (Ord. 2007-4, 2007)
17.48.040: COUNCIL APPEALS:
An affected person aggrieved by a decision of the council may within twenty
eight (28) days after all remedies have been exhausted under local ordinance
seek judicial review as provided in Idaho Code. (Ord. 2007-4, 2007)
17.48.050: REQUEST FOR HEARING BY AFFECTED PERSONS:
Any affected person may at any time prior to final action on conditional use or
variance, if no hearing has been held on the application, petition the
commission or council in writing to hold a public hearing as outlined by
section 67-6512, Idaho Code; provided, however, that if twenty (20) affected
persons petition for a hearing, the hearing shall be held. (Ord. 2007-4, 2007)
17.48.060: FEES:
A fee for appeals of the decisions of the administrator, commission, and
council, as established by the council, shall be paid by the applicant to the
administrator when the appeal is submitted. (Ord. 2007-4, 2007)
CHAPTER 17.52
AMENDMENTS
SECTION:
17.52.010: Purpose
17.52.020: Initiation Of Amendments
17.52.030: Application Procedures
17.52.040: Determination Of Appropriate Classification
17.52.050: Commission Action
17.52.060: Standards For Approval
17.52.070: Action By Council
17.52.080: Fees
17.52.010: PURPOSE:
Whenever the public necessity, convenience, general welfare or good land use
and development practices require, the council may, by ordinance, after receipt
of recommendation thereon from the commission and subject to procedures
provided by Idaho Code section 67-6511, amend, supplement, change or repeal the
regulations, restrictions, and boundaries or classification of property. (Ord.
2007-4, 2007)
17.52.020: INITIATION OF AMENDMENTS:
   A.   Initiation: Amendment of this title or the Kamiah comprehensive plan
may be initiated by the council, by the commission, or by a property owner or
other affected person.
A property owner or other affected person may initiate a request for an
amendment by submitting an application in writing to the administrator at least
thirty (30) days prior to the commission meeting at which it will be
considered.
   B.   Zoning Upon Annexation: Prior to annexation of an unincorporated area,
the city council shall request and receive a recommendation from the planning
and zoning commission on the proposed comprehensive plan and zoning ordinance
changes for the unincorporated area. The commission and the city council shall
follow the notice and hearing procedures provided in this title. Concurrently
or immediately following the adoption of an ordinance of annexation, the city
council shall amend the comprehensive plan and zoning ordinance. (Ord. 2007-4,
2007)
17.52.030: APPLICATION PROCEDURES:
   A.   Filing: An application for an amendment shall be filed with the
administrator by the property owner or other affected person.
Following acceptance of the completed amendment application by the
administrator, the application shall be placed on the commission agenda for
action at the next regularly scheduled meeting.
   B.   Application Contents: Applications for amendment to this title shall
contain at least the following information:
      1.   Name, address and daytime telephone number of the applicant; and
      2.   A description of the proposed amendment; and
      3.   A statement on how the proposed amendment relates to the city
comprehensive plan; and
      4.   The application fee as established by the city council. (Ord. 2007-
4, 2007)
17.52.040: DETERMINATION OF APPROPRIATE CLASSIFICATION:
   A.   Classification of any unlisted land use shall be made based on the
impact of that use upon adjacent and neighboring properties and with regard for
the allowed uses existing on those properties and compliance with the
comprehensive plan.
   B.   The administrator shall make a determination as to whether or not the
unlisted use is similar to a listed allowed or conditional use.
   C.   When the administrator determines that the unlisted use is similar to a
listed use he shall direct the applicant to the appropriate classification and
the applicable rules, standards, etc.
   D.   If the administrator determines that the requested use is not similar
to any listed use he shall refer the classification question to the commission.
The commission shall consider the request and make a classification
recommendation to the council.
   E.   The council shall consider the classification question and commission
recommendation and may accept the unlisted use as a new use classification and
amend this title. (Ord. 2007-4, 2007)
17.52.050: COMMISSION ACTION:
Amendment applications shall be heard by the commission.
   A.   If the proposed amendment is found to be in accordance with the
comprehensive plan, within thirty five (35) days following review of the
application the commission will hold a public hearing to allow public review of
the proposed amendment.
Within forty five (45) days after the public hearing, the commission will
either recommend approval, recommend approval subject to modifications as it
deems necessary, or recommend denial of the application. The action must state
in writing:
      1.   The standards used in evaluating the application.
      2.   The reason(s) for the decision.
   B.   If approval is denied, the applicant will be provided with a written
statement from the administrator containing the specific reasons for denial.
The applicant may reapply for an amendment provided that all deficiencies that
caused the original application to be denied have been substantially corrected.
   C.   The commission may request review by any qualified professional person,
and may conduct, or cause to be conducted, investigations, examinations, tests
and site evaluations as it deems necessary to verify the information contained
in the application. The applicant grants the commission or its agent permission
to enter upon the land in question for these purposes by having made
application for an amendment. (Ord. 2007-4, 2007)
17.52.060: STANDARDS FOR APPROVAL:
The commission shall consider the facts and circumstances of each application
and shall make findings of fact based upon the proposed amendment's accordance
with the city comprehensive plan and impacts on neighboring properties and land
uses. (Ord. 2007-4, 2007)
17.52.070: ACTION BY COUNCIL:
The council, prior to adopting, revising, or rejecting the recommendation of
the commission to amend this title shall conduct at least one public hearing
using the same notice and hearing procedures as the commission. Following the
hearing, if the council makes a material change from what was presented at the
public hearing, further notice and hearing shall be provided before the council
adopts the amendment.
Upon granting or denying an application to amend this title, the city council
shall specify:
   A.   The ordinance and standards used in evaluating the application.
   B.   The reasons for approval or denial. (Ord. 2007-4, 2007)
17.52.080: FEES:
An amendment application fee as established by the council shall be paid by the
applicant to the administrator when the application is submitted. (Ord. 2007-4,
2007)
CHAPTER 17.56
WIRELESS TELECOMMUNICATION FACILITIES
SECTION:
17.56.010: Purpose
17.56.020: Where Allowed
17.56.030: Preferred Facilities
17.56.040: Disfavored Facilities
17.56.050: Performance Standards And Design Requirements
17.56.060: Application Process
17.56.070: Exemptions
17.56.080: Abandonment
17.56.090: Obsolescence And Removal
17.56.010: PURPOSE:
The purpose of this chapter is to establish a process, rules and standards for
the construction of wireless telecommunication facilities to:
   A.   Protect and promote the public health, safety and welfare.
   B.   Provide guidelines for the siting and design of wireless communication
facilities.
   C.   Protect the city's environmental resources and to minimize adverse
impacts on visual resources.
   D.   Ensure that wireless telecommunication facilities are compatible with
adjacent land uses.
   E.   Minimize the number of towers by encouraging the joint use
(collocation) of facilities and by maximizing the use of existing towers and
structures.
   F.   Allow competition in telecommunication service.
   G.   Enhance the ability to provide wireless telecommunication services to
city residents, businesses and visitors. (Ord. 2007-4, 2007)
17.56.020: WHERE ALLOWED:
Wireless telecommunication facilities require the granting of a conditional use
permit by the planning and zoning commission except as specified in section
17.56.070 of this chapter. Facilities are allowed in the industrial (M) zone
but are also permitted with a conditional use permit in the C-2 zone when not
in the designated scenic corridor of U.S. Highway 12. Facilities are not
permitted in the residential (R) or commercial (C-1) zones. (Ord. 2007-4, 2007)
17.56.030: PREFERRED FACILITIES:
Site location and development of wireless communication facilities shall
preserve the existing character of the surrounding land uses and buildings and
the aesthetic visual character of the area. If technically feasible, new
facilities shall use the most preferred facility type. The order of preference
for new facilities is as follows (from most preferred to least preferred):
   A.   Collocation on an existing tower.
   B.   Antennas attached to existing structures such as buildings, light
poles, utility poles.
   C.   Concealed or camouflaged facilities.
   D.   New towers/facilities under one hundred feet (100') in industrial
zones.
   E.   New towers/facilities one hundred feet (100') to one hundred seventy
five feet (175') in industrial zones.
New facilities shall use the most preferred type and location where technically
feasible, even if it results in an increase in the number of facilities or a
higher cost. A lesser preferred facility type may be permitted only if the
applicant presents substantial evidence to show that it will have a lesser
visual impact or is more technically necessary than the use of more preferred
facilities. (Ord. 2007-4, 2007)
17.56.040: DISFAVORED FACILITIES:
   A.   Any site that is within a state or federal designated scenic corridor
such as U.S. Highway 12.
   B.   Any site within a visual corridor or scenic vista, for example, in or
along a ridgeline exposed to view from highway travelers or to residential
areas, along a public trail, in a park or recreation area, unless the facility
blends with the surrounding natural or manmade environment.
   C.   Sites adjacent to or very close to residential areas.
   D.   Sites adjacent to or very close to sacred sites. (Ord. 2007-4, 2007)
17.56.050: PERFORMANCE STANDARDS AND DESIGN REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Height: New facilities shall not exceed one hundred ninety nine feet
(199') in height.
   B.   Setbacks: The setback for towers is one hundred five percent (105%) of
the tower height from all property lines so that in case of collapse or failure
the tower would be contained on the property. Setbacks may be allowed to extend
onto adjacent properties if there are dedicated fall zone easements. The
setbacks may be reduced if a registered engineer can certify that in case of
failure the tower would be contained on site. In commercial and industrial
zones, the setbacks may be reduced to thirty percent (30%) of the tower height
if a registered engineer can prove that in case of failure the tower would be
contained on site. Guys and accessory buildings must meet the setbacks of the
underlying zoning classification. Facilities that are located on new or
replaced utility poles, streetlights, or traffic signal poles are exempt from
setback requirements.
   C.   Color And Materials: Towers and attached antennas must be painted or
coated in a color that blends with the surrounding environment. Muted colors,
earth tones and subdued hues such as gray shall be used. All associated
structures such as equipment and buildings, including the roofs, shall be
painted the earth tone colors.
   D.   Fencing: New towers, other than flagpoles, utility poles, or other
camouflaged facilities, shall be fenced to prevent trespass.
   E.   Lighting: Lighting on any new tower is prohibited unless required by
the federal aviation administration or by other applicable state or federal
requirements. Motion detector security lighting may be approved if the lights
are fully shielded. Any outdoor lighting requires a separate lighting permit.
   F.   Landscaping: Perimeter landscaping may be required as a condition of
approval of the facility, depending on the location. Existing vegetation shall
be preserved to the maximum extent possible.
   G.   Signs: No advertising is permitted anywhere upon or attached to the
facility. Signage is limited to two (2) small nonilluminated warning and
identification signs not to exceed four (4) square feet in area.
   H.   Permits: A building permit is required for the construction of any new
tower and for accessory structures.
   I.   Storage: Long term vehicle storage and other outdoor storage are
prohibited.
   J.   Term Of Use Permit: The conditional use permit shall have a time limit
of no more than a five (5) year period; the applicant and/or structure owner
shall be responsible for submitting a new application for renewal. The
applicant shall demonstrate that changes in technology have not eliminated the
need for the facility as approved. Renewal of the conditional use permit shall
be based on compliance with the conditions of approval. (Ord. 2007-4, 2007)
17.56.060: APPLICATION PROCESS:
Prior to the submittal of a conditional use permit application, the applicant
shall schedule a preapplication conference with the Kamiah planning and zoning
commission. Staff will review the ordinance requirements and submittal
requirements to ensure a complete application, for facilities located within
one-half (1/2) mile of a residential area, the applicant shall hold a
neighborhood meeting prior to submittal of an application. Staff will attend
the meeting and utilize the comments of neighbors in the analysis presented to
the planning and zoning commission. The requirement for a neighborhood meeting
may be waived by the planning and zoning commission. The applicant shall
include all of the requirements for any conditional use permit, including eight
(8) copies of a detailed site plan and elevations, landscape and fencing plans,
etc., plus the following:
   A.   Site Plan: The site plan shall show existing improvements on the
property, adjacent roads and access roads, parking, fencing, lighting, existing
trees that will be retained and those that will be removed, setbacks from all
property lines, and all proposed improvements including those on the ground.
   B.   Elevation Drawings: The drawings shall show the tower and proposed
attached antennas, as well as proposed structures on the ground. Materials and
colors shall be indicated and color samples shall be provided.
   C.   Photo Images: Photo simulations of the proposed facility from each
direction shall be provided showing the antennas, structures, and equipment
facilities demonstrating the true impact of the facility on the surrounding
visual environment. The planning and zoning commission will assist in
specifying recommended vantage points and the requested number of photo
simulations at the preapplication conference.
   D.   Communication Plan: Each applicant shall provide a plan of its
facilities to the city prior to or in conjunction with any application for the
installation of a wireless telecommunication facility. The plan shall cover the
entire city. The plan shall include the following (these shall be in general
terms and are not meant to require submittal of confidential or proprietary
information):
      1.   All of the applicant's existing wireless facilities by size, type
and coverage area.
      2.   All presently anticipated future service areas, anticipated dates of
the development, and types and heights of facilities desired for each of the
service areas.
      3.   The various types of wireless telecommunication facilities used by
the applicant to furnish service and when they are used. This includes drawings
providing the sizes and shapes of the antennas and other equipment as well as
written materials describing their application.
      4.   The applicant's policy direction for the mitigation and/or reduction
of existing and proposed towers to avoid the proliferation of such facilities.
      5.   The applicant's policy direction on the mitigation and/or reduction
of the negative visual impacts created by the new towers, including any
proposals to conceal or disguise such facilities designed to be architecturally
and/or environmentally compatible with the surroundings.
      6.   The applicant's policy direction on collocation of antennas on its
own facilities, on facilities from other applicants or tower companies, or on
other structures that provide the verticality required for the antennas.
      7.   Designation of an agent (contact person) of the applicant who is
authorized to receive communications and notices pursuant to this section.
   E.   Written Narrative: A written narrative shall be submitted with the
application explaining why the proposed site has been chosen, why the proposed
telecommunication facility is necessary, why the requested height was chosen,
ability of the facility to accommodate other providers, and any other
information requested at the preapplication conference.
   F.   Existing Structures: Evidence shall be submitted demonstrating that no
existing verticality can be utilized within the targeted "search area", defined
generally as a one mile radius, to meet the applicant's requirements.
   G.   Property Owner List: A typewritten list of the names and addresses of
all property owners, keyed to assessor's parcel numbers, within five hundred
feet (500') outside the boundaries of the subject property for towers up to
ninety nine feet (99'), and within one thousand feet (1,000') from towers one
hundred (100) to one hundred ninety nine feet (199').
   H.   Notification Evidence: For facilities within one-fourth (1/4) mile of
"residential areas", defined as neighborhoods or subdivisions, evidence of
notification of property owners within one-fourth (1/4) mile, a map indicating
tower site and residential area, and evidence of neighborhood meeting including
sign-in sheet and a description on how the design addresses the residents'
concerns. (Ord. 2007-4, 2007)
17.56.070: EXEMPTIONS:
This chapter does not apply to ham radio antennas which are regulated elsewhere
in this title, or to satellite dishes for television reception at individual
single-family residences. In addition, a conditional use permit is not required
to collocate additional antennas on already approved towers unless it results
in a substantial change in the approval, such as an increase in tower height. A
conditional use permit is not required when the height of the structure where
the antennas are attached is not increased. Examples would be antennas on
existing utility poles, water towers, or on the fascia of existing buildings.
(Ord. 2007-4, 2007)
17.56.080: ABANDONMENT:
A facility/tower shall be considered abandoned and the use discontinued if it
is not utilized, i.e., there are no providers/antennas on the tower, for a
continuous period of one hundred eighty (180) days. (Ord. 2007-4, 2007)
17.56.090: OBSOLESCENCE AND REMOVAL:
In addition to all other remedies available to the city of Kamiah, if a
facility/tower is abandoned pursuant to section
17.56.080 of this chapter or if the facility/tower becomes obsolete due to
changing technology, it shall be the responsibility of the tower owner and/or
property owner to remove the facility/tower and to restore the site to its
original condition within sixty (60) days. If the facility/tower is not removed
within this sixty (60) day period, the city of Kamiah may notify the tower
owner that it will contract for removal at a cost to the owner. (Ord. 2007-4,
2007)
CHAPTER 17.60
ADMINISTRATION
SECTION:
17.60.010: Administrator
17.60.020: Duties Of The Commission
17.60.030: Conflict Of Interest
17.60.040: Compliance By Issuers Of Permits
17.60.050: Penalties
17.60.060: Alternative Remedy
17.60.070: Enforcement Procedures
17.60.080: Schedule Of Fees
17.60.010: ADMINISTRATOR:
   A.   The council shall appoint an administrator to administer this title.
The administrator may be provided with the assistance of such other persons as
the council may direct.
   B.   For the purpose of this title, the administrator may have the following
duties:
      1.   Assist applicants in the preparation of required forms and permit
procedures; review preapplication materials; and explain proper procedures.
      2.   Inform the news media regarding land use and development matters of
public interest, particularly the time and place of public hearings.
      3.   Prepare the agenda for the meetings of the commission, in
cooperation with commission members.
      4.   Analyze permit requests and prepare reports and summaries of said
analysis.
      5.   Mail necessary submission to referral agencies and analyze the
comments and recommendations.
      6.   Receive, file, and transmit to the commission and/or council all
applications, petitions, transcripts, and other communications on which they
must act.
      7.   Maintain permanent and current records of applications,
reclassifications, variances, and conditional use permits and of the hearing
and actions thereon.
      8.   Advise interested citizens of ordinance provisions.
      9.   Perform such other duties as may be assigned by the Kamiah city
council and the planning and zoning commission. (Ord. 2007-4, 2007)
17.60.020: DUTIES OF THE COMMISSION:
For the purposes of this title the commission shall have the following duties:
   A.   The commission shall be empowered to issue conditional use permits and
variances.
   B.   The commission shall conduct public hearings required by this title.
   C.   The commission shall make recommendations or suggestions to the council
regarding:
      1.   The health, safety and general welfare of the residents and
landowners of the county.
      2.   The future growth, physical development, and beautification of the
city.
      3.   The layout, width, and location of streets, roads, highways, etc.
      4.   The design, construction, quality of materials, use, occupancy,
location and maintenance of all buildings and structures in the unincorporated
area of the city.
      5.   Subdivision and planned unit developments.
      6.   Road naming and addressing.
      7.   Amendments to the comprehensive plan, this title, uniform building
code ordinance, and other land use related ordinances of the city.
   D.   The commission may advise the council in matters relating to areas of
impact and annexation of lands by municipalities and other intergovernmental
matters within the city.
   E.   The commission may meet annually with the council to discuss matters
relating to city planning and development.
   F.   All activities undertaken by the commission shall be consistent with
budgetary appropriations established by the council for commission activities.
   G.   The commission shall assume those additional powers and duties not
listed and as may be assigned to them by the council for commission activities.
(Ord. 2007-4, 2007)
17.60.030: CONFLICT OF INTEREST:
The council creating a commission shall provide that the area and interests
within its jurisdiction are broadly represented on the commission. A member or
employee of the council or commission shall not participate in any proceeding
or action when the member or employee or his employers, business partner,
business associate or any person related to him by affinity or consanguinity
within the second degree has economic interest in the procedure or action. Any
actual or potential interest in any proceeding shall be disclosed at or before
any meeting at which the action is being heard or considered. (Ord. 2007-4,
2007)
17.60.040: COMPLIANCE BY ISSUERS OF PERMITS:
All departments, officials, and public employees of the city vested with the
duty or authority to issue permits, shall conform to the conditions of this
title, and shall issue no permit, certificate, or license for the use of land,
buildings, or purposes, in conflict with the provisions of this title and such
permit, certificate, or license issued in conflict with the provisions of this
title shall be null and void. (Ord. 2007-4, 2007)
17.60.050: PENALTIES:
Each violation of this chapter or of any regulation, order, or ruling
promulgated hereunder shall constitute a misdemeanor and be punishable by a
fine of not more than three hundred dollars ($300.00) or by imprisonment for
not more than six (6) months or both; and each day a violation continues to
exist shall constitute a separate offense. (Ord. 2007-4, 2007)
17.60.060: ALTERNATIVE REMEDY:
Where a building or other structure is, or is proposed to be located,
constructed, maintained, repaired, altered or used, or the land proposed to be
used, is in violation of this title, the building or land in violation shall
constitute a nuisance, and the city may, as an alternative to other remedies
that are legally available for enforcing this title, institute an injunction,
abatement, or other appropriate proceeding to prevent, enjoin, temporarily or
permanently abate, or remove the unlawful location, construction, maintenance,
repair, alteration or use. (Ord. 2007-4, 2007)
17.60.070: ENFORCEMENT PROCEDURES:
In the event that any use of land or any construction commences in violation of
the provisions of this title, the proper authorities of the city, in addition
to other remedies, may institute any appropriate action or proceedings to
prevent such unlawful use of land or construction, to restrain, correct or
abate such violation or to prevent any illegal act, conduct, construction,
business or use of land in or about such premises. (Ord. 2007-4, 2007)
17.60.080: SCHEDULE OF FEES:
The council shall establish by resolution a schedule of fees for amendments,
appeals, variances, conditional use permits, plan approvals, and other matters
pertaining to the administration and enforcement of this title. The schedule of
fees shall be on file in the office of the city clerk and may be altered or
amended only by the council. Until all applicable fees have been paid in full,
no action shall be taken on the application or appeal. (Ord. 2007-4, 2007)
